PMP Exam 4
Filtered Mode: Displaying 200 questions
Question 26 of 200
Question ID: 612691
You are performing activities necessary to close out the second phase of a multi-phase project.
The project documents of this phase indicate that the planned risk responses to several of the
realized risks were found to be ineffective.
What should you do next before moving to the next phase of your project?
- **A Increase the management reserves allocated to the third phase**
- **B Update the risk management plan for the third phase**
- **C Submit a change request to update the lessons learned register**
- **D Transfer the knowledge gained to the lessons learned repository**
Question answered incorrectly

**Hint:**

What should be done with knowledge gained during the project after the project documents have
been finalized?
Correct Answer: D

**Explanation:**

The question implies that the Close Project or Phase process of the second phase of the project is
being carried out. The lessons learned register is a project document used to record knowledge
gained during a project (or phase) so that it can be used in the current project and entered into the
lessons learned repository at the end of the project or phase. The question indicates that the
knowledge gained came from the project documents of the current phase, which suggests that the
knowledge was previously captured in the lessons learned register. As part of the Close Project
or Phase process, the information from the lessons learned register should be transferred to the
lessons learned repository which is what you should do before moving to the next phase of your
project.

---


**Details for Each Option:**

- **A Increase the management reserves allocated to the third phase**
Incorrect. Management reserves are a specified amount of the project budget withheld for
management control purposes and are reserved for unforeseen work that is within the
scope of the project. A project manager needs an approved change request to increase the
management reserves. Also, increasing the management reserves for a subsequent phase
based on the ineffective risk responses of a previous phase is not good project management
practice.
- **B Update the risk management plan for the third phase**
Incorrect. While updating the risk management plan for the third phase is a plausible
option, it is not the next step for you to take. First, all activities associated with the closure
of the second phase should be completed. Even then, the next phase of the project does not
start with the development or update of the risk management plan. Additionally, risk
responses for particular risks are specified in the risk register, not in the risk management
plan.
- **C Submit a change request to update the lessons learned register**
Incorrect. The lessons learned register is a project document that is not typically subject to
a formal change control process. While the lessons learned register might be updated as
part of the process described in the scenario, no change request is required to update this
document.
- **D Transfer the knowledge gained to the lessons learned repository**
Correct. The lessons learned repository is a store of historical information about lessons
learned from projects. As part of the Close Project or Phase process, the information from
the lessons learned register could be transferred to the lessons learned repository.

**Reference:**

- **A Guide to the Project Management Body of Knowledge, (PMBOK® Guide) – Sixth Edition,**
Project Management Institute Inc., 2017, Page(s) 128

PMP Exam 4
Filtered Mode: Displaying 200 questions
Question 27 of 200
Question ID: 612717
- **A project sponsor creates a draft of the project charter and asks you to complete its development**
and lead the project.
What should you do next?
- **A Gather information from stakeholders to document high-level details on the project**
- **B Determine whether the expected outcomes of the project justify the required investment**
- **C Create a document that describes how the project will be executed, monitored, controlled,**
and closed
- **D Develop a document that describes how and when the benefits of the project will be**
delivered
Question answered incorrectly

**Hint:**

Which of the answer choices represent a tool or technique of the Develop Project Charter
process?
Correct Answer: A

**Explanation:**

You are requested by the project sponsor to complete the development of the project charter and
to lead the project. This implies you have been assigned as a project manager (even though the
project charter has not yet been approved). Since you have been assigned to the project, it has
been determined that the project will contribute to the company's business goals. The next step
would be chartering the project. The project charter is the document that formally authorizes the
project manager to apply organizational resources to project activities and is an essential
document for project success. Gathering data from stakeholders to obtain information on high-
level requirements, assumptions, constraints, approval criteria, and other information is one of
the techniques used when developing the project charter and therefore, the next thing you should
do.

---


**Details for Each Option:**

- **A Gather information from stakeholders to document high-level details on the project**
Correct. A document with high-level details on the project would be the project charter.
The project charter is the document that formally authorizes the project and provides the
project manager with the authority to apply organizational resources to project activities.
Gathering information from stakeholders is one of the techniques used to develop the
project charter and is, therefore, what you should do next.
- **B Determine whether the expected outcomes of the project justify the required investment**
Incorrect. The business case describes the necessary information to determine whether the
expected outcomes of the project justify the required investment. The business case is
developed before the project and commonly used as an input to create the project charter.
Since you have already been assigned to the project, it is reasonable to assume that the
business case would have been already completed. Therefore, this choice is not the best
answer to the question asked.
- **C Create a document that describes how the project will be executed, monitored, controlled,**
and closed
Incorrect. A document that describes how the project will be executed, monitored,
controlled, and closed is the project management plan. This plan is developed during
project planning, while according to the scenario, the project is in initiation.
- **D Develop a document that describes how and when the benefits of the project will be**
delivered
Incorrect. The benefits management plan is the document that describes how and when the
benefits of the project will be delivered. The benefits management plan is developed early
in the project life cycle and is one of the business documents commonly used to create the
project charter. You have been assigned as a project manager, therefore, one may assume
the benefits management plan has already been completed, making this choice an incorrect
answer.

**Reference:**

- **A Guide to the Project Management Body of Knowledge, (PMBOK® Guide) – Sixth Edition,**
Project Management Institute Inc., 2017, Page(s) 80, 77, 30-33
Live FeedbackTM Back to Results

Question 28 of 200
Question ID: 610053
Your project to produce a new vending machine is almost over, and you are now in the process
of handing over the product to the operations team. You are meeting with the company president
who initiated the project and with operations senior managers to demonstrate the vending
machine functionality.
Which of the following is most important for you to achieve when meeting with these
individuals?
- **A Understanding of the specific features of the vending machine**
- **B Confirming the formal acceptance of the vending machine**
- **C Getting support from operations management**
- **D Being recognized for project completion**
Question answered incorrectly

**Hint:**

Fulfill the expectations of the project stakeholders.
Correct Answer: B

**Explanation:**

The question implies you are in the Close Project or Phase process. One of the activities
associated with this process is to confirm the delivery and formal acceptance of the project
deliverables from the relevant project stakeholders. In this case, the project has been initiated by
the company president. Therefore, of the choices provided, obtaining final formal acceptance of
the project deliverables is what you should achieve when meeting with the president and
operations management. Note, the final acceptance should be obtained from the president and
not from the operations management. However, as we frequently mention, the correct answer is
not always the ideal answer that you would like to see among the choices available. For an
answer to be correct, it should be just a little better than the others.

---


**Details for Each Option:**

- **A Understanding of the specific features of the vending machine**
Incorrect. While an understanding of the vending machine functionality is important to the
operations team to operate the machine when it is deployed in production, the question
states that the meeting is conducted with the company president and the operations senior
management. It is reasonable to assume that these individuals are more interested in the
overall functionality rather than in specific features of the product. Therefore, this choice is
not the best answer to the question asked.
- **B Confirming the formal acceptance of the vending machine**
Correct. A key component of closing a project is confirming the delivery and formal
acceptance of the project deliverable from relevant stakeholders. Since the company
president commissioned the project and is, therefore, a key stakeholder, you should confirm
their acceptance of the final output during the Close Project or Phase process implied by
the scenario.
- **C Getting support from operations management**
Incorrect. While obtaining support from operations management will benefit the project
while transferring the new vending machine to operations, of the choices given, support
from operations management is not the most important thing you need to achieve during
the meeting described in the scenario.
- **D Being recognized for project completion**
Incorrect. Although you may be seeking recognition from the company president for
completing the project, recognition for project completion can be made later, after the
project is formally closed, and is, therefore, not the most important thing to be achieved in
the scenario, making this choice an incorrect answer.

**Reference:**

- **A Guide to the Project Management Body of Knowledge, (PMBOK® Guide) – Sixth Edition,**
Project Management Institute Inc., 2017, Page(s) 123

PMP Exam 4

Question 29 of 200
Question ID: 626010
You have developed a project schedule, but the project completion date falls beyond the deadline
defined by the project sponsor. You explained this situation to the sponsor and asked them to
provide you with additional funds to bring in more people, but the sponsor refused.
What can you do to shorten the project duration?
- **A Crash the project**
- **B Fast track the project**
- **C Apply resource leveling**
- **D Do nothing**
Question answered incorrectly

**Hint:**

Which tool or technique may help in shortening the project duration without applying additional
resources?
Correct Answer: B

**Explanation:**

Fast tracking is a schedule compression technique that can be used during the Develop Schedule
process. In this technique, activities on the critical path that were planned to be performed
sequentially are performed in parallel for some or all of their duration, thus shortening the overall
project length. While no additional resources are required while applying fast tracking, the
project manager should be aware that fast tracking may result in rework and an increased risk.

**Details for Each Option:**

- **A Crash the project**

---

Incorrect. Crashing the project requires additional resources. The project sponsor refused
to provide funds to bring in more people.
- **B Fast track the project**
Correct. Fast tracking is a schedule compression technique in which critical path project
activities that were planned to be executed sequentially are performed in parallel resulting
in a shorter project duration.
- **C Apply resource leveling**
Incorrect. Resource leveling usually increases the project duration.
- **D Do nothing**
Incorrect. Doing nothing knowing that the project will not be completed on time is not a
responsible choice of project manager.

**Reference:**

- **A Guide to the Project Management Body of Knowledge, (PMBOK® Guide) – Sixth Edition,**
Project Management Institute Inc., 2017, Page(s) 215

PMP Exam 4
Filtered Mode: Displaying 200 questions
Question 30 of 200
Question ID: 612011
The project management plan and the performance measurement baseline have been approved.
As you monitor the project's progress, you realize the approved budget is limiting the project and
will affect the targeted completion date. This constraint could affect the company's success in the
new venture.
What is your best course of action?
- **A Use the contingency reserves**
- **B Use the management reserves**
- **C Cut costs on the project to stay within the budget**
- **D Ask for a change in the budget**
Question answered incorrectly

**Hint:**

- **A project manager needs to take appropriate actions to meet the project's objectives which likely**
will assist the company in achieving its strategic goals.
Correct Answer: D

**Explanation:**

As the project manager, you are ultimately responsible for the project as a whole and its success.
You are also the one that has the overall view of the project. The scenario suggests the project
budget is limiting the project's ability to meet the targeted completion date. While staying within
budget is one of your responsibilities, you also need to make integrated decisions and act to
ensure the project's objectives are met and remains aligned with the business plan and the
benefits management plan. By deciding to ask for a budget increase so that the completion date
can be met, rather than trying to cut costs to stay within the budget, you are contributing toward a
successful launch into a new area of retail, which is one of the company's strategic goals.
Obviously, an approved change request will be required to change the project budget.

---


**Details for Each Option:**

- **A Use the contingency reserves**
Incorrect. Contingency reserves are allocated for known risks that have been specifically
identified during risk analysis. Since the contingency reserves are included in the budget,
using them would not increase the funding for the project and therefore is not your best
course of action.
- **B Use the management reserves**
Incorrect. Management reserves are additional funds to cover unforeseen risks that could
impact the project. These reserves are 'not' included in the cost baseline but are part of the
approved cost budget. An approved change request is required to utilize management
reserves and, therefore, cannot be used at the project manager's discretion. Since the
management reserves are included in the budgeted amount, using them would not increase
the funding for the project.
- **C Cut costs on the project to stay within the budget**
Incorrect. The scenario suggests the current budget is a constraint to the project and that
increased funding is required to meet the objectives. While staying within budget is one of
your responsibilities as the project manager, you also need to make integrated decisions
and act to ensure both the project's and the company's objectives are met. Your project
contributes to the company's strategic goal of entering a new area of retail, therefore, by
trying to cut costs to stay within budget, the company might miss one of its strategic goals.
- **D Ask for a change in the budget**
Correct. The scenario suggests you find the budget is a constraint that could hinder the
company's realization of one of their strategic goals. By asking for a change in the budget,
you increase the chances of the company's successful launch into a new area of retail. As
the project manager, you are responsible for the success of the project. Therefore, you need
to monitor the project's progress and act to meet the project's objectives and ultimately the
company's goals.

**Reference:**

- **A Guide to the Project Management Body of Knowledge, (PMBOK® Guide) – Sixth Edition,**
Project Management Institute Inc., 2017, Page(s) 72
Live FeedbackTM Back to Results

Question 31 of 200
Question ID: 613622
You have just completed the Collect Requirements process with a group of senior executives and
your team. You begin developing the scope statement and realize that you need more
clarification on a specific component of the deliverable.
What document should you reference to find the person who requested the specific component?
- **A Stakeholder engagement assessment matrix**
- **B Responsibility assignment matrix (RAM)**
- **C RACI chart**
- **D Requirements traceability matrix**
Question answered incorrectly

**Hint:**

There are two outputs to the Collect Requirements process. One is the requirements
documentation. What is the other output?
Correct Answer: D

**Explanation:**

Part of the Collect Requirements process is to link product requirements from their origin
(including the person who requested the requirement) to the deliverables that satisfy them.
Attributes, including source, associated with each requirement are recorded in the requirements
traceability matrix. You may need to contact the person (or source) who requested the
requirement to clarify the specifications for the scope statement, as in this scenario, but also in
cases where the stakeholder should be informed a deliverable they expected may need to be
eliminated, changed or delayed.

**Details for Each Option:**


---

- **A Stakeholder engagement assessment matrix**
Incorrect. The stakeholder engagement assessment matrix is typically used in the Plan
Stakeholder Engagement process to compare current and desired stakeholder engagement
levels required for successful project delivery. It does not indicate who requested a
requirement.
- **B Responsibility assignment matrix (RAM)**
Incorrect. RAM is a general term for a grid that shows what project resources are assigned
to each work package. RAM illustrates connections between work packages, or activities
and project team members. It does not indicate who requested a requirement.
- **C RACI chart**
Incorrect. A RACI chart is a common type of RAM that defines the involvement of
stakeholders and team members with responsible, accountable, consult and inform statuses
for project activities. It does not indicate who requested a requirement.
- **D Requirements traceability matrix**
Correct. The requirements traceability matrix links product requirements from their origin
to the deliverables that satisfy them. It identifies the person (or source) who originally
requested the requirement. You can then contact them to get more details about the specific
requirement.

**Reference:**

- **A Guide to the Project Management Body of Knowledge, (PMBOK® Guide) – Sixth Edition,**
Project Management Institute Inc., 2017, Page(s) 148-149

Filtered Mode: Displaying 200 questions
Question 32 of 200
Question ID: 612565
- **A project management plan has been approved, and the project is now in execution. The project**
manager would like to communicate project status to the stakeholders.
Which of the following should the project manager send to stakeholders to achieve her
immediate goal?
- **A Work performance report**
- **B Work performance data**
- **C Communications management plan**
- **D Project management plan**
Question answered incorrectly

**Hint:**

Which answer choice represents the physical or electronic representation of work performance
information compiled in project documents, intended to generate decisions, actions, or
awareness?
Correct Answer: A

**Explanation:**

Project reporting is the act of collecting and distributing project information. Project information
is distributed to various groups of stakeholders and should be in a form to provide information at
an appropriate level, detail, and format for the stakeholders. Work performance reports are the
physical or electronic representation of work performance information compiled in project
documents, intended to generate decisions, actions, or awareness. Work performance reports
would allow the project manager to communicate the project status to the stakeholders.

**Details for Each Option:**


---

- **A Work performance report**
Correct. The act of collecting and distributing project information to groups of
stakeholders is known as project reporting. To complete the project reporting, the work
performance reports, which contain the work performance data that is collected during
execution and analyzed and put into context during the Monitor and Control Project Work
process, should be sent to the stakeholders.
- **B Work performance data**
Incorrect. Work performance data are the raw observations and measurements collected
while project activities are being performed. Work performance data is not in a useful or
appropriate form until it is analyzed in the various controlling processes to create work
performance reports.
- **C Communications management plan**
Incorrect. The communications management plan is a component of the project
management plan that describes how project communications will be planned, structured,
implemented, and monitored for effectiveness. The plan does not contain information on
project performance.
- **D Project management plan**
Incorrect. The project management plan is the document that describes how the project will
be executed, monitored and controlled, and closed. The plan does not have project
performance information that would help the stakeholders to understand the status of the
project.

**Reference:**

- **A Guide to the Project Management Body of Knowledge, (PMBOK® Guide) – Sixth Edition,**
Project Management Institute Inc., 2017, Page(s) 382, 385, 112

PMP Exam 4
Filtered Mode: Displaying 200 questions
Question 33 of 200
Question ID: 613704
The project team that you are managing is entirely virtual and distributed all over the country.
You know that as the project progresses, your team will learn things and gather more information
about the project. You would like to ensure all that knowledge and information does not get lost.
By managing project knowledge, you can improve current project outcomes as well as support
future projects.
Which of the following will you need to remember when managing knowledge on this project?
- **A Managing project knowledge only involves documenting information so it can be shared.**
- **B Managing project knowledge only involves obtaining lessons learned.**
- **C Explicit knowledge can be easily shared but isn't always understood correctly.**
- **D Tacit knowledge is easy to organize and index.**
Question answered incorrectly

**Hint:**

The information contained in lessons learned is an example of explicit knowledge.
Correct Answer: C

**Explanation:**

Knowledge is commonly split into two forms. Tacit knowledge is personal and hard to express.
It involves the collective know-how, techniques, and expertise gained from one's experiences.
Tacit knowledge is difficult to organize and is typically shared through conversations and
interactions between people. Explicit knowledge can be expressed in words, numbers, and
symbols and therefore can be easily documented and shared. However, explicit knowledge lacks
context and is open to different interpretations making it been easily misunderstood. You need to
remember this drawback of using only explicit knowledge in order to effectively manage
knowledge on this project. You need to take actions, such as building an atmosphere of trust so
that people are motivated to share their knowledge, to reduce the risk of relying only on explicit
knowledge.

---


**Details for Each Option:**

- **A Managing project knowledge only involves documenting information so it can be shared.**
Incorrect. Managing project knowledge is not limited to only documenting explicit
knowledge and information so it can be shared. Rather, managing project knowledge is
concerned with managing 'both' explicit and tacit knowledge. While explicit knowledge can
be expressed in words, numbers, and symbols allowing it to be easily documented as
information, explicit knowledge lacks context and can be misunderstood. Therefore, only
documenting information is not enough.
- **B Managing project knowledge only involves obtaining lessons learned.**
Incorrect. Managing project knowledge is concerned with managing both tacit and explicit
knowledge. Lessons learned, an example of explicit knowledge, can be easily documented.
Without context, however, lessons learned can be misunderstood; therefore, there is more
involved in managing project knowledge than recording lessons learned.
- **C Explicit knowledge can be easily shared but isn't always understood correctly.**
Correct. Explicit knowledge can be expressed in words, numbers, and symbols and
therefore can be easily documented. Explicit knowledge, however, lacks context and is open
to different interpretations. Consequently, it can be easily misunderstood.
- **D Tacit knowledge is easy to organize and index.**
Incorrect. Tacit knowledge resides in the minds of people and is best shared through
conversations and interactions between people. This type of knowledge, such as beliefs and
experience, is personal and difficult to express, organize, and index.

**Reference:**

- **A Guide to the Project Management Body of Knowledge, (PMBOK® Guide) – Sixth Edition,**
Project Management Institute Inc., 2017, Page(s) 100
Live FeedbackTM Back to Results
Prev Next

PMP Exam 4
Filtered Mode: Displaying 200 questions
Question 34 of 200
Question ID: 613502
You are managing a project to produce new smartwatches. Several inspections have been
conducted during the manufacturing process, and defects of various types have been detected.
You want to document these defects in a way that will specify how many defects of each type
were found per inspection.
Which tool is the best to use in this situation?
- **A Control charts**
- **B Check sheets**
- **C Scatter diagrams**
- **D Pareto diagrams**
Question answered incorrectly

**Hint:**

This tool can be in the form of a matrix where rows represent various types of defects, and
columns represent inspections conducted on different days.
Correct Answer: B

**Explanation:**

The scenario suggests you are performing the Control Quality process. Check sheets are an
example of a data gathering techniques that can be used as part of this process. A check sheet can
be used to gather data, such as quality problems uncovered during inspections, as well as to
document how often a particular defect occurs. Check sheets can be used to organize facts in a
manner that facilitate the effective collection of data about a potential quality problem. A check
sheet can be in the form of a matrix where rows represent various types of defects, and columns
represent inspections conducted on different days. This description accurately addresses the
question asked, making check sheets the best tool to use in the situation presented in the
scenario.

---


**Details for Each Option:**

- **A Control charts**
Incorrect. Control charts are used to determine whether a process is stable or has
predictable performance rather than document the type and the frequency of defects.
- **B Check sheets**
Correct. A check sheet, also known as a tally sheet, can be used to gather data, such as
quality problems uncovered during inspections, as well as to document how often a
particular defect occurs.
- **C Scatter diagrams**
Incorrect. A scatter diagram is a graph that shows the relationship between two variables.
According to the scenario, you want to document defects in a way that will specify how
many defects of each type were found per inspection. A scatter diagram does not provide
this information.
- **D Pareto diagrams**
Incorrect. A Pareto diagram is a type of histogram where data is presented with relative
frequencies of each specified cause listed in the horizontal axis decreasing in magnitude.
This is done to identify vital few sources that are responsible for causing most of the
problem's effects. The Pareto diagram is typically used in root cause analysis to help
identify which root causes are resulting in the most problems. Since the scenario does not
require to identify root causes, the Pareto diagram is not the best answer to the question
asked.

**Reference:**

- **A Guide to the Project Management Body of Knowledge, (PMBOK® Guide) – Sixth Edition,**
Project Management Institute Inc., 2017, Page(s) 302
Live FeedbackTM Back to Results
Prev Next

PMP Exam 4
Filtered Mode: Displaying 200 questions
Question 35 of 200
Question ID: 612788
You have just been assigned to a new project which will begin in the near future. The project
sponsor has informed you that this project will require rigorous change control.
When will you develop the change management plan?
- **A Along with the processes of the Initiating Process Group**
- **B As part of the Develop Project Management Plan process**
- **C As an output of the Plan Change Management process**
- **D During the Perform Integrated Change Control process**
Question answered incorrectly

**Hint:**

The change management plan is created as part of project planning.
Correct Answer: B

**Explanation:**

The change management plan is a component of the project management plan that establishes the
change control board, documents the extent of its authority, and describes how the change
control system will be implemented. Most components of the project management plan are
produced as the output from other processes, but the change management plan is created as part
of the Develop Project Management Plan process.

**Details for Each Option:**

- **A Along with the processes of the Initiating Process Group**
Incorrect. The Initiating Process Group includes the Develop Charter process and the
Identify Stakeholders process. The change management plan is developed as part of the

---

Planning Process Group and not the Initiating Process Group.
- **B As part of the Develop Project Management Plan process**
Correct. The change management plan is a component of the project management plan and
is developed as part of the Develop Project Management Plan process.
- **C As an output of the Plan Change Management process**
Incorrect. 'Plan Change Management' is not a process specified in the PMBOK® Guide.
- **D During the Perform Integrated Change Control process**
Incorrect. The change management plan is a critical input into the Perform Integrated
Change Control process and must be completed before this process can be executed. The
change management plan is created during project planning rather than during the
Perform Integrated Change Control process which occurs later in the project as part of the
Monitoring and Controlling Process Group.

**Reference:**

- **A Guide to the Project Management Body of Knowledge, (PMBOK® Guide) – Sixth Edition,**
Project Management Institute Inc., 2017, Page(s) 88

PMP Exam 4
Filtered Mode: Displaying 200 questions
Question 36 of 200
Question ID: 612350
- **A project manager has just completed the development of the project management plan and now**
needs the plan to be reviewed and signed off by the key stakeholders.
What should the project manager do to find the names of these individuals?
- **A Check the lessons learned repository**
- **B Review project documents**
- **C Contact the human resources department**
- **D Ask the project sponsor**
Question answered incorrectly

**Hint:**

What is the best source of information regarding the identification, assessment, and classification
of project stakeholders?
Correct Answer: B

**Explanation:**

Ideally, the correct answer could have been worded as, “Review the stakeholder register.”
However, this option is not provided. Instead, a wider term, ‘project documents’, is used. Project
documents are not part of the project management plan; however, along with the project
management plan, they are necessary to manage the project effectively. The stakeholder register
is among the project documents. It should have been created as part of the Identify Stakeholders
process during project initiation. The stakeholder register is a project document which includes
the identification, assessment, and classification of project stakeholders. Since, according to the
scenario described, the functional leaders are involved in the project, they are considered project
stakeholders. Thus, the stakeholder register should list the names of the project sponsor and
functional leaders. Therefore, to find the names of those relevant stakeholders that need to be
invited to the meeting, the project manager should review the project documents.

---


**Details for Each Option:**

- **A Check the lessons learned repository**
Incorrect. The lessons learned repository may or may not have information from past
projects regarding the approval of the project management plan. However, this information
will not likely have the current roles and responsibilities of key stakeholders.
- **B Review project documents**
Correct. A stakeholder register is one of the project documents. The stakeholder register
includes the identification, assessment, and classification of project stakeholders. The
project manager should review the stakeholder register to determine who are the relevant
stakeholders that need to attend the meeting and invited them as necessary.
- **C Contact the human resources department**
Incorrect. The human resource department may have contact information for the identified
stakeholders. However, the department is unlikely to have the information on 'who' the
stakeholders are for this (or any other) project.
- **D Ask the project sponsor**
Incorrect. The project sponsor may be aware of the names of individuals associated with
the identified roles. However, this is not a good use of time nor is the project sponsor the
best source for this information. The project manager should use the resources which are
already available whenever possible.

**Reference:**

- **A Guide to the Project Management Body of Knowledge, (PMBOK® Guide) – Sixth Edition,**
Project Management Institute Inc., 2017, Page(s) 514, 88-89; see also Project Management
Professional (PMP)® Examination Content Outline, Project Management Institute Inc., June
2015, Domain 2, Task 11

PMP Exam 4
Filtered Mode: Displaying 200 questions
Question 37 of 200
Question ID: 613656
- **A project manager is provided a fixed budget, but the cost estimates for the equipment required**
for the project were 30% higher than expected.
What would be the best technique to find alternatives that can be presented to the project
sponsors for consideration to lower the cost and meet their budget?
- **A Plan cost management**
- **B Value engineering**
- **C Fishbone diagram**
- **D Basis of estimates**
Question answered incorrectly

**Hint:**

When assessing cost, think of inherent or intrinsic worth.
Correct Answer: B

**Explanation:**

As the project manager, you look for ways to optimize the value of the project, especially
working with cost constraints. Value engineering (also known as value analysis) is an example of
product analysis, a technique used in the Define Scope process, which is described in the
question. Value engineering is a way to look in-depth at all project elements (in this case,
equipment) to improve cost efficiencies without loss of performance. Two of the answer choices,
the plan cost management and the basis of estimates, can be eliminated because they are not
techniques. Fishbone diagram can be eliminated because the technique focuses on the root causes
of a problem and does not assess the value of individual elements of a project. Therefore, of the
choices provided, value engineering is considered the best answer to the question asked.

**Details for Each Option:**


---

- **A Plan cost management**
Incorrect. Plan cost management is not a technique, but a component of the project
management plan that describes the approach to the project's cost management.
- **B Value engineering**
Correct. Value engineering is a type of product analysis technique that "supports cost
reduction activities by relating the cost of individual components to their function
contributions."
- **C Fishbone diagram**
Incorrect. A fishbone diagram (also known as a cause-and-effect diagram) is a technique
that illustrates the causes of a problem in separate branches which help determine the main
cause of the issue. It does not evaluate the value of a project's components nor consider
alternatives.
- **D Basis of estimates**
Incorrect. The basis of estimates is not a technique, but a project document with details on
how estimates were derived.

**Reference:**

- **A Guide to the Project Management Body of Knowledge, (PMBOK® Guide) – Sixth Edition,**
Project Management Institute Inc., 2017, Page(s) 153
Live FeedbackTM Back to Results
Prev Next

PMP Exam 4
Filtered Mode: Displaying 200 questions
Question 38 of 200
Question ID: 613618
You are finalizing your project. As you start this process, you need to gain a clear understanding
of the project's approval requirements and who will sign off on the project.
What should you do to find this information?
- **A Review the project charter**
- **B Check the business case**
- **C Consult the benefits management plan**
- **D Review the responsibility assignment matrix (RAM)**
Question answered incorrectly

**Hint:**

What project document is issued by the sponsor and formally authorizes the existence of the
project?
Correct Answer: A

**Explanation:**

The Close Project or Phase is the process described in the question. The project charter is one of
the inputs used in the Close Project or Phase process. The project charter documents the project
success criteria, the approval requirements, and who will sign off on the project. The project
charter is the document that is most useful in this scenario, and reviewing this document is what
you should do.

**Details for Each Option:**

- **A Review the project charter**
Correct. The project charter documents the project success criteria, the approval

---

requirements, and who will sign off on the project.
- **B Check the business case**
Incorrect. The business case is a document that outlines the business need and the cost-
benefit analysis that justifies the project. The business case does not contain information on
approval requirements or who will sign off on the project.
- **C Consult the benefits management plan**
Incorrect. The benefits management plan outlines the target benefits that justify the project,
but it does not document the approval requirements or who will sign off on the project.
- **D Review the responsibility assignment matrix (RAM)**
Incorrect. The responsibility assignment matrix (RAM) is a grid that shows the project
resources assigned to each work package. The RAM does not contain the project success
criteria, the approval requirements, or who will sign off on the project.

**Reference:**

- **A Guide to the Project Management Body of Knowledge, (PMBOK® Guide) – Sixth Edition,**
Project Management Institute Inc., 2017, Page(s) 124

PMP Exam 4
Filtered Mode: Displaying 200 questions
Question 39 of 200
Question ID: 610020
As you are monitoring the cost baseline for your project, you notice that project expenses are
higher than expected at this point in the project.
What is the most likely cause of the variance?
- **A Overestimated material costs**
- **B Lack of stakeholder support**
- **C An incomplete milestone list**
- **D Excess inventory**
Question answered incorrectly

**Hint:**

Proper physical resource management is necessary for successful completion of a project.
Correct Answer: D

**Explanation:**

Physical resource management is concentrated in allocating and using the physical resources
such as materials, equipment, and supplies efficiently and effectively. Organizations should have
data on how much inventory to keep on hand as the project progresses. Failing to manage and
control resources efficiently can be a source of increased costs in a project. In the scenario
described, you have determined expenses are higher than expected. One of the causes for
increased costs is failing to maintain appropriate levels of inventory. Too much stock on hand
may result in realizing the expenses for those supplies before they were expected when
comparing against the cost baseline.

**Details for Each Option:**


---

- **A Overestimated material costs**
Incorrect. Estimating material costs is completed as part of Project Cost Management to
develop a project budget. Overestimating material costs would lead to a higher approved
budget and, therefore, a higher cost baseline, i.e., a smaller variance, and would not cause
increased expenses.
- **B Lack of stakeholder support**
Incorrect. While stakeholder support is essential for the success of a project, it is hard to
find the direct correlation between the stakeholder support and higher than expected
project expenses. Another answer choice better addresses the question asked.
- **C An incomplete milestone list**
Incorrect. A milestone list is a project document that identifies all project milestones. The
existence or lack of a milestone list would unlikely cause project expenses to be higher than
expected.
- **D Excess inventory**
Correct. Keeping too much inventory may result in high operational costs and higher
expenses. The increased cost of additional supplies could cause a deviation from the cost
baseline.

**Reference:**

- **A Guide to the Project Management Body of Knowledge, (PMBOK® Guide) – Sixth Edition,**
Project Management Institute Inc., 2017, Page(s) 310
Live FeedbackTM Back to Results
Prev Next

PMP Exam 4
Filtered Mode: Displaying 200 questions
Question 40 of 200
Question ID: 612192
While reviewing the quality management plan, you notice that the cost of quality specified in the
plan includes a wrong component.
Which component did you likely notice?
- **A Change costs**
- **B Appraisal costs**
- **C Failure costs**
- **D Prevention costs**
Question answered incorrectly

**Hint:**

One of the answer choices is a made up term.
Correct Answer: A

**Explanation:**

The quality management plan is the main output of the Plan Quality Management process. As
part of this process, the cost of quality associated with the project can be determined to reflect
the appropriate balance for investing in the cost of prevention and appraisal to avoid failure
costs. Cost of quality is an example of the data analysis technique that is associated with this
process. The cost of quality includes prevention costs, appraisal costs, and failure costs. ‘Change
costs’ are not specified by the PMBOK® Guide as a component of the cost of quality and is,
therefore, the wrong component you likely noticed while reviewing the quality management
plan.

**Details for Each Option:**


---

- **A Change costs**
Correct. 'Change costs' are not a recognized component of the cost of quality. Therefore,
including an unrecognized element in the cost of quality is most likely the identified
problem.
- **B Appraisal costs**
Incorrect. Appraisal costs are costs related to evaluating, measuring, auditing, and testing
the products, deliverables, or services of the specific project. Appraisal costs are included
in the cost of quality.
- **C Failure costs**
Incorrect. Failure costs are costs related to nonconformance of the products, deliverables,
or services to the needs or expectations of the stakeholders. Failure costs are an element of
the cost of quality.
- **D Prevention costs**
Incorrect. Prevention costs are costs related to the prevention of poor quality in the
products, deliverables, or services of the specific project. Prevention costs should be
included in the cost of quality.

**Reference:**

- **A Guide to the Project Management Body of Knowledge, (PMBOK® Guide) – Sixth Edition,**
Project Management Institute Inc., 2017, Page(s) 282
Live FeedbackTM Back to Results
Prev Next

PMP Exam 4
Filtered Mode: Displaying 200 questions
Question 41 of 200
Question ID: 612453
You are leading a project team with the development of the stakeholder engagement plan. Using
a data representation technique, you have created the diagram below, and you are sharing it with
your team.
How might you explain the purpose of this diagram?

---

- **A Visually organizes information about stakeholders and their relationship to each other and**
the organization
- **B Supports comparison between the current engagement levels of stakeholders and the**

---

desired engagement levels
- **C Identifies underlying reasons for the level of support of project stakeholders**
- **D Displays results of stakeholder analysis comparing to other organizations or other projects**
that are considered to be world class
Question answered incorrectly

**Hint:**

Which answer choice describes the data representation technique of mind mapping?
Correct Answer: A

**Explanation:**

The question states that the project team is developing the stakeholder engagement plan, which
suggests that the Plan Stakeholder Engagement process is being performed. The diagram
presented in the question is an example of a data representation technique referred to as mind
mapping, which may be used during the Plan Stakeholder Engagement process. Mind mapping is
used to visually organize information about stakeholders and their relationship to each other and
the organization.

**Details for Each Option:**

- **A Visually organizes information about stakeholders and their relationship to each other and**
the organization
Correct. The diagram presented in the question is an example of a data representation
technique referred to as mind mapping. Mind mapping is used to visually organize
information about stakeholders and their relationship to each other and the organization.
- **B Supports comparison between the current engagement levels of stakeholders and the**
desired engagement levels
Incorrect. This answer choice describes a stakeholder engagement assessment matrix. The
matrix compares the current and desired stakeholder engagement levels. The diagram
presented in the question does not provide stakeholder engagement levels, making this
answer choice incorrect.
- **C Identifies underlying reasons for the level of support of project stakeholders**

---

Incorrect. Root cause analysis identifies underlying reasons for the level of support of
project stakeholders. The diagram presented in the question does not indicate reasons for
the level of support of project stakeholders. Therefore, this answer choice can be
eliminated.
- **D Displays results of stakeholder analysis comparing to other organizations or other projects**
that are considered to be world class
Incorrect. This answer choice describes benchmarking which is an example of a data
gathering technique that can be used in the Plan Stakeholder Engagement process. Since
benchmarking is a data gathering technique, and the diagram presented in the question is
an example of the data representation technique, this choice is not the best answer to the
question asked.

**Reference:**

- **A Guide to the Project Management Body of Knowledge, (PMBOK® Guide) – Sixth Edition,**
Project Management Institute Inc., 2017, Page(s) 521; see also
https://www.pmi.org/learning/library/brainstorming-pizzazz-mind-mapping-5992

PMP Exam 4
Filtered Mode: Displaying 200 questions
Question 42 of 200
Question ID: 612710
- **A project manager conducted a walkthrough with the sponsors to obtain approval for the project**
deliverables. The sponsors were very pleased with the completed scope and after the inspection
sent a letter praising the project team for exceeding their expectations of quality.
Which of the following is least likely to be updated as the result of this letter?
- **A Quality management plan**
- **B Lessons learned register**
- **C Requirements traceability matrix**
- **D Requirements documentation**
Question answered incorrectly

**Hint:**

Project documents are updated with the results of the Validate Scope process to assist with the
management of the ongoing project as well as future projects.
Correct Answer: A

**Explanation:**

The scenario indicates that the project manager has carried out the Validate Scope process. In
this process, the project manager reviews verified deliverables from the Control Quality process
with the customer or sponsor. The inspection may take the form of a review or walkthrough.
Once the deliverables have been signed off as meeting acceptance criteria, several project
documents, such as the lessons learned register, the requirements documentation, and the
requirements traceability matrix can be updated as an output from this process. The question is
asking about a document that is the 'least' likely to be updated. The fact the customer praised
high-quality makes the quality management plan the least likely to need updating, making it the
best answer to the question asked.

---


**Details for Each Option:**

- **A Quality management plan**
Correct. The quality management plan documents how applicable policies will be
implemented to achieve the quality objectives of the project. There is nothing in the
scenario that indicates that any of the policies or their implementation should be modified
as a result of the successful inspection.
- **B Lessons learned register**
Incorrect. The lessons learned register is updated with information on challenges
encountered with ideas on how to avoid them in the future. This register is also updated to
highlight approaches that worked especially well. The project manager should add the
lessons learned about the efforts of managing quality and validating deliverables that led to
the sponsors' praise.
- **C Requirements traceability matrix**
Incorrect. The requirements traceability matrix is a grid that connects each requirement to
the deliverable that fulfills it. The matrix would be updated with the validation results,
making this choice an incorrect answer.
- **D Requirements documentation**
Incorrect. During the inspection, the client or sponsor compares each requirement to the
verified deliverables. As an output, the project manager should update the requirements
documentation with the validation results, including client signoff, change requests,
waivers of requirements and cases where quality exceeds requirements. As a project
document that would be updated, the requirements document is an incorrect answer.

**Reference:**

- **A Guide to the Project Management Body of Knowledge, (PMBOK® Guide) – Sixth Edition,**
Project Management Institute Inc., 2017, Page(s) 166-167
Live FeedbackTM Back to Results

PMP Exam 4
Filtered Mode: Displaying 200 questions
Question 43 of 200
Question ID: 612629
You work as a project manager for an organization that has a directive type of project
management office (PMO). The PMO requires you to document relevant information in the
lessons learned register.
What is the main purpose of preparing this documentation?
- **A To enable the ongoing improvement of products, services, and processes**
- **B To capture issues and risks and document how they were handled**
- **C To ensure quality policies and procedures are implemented on the project**
- **D To satisfy the requirements of the project management office (PMO)**
Question answered incorrectly

**Hint:**

The lessons learned register is a project document used to record knowledge gained during a
project.
Correct Answer: A

**Explanation:**

Continuous improvement, sometimes called continual improvement, is the ongoing improvement
of products, services or processes through incremental and/or breakthrough improvements. The
lessons learned register is a project document used to record knowledge gained during a project
so that it can be used to improve performance in the current project and entered into the lessons
learned repository for use in future projects. The lessons learned register is produced as an output
of the Manage Project Knowledge process and then used as an input and updated as an output in
many processes throughout the project. The main purpose of capturing information in the lessons
learned register is so it can be used throughout the project lifecycle to improve the performance
of the current project as well as future projects. In this manner, documenting the knowledge
gained during the project in the lessons learned register supports continuous improvement.
Therefore, of the available choices, enabling the ongoing improvement of products, services, and
processes best describes the purpose of documenting relevant information in the lessons learned

---

register.

**Details for Each Option:**

- **A To enable the ongoing improvement of products, services, and processes**
Correct. The lessons learned register is a project document used to record knowledge
gained during a project so that it can be used to improve products, services, and processes
in the current project and entered into the lessons learned repository for use in future
projects.
- **B To capture issues and risks and document how they were handled**
Incorrect. While the lessons learned register might include issues and risks and how they
were handled, it is not limited to issues and risks. The lessons learned register is used to
document the knowledge gained during the project to improve future performance.
Additionally, issues are primarily recorded in the issue log and risks are recorded in the
risk register. Another answer choice better addresses the question asked.
- **C To ensure quality policies and procedures are implemented on the project**
Incorrect. Ensuring quality policies and procedures are implemented on the project is part
of the activities associated with the Project Quality Management Knowledge Area.
Documenting information in the lessons learned register serves another purpose.
- **D To satisfy the requirements of the project management office (PMO)**
Incorrect. Although complying with organizational requirements might motivate a project
manager to maintain a lessons learned register, the question is asking for the main purpose
of preparing this documentation. The purpose of preparing and maintaining the lessons
learned register is to document the knowledge gained during the project in order to
improve future performance.

**Reference:**

- **A Guide to the Project Management Body of Knowledge, (PMBOK® Guide) – Sixth Edition,**
Project Management Institute Inc., 2017, Page(s) 48, 104, 113; see also http://asq.org/learn-
about-quality/continuous-improvement/overview/overview.html
Live FeedbackTM Back to Results
Prev Next

PMP Exam 4
Filtered Mode: Displaying 200 questions
Question 44 of 200
Question ID: 612766
To determine the project needs and structure, the project manager has had several meetings with
the project sponsor and some of the key stakeholders. As a result, the project manager has
completed the development of a document that describes the project purpose, quantifiable
criteria that must be met by the project, and key deliverables.
What should the project manager do next?
- **A Get approval for the document**
- **B Develop the project management plan**
- **C Develop the project charter**
- **D Identify stakeholders and analyze them**
Question answered incorrectly

**Hint:**

What is required before a project is formally authorized?
Correct Answer: A

**Explanation:**

The document described in the scenario is the project charter. The project charter documents
high-level information on the project and describes the quantifiable criteria that must be met by
the project as well as the key deliverables. Chartering a project validates the alignment of the
project to the strategy and ongoing work of the organization. An 'approved' project charter
formally authorizes the project and allows the project manager to apply organizational resources
to project activities. Hence, of the choices provided, getting the approval of the document,
namely the project charter, is what the project manager should do next and is, therefore, the best
answer to the question asked.
Note, while some of the elements typically included in the project charter are not specified in the
scenario (such as the high-level risks, assumptions, constraints, milestone list, etc.), it can be
reasonably assumed the document described by the scenario is a project charter.

---


**Details for Each Option:**

- **A Get approval for the document**
Correct. The document described in the scenario is the project charter. The project charter
documents high-level information on the project, the quantifiable criteria that must be met
by the project, and the key deliverables. To authorize the project officially, the project
charter should be approved.
- **B Develop the project management plan**
Incorrect. The project management plan is a comprehensive document that defines the
project work and how the work will be performed. The project charter is an input to the
Develop Project Management Plan process. Since the scenario implies the project charter
has not yet been approved, the development of the project management plan cannot begin.
- **C Develop the project charter**
Incorrect. The project charter documents high-level information on the project and
describes the quantifiable criteria that must be met by the project. The scenario implies the
document the project manager helped develop is the project charter. Since the project
charter has already been developed, this answer choice is incorrect.
- **D Identify stakeholders and analyze them**
Incorrect. The document described in the scenario is the project charter. Since the project
charter authorizes both the project and the project manager, getting the charter approved
should precede any other activity, including the identification of stakeholders and
stakeholder analysis.

**Reference:**

- **A Guide to the Project Management Body of Knowledge, (PMBOK® Guide) – Sixth Edition,**
Project Management Institute Inc., 2017, Page(s) 81
Live FeedbackTM Back to Results

PMP Exam 4
Filtered Mode: Displaying 200 questions
Question 45 of 200
Question ID: 613550
- **A project manager is leading a project to install self-service kiosks. After a bidder conference,**
one of the prospective vendors asks the project manager if a WiFi connection is required to
establish connectivity with the kiosks. The project manager realizes that the WiFi is indeed
required but was not discussed at the conference nor was it part of the bid documents.
What is the best course of action for the project manager?
- **A Thank the vendor for raising this point and let this vendor know that WiFi access should be**
delivered
- **B Send a formal letter to all prospective vendors clarifying that WiFi access is part of the bid**
- **C Hold another bidder conference with all prospective vendors to clarify the WiFi**
requirement
- **D Ignore the question as no additional clarifications are allowed after the conference has been**
concluded
Question answered incorrectly

**Hint:**

What is the best and most efficient way to ensure fairness in the procurement process?
Correct Answer: B

**Explanation:**

The scenario presents a situation where providing one vendor with critical information may give
a competitive advantage to that vendor. The PMI Code of Ethics and Professional Conduct sets a
standard of fairness which is applicable in this case. The Code reads, "Fairness is our duty to
make decisions and act impartially and objectively. Our conduct must be free from competing
self interest, prejudice, and favoritism." It also states, "We provide equal access to information to
those who are authorized to have that information." Sending a clarification to all of the vendors
ensures that they all have a clear and common understanding of the procurement and that no one
has an unfair advantage. This action is consistent with the standard of fairness as described by
the PMI Code of Ethics and Professional Conduct and provides the most efficient and effective

---

method of ensuring the vendors have all of the necessary information to prepare their proposals.

**Details for Each Option:**

- **A Thank the vendor for raising this point and let this vendor know that WiFi access should be**
delivered
Incorrect. The knowledge of a WiFi requirement might give the vendor that asked the
question a competitive advantage over the other vendors that attended the bidder
conference. This situation would create a conflict with the value of fairness as described by
the PMI Code of Ethics and Professional Conduct.
- **B Send a formal letter to all prospective vendors clarifying that WiFi access is part of the bid**
Correct. Sending a clarification to all of the prospective vendors ensures that they have a
clear and common understanding of the procurement and that no one has an unfair
advantage. This action is consistent with the standard of fairness outlined in the PMI Code
of Ethics and Professional Conduct.
- **C Hold another bidder conference with all prospective vendors to clarify the WiFi**
requirement
Incorrect. Holding another bidder conference to clarify the WiFi requirement would ensure
the fairness of the bid process. However, doing this would not be the best use of time for the
project manager and the vendors. There is another answer choice which is aligned with the
value of fairness in a more efficient manner.
- **D Ignore the question as no additional clarifications are allowed after the conference has been**
concluded
Incorrect. Having the WiFi is a project requirement and, therefore, should be
communicated to the vendors. Additionally, the purpose of a bidder conference is to ensure
that the vendors have a clear and common understanding of the procurement. If an
important aspect of the project was overlooked during the bidder conference, a
clarification should be provided to all of the vendors that were in attendance.

**Reference:**

- **A Guide to the Project Management Body of Knowledge, (PMBOK® Guide) – Sixth Edition,**
Project Management Institute Inc., 2017, Page(s) 3; see also The PMI Code of Ethics and
Professional Conduct, Fairness

---

PMP Exam 4
Filtered Mode: Displaying 200 questions
Question 46 of 200
Question ID: 613708
You as a project manager have outsourced a portion of your work to a vendor with whom neither
you nor the sponsor has worked with before. You have a cost-reimbursable contract with the
seller. The sponsor, on more than one occasion, has discussed his concerns with you that the
seller could easily increase their profits with this type of agreement.
What should you tell the sponsor to decrease his apprehensions?
- **A You audit every invoice to ensure the costs are applicable and chargeable to your project.**
- **B You do not expect any changes to the scope.**
- **C The seller has the risk with this type of contract.**
- **D With this type of contract, the seller agrees to a set reimbursement amount, so the final**
costs to your project are pre-determined.
Question answered incorrectly

**Hint:**

Part of the Control Procurements process is monitoring payments to the sellers.
Correct Answer: A

**Explanation:**

The Control Procurements process has a financial management component that involves
monitoring payments to the seller. One of the chief concerns is making sure the charges from the
seller represent the work that has been completed. By auditing the seller invoices, you can ensure
the seller is charging you correctly for the work that has been completed. In this scenario, the
audit should help ease the sponsor's concerns of being overcharged by the seller.

**Details for Each Option:**


---

- **A You audit every invoice to ensure the costs are applicable and chargeable to your project.**
Correct. A cost-reimbursable contract involves payments (cost reimbursements) to the
seller for all costs incurred for completed work. By auditing every invoice, you can ensure
that the costs that have been billed are aligned with the work that has been completed and
any extra charges will be investigated. This proactive review should put the sponsor at ease
regarding the cost-reimbursable contract.
- **B You do not expect any changes to the scope.**
Incorrect. A cost-reimbursable contract involves payments (cost reimbursements) to the
seller for all costs incurred for completed work. This type of agreement is used when the
scope of the work is expected to change, and costs cannot be estimated accurately enough
to use a fixed-price contract, which has less buyer cost risk. If you did not expect changes
to the scope, you would likely have negotiated a fixed-price contract. Furthermore, saying
that you do not expect 'any' changes to the scope is likely to be unrealistic even with fixed-
price contracts.
- **C The seller has the risk with this type of contract.**
Incorrect. A cost-reimbursable contract involves payments (cost reimbursements) to the
seller for all costs incurred for completed work. In this type of agreement, you, as the
buyer, have the most cost risk because the total costs are unknown.
- **D With this type of contract, the seller agrees to a set reimbursement amount, so the final**
costs to your project are pre-determined.
Incorrect. This answer is describing a fixed-price contract where a fixed total price is set
for the work while in the scenario described you have a cost-reimbursable contract which
involves payments (cost reimbursements) to the seller for all costs incurred for completed
work.

**Reference:**

- **A Guide to the Project Management Body of Knowledge, (PMBOK® Guide) – Sixth Edition,**
Project Management Institute Inc., 2017, Page(s) 494, 471-472
Live FeedbackTM Back to Results

Filtered Mode: Displaying 200 questions
Question 47 of 200
Question ID: 612468
- **A project manager is reviewing a document where information about problems impacting project**
performance is recorded and monitored. According to the document, a new problem that was
logged yesterday by a project team member indicates that delays have just exceeded the
established schedule variance threshold and corrective action is required. No additional details
about the new problem are provided in the document.
What should the project manager do immediately?
- **A Assign a responsible party to follow up on the problem**
- **B Record the disposition of the change request**
- **C Send the project progress report to the stakeholders**
- **D Update the lessons learned register**
Question answered incorrectly

**Hint:**

What other information should be recorded in the issue log?
Correct Answer: A

**Explanation:**

Based on the scenario described, the project is in the Monitor and Control Project Work process.
The question implies that the project manager is reviewing the issue log, which is an input to this
process. The question indicates a new issue has been recorded. The issue log is a project
document where information about issues is captured and monitored. According to the scenario,
the information already recorded in the issue log includes the name of the person who raised the
issue, the date the issue was captured, and a description of the issue. Other information that
should be documented in the issue log includes the name of the person assigned to the issue,
priority of the issue, target resolution date, status, and final resolution. The question indicates
that corrective action is required, therefore, of the available choices, the next logical step for the
project manager is to assign a responsible party to follow up on the issue so it can be addressed
and then record that information in the issue log.

---


**Details for Each Option:**

- **A Assign a responsible party to follow up on the problem**
Correct. The question implies that the project manager is reviewing the issue log, and a
new issue was documented. The next logical step for the project manager is to assign a
responsible party to follow up on the issue and record that information in the issue log.
- **B Record the disposition of the change request**
Incorrect. The disposition of all change requests is captured in the change log. The
question is describing the issue log as opposed to the change log, and the disposition of
change requests is not recorded in the issue log. Additionally, the question does not provide
any information suggesting a change request has been submitted.
- **C Send the project progress report to the stakeholders**
Incorrect. Typically, the communications management plan would define how project
communications will be planned, structured, implemented, and monitored for effectiveness.
There is not enough information in the question to determine if this plan requires to send of
the project progress report to stakeholders under the circumstances described in the
scenario.
- **D Update the lessons learned register**
Incorrect. Knowledge gained during the project should be captured in the lessons learned
register to improve future performance on the project. However, based on the limited
information available to the project manager, there are no lessons learned to be
documented at this point. Additionally, the project manager should first seek to the resolve
the problem at hand before being concerned about updating the lessons learned register.

**Reference:**

- **A Guide to the Project Management Body of Knowledge, (PMBOK® Guide) – Sixth Edition,**
Project Management Institute Inc., 2017, Page(s) 96, 108-109

Question 48 of 200
Question ID: 612140
You are currently carrying out activities to determine whether the quality processes agreed on in
the quality management plan are providing the intended results, whether the work that was
planned to measure the quality of the product is the right work to meet the customer
requirements, and whether the procedures and policies are being followed as planned.
Which process are you currently involved in?
- **A Control Quality**
- **B Manage Quality**
- **C Plan Quality Management**
- **D Perform Quality Assurance**
Question answered incorrectly

**Hint:**

Which part of the Project Quality Management Knowledge Area is being focused on in the
scenario?
Correct Answer: B

**Explanation:**

The Manage Quality process uses the measurements gathered in the Control Quality process to
determine the following;
• Whether the quality processes agreed on in the quality management plan are providing the
intended results,
• Whether the work that was planned to measure the quality of the product is the right work to
meet the customer requirements and the right quality,
• Whether the procedures and policies are being followed as planned, and

---

• Can any improvements be made?
The activities you are performing in the scenario described are essentially the broader definition
of the Manage Quality process, making the Manage Quality process the best answer to the
question asked.

**Details for Each Option:**

- **A Control Quality**
Incorrect. Control Quality is the process of measuring the quality of the deliverables to
determine if they meet the requirements outlined in the quality management plan. The
scenario describes a different set of activities which does not fall under the definition of the
Control Quality process.
- **B Manage Quality**
Correct. The scenario ultimately specifies some of the main activities associated with the
Manage Quality process.
- **C Plan Quality Management**
Incorrect. Plan Quality Management is the process of determining how you will measure
and what methods you will use to make sure you are meeting the requirements of the
deliverable. Those activities are different from what is being described by the scenario
provided.
- **D Perform Quality Assurance**
Incorrect. 'Perform Quality Assurance' is not a process specified in the PMBOK® Guide,
Sixth Edition.

**Reference:**

- **A Guide to the Project Management Body of Knowledge, (PMBOK® Guide) – Sixth Edition,**
Project Management Institute Inc., 2017, Page(s) 288-290

PMP Exam 4
Filtered Mode: Displaying 200 questions
Question 49 of 200
Question ID: 612090
- **A project has short iterative planning and executing cycles where the requirements are**
progressively elaborated. The key stakeholders are continuously involved and provide frequent
feedback allowing the team to respond to changes more quickly.
What is the best way for the project manager to manage quality in this type of project
environment?
- **A By conducting periodic quality audits**
- **B By using the Validate Scope process**
- **C By scheduling regular retrospectives**
- **D By using the quality control matrix**
Question answered incorrectly

**Hint:**

How is quality managed on agile projects?
Correct Answer: C

**Explanation:**

The project in the scenario is using an agile methodology which focuses on small batches of
work and allows the team to uncover inconsistencies and quality issues earlier in the project life
cycle. Quality is managed by scheduling regular retrospectives to check on the effectiveness of
the quality processes. During a retrospective, root causes of issues are sought, and new
approaches are suggested to improve the development process in general and quality in
particular. Subsequent retrospectives evaluate any new approaches to determine if they are
working and should be continued, need adjusting, or should be dropped from use. Therefore, of
the available choices, scheduling regular retrospectives is the best way for the project manager to

---

manage quality on his project which is being conducted using agile practices.

**Details for Each Option:**

- **A By conducting periodic quality audits**
Incorrect. A quality audit is a structured independent process to determine if project
activities comply with organizational and project policies, processes, and procedures.
While it's important to conduct quality audits, the question is asking about the best way to
manage quality in the project environment described in the scenario. The scenario
describes a project which is managed using agile methodologies where recurring
retrospectives, rather than audits, are the best practice to check on the effectiveness of the
quality processes.
- **B By using the Validate Scope process**
Incorrect. Validate Scope is the process of formalizing acceptance of the completed project
deliverables. The project in the scenario is using agile methodology where requirements, or
scope, is defined and redefined throughout the project. Since the scope is defined
iteratively, the Validate Scope process, in its traditional or waterfall meaning, is not
performed. Additionally, even if the question was about a traditional project, the Manage
Quality and Control Quality processes, not the Validate Scope process, are used to manage
quality on a project.
- **C By scheduling regular retrospectives**
Correct. Retrospectives are recurring meetings that are intended to regularly check on the
effectiveness of the quality processes. Retrospectives are typically used on projects that are
conducted using agile methodologies. Since the scenario describes an agile environment,
using recurring retrospectives would be the best tool for the project manager to use on his
project to manage quality.
- **D By using the quality control matrix**
Incorrect. 'Quality control matrix' is a made-up term.

**Reference:**

- **A Guide to the Project Management Body of Knowledge, (PMBOK® Guide) – Sixth Edition,**
Project Management Institute Inc., 2017, Page(s) 276, 666

Question 50 of 200
Question ID: 651311
In a meeting with all the project managers of a department-wide improvement program, the
program manager states the program’s mission and authority relationships.
As one of the project managers attending the meeting, what do the mission and authority
relationships represent to your project?
- **A Organizational process assets**
- **B Matrix organization**
- **C Enterprise environmental factors**
- **D Project requirements**
Question answered incorrectly

**Hint:**

These conditions are not under the control of the project manager.
Correct Answer: C

**Explanation:**

Any condition or factor that stems from outside the project or even outside the project’s
enterprise is considered an enterprise environmental factor. The program’s mission, values, and
authority relationships are outside the project’s immediate control, yet they factor into how the
project operates within the enterprise. Hence these are good examples of enterprise
environmental factors.

**Details for Each Option:**


---

- **A Organizational process assets**
Incorrect. Organizational process assets are the materials, resources, and references, for
example, that an enterprise may supply or mandate on a project. What the program
manager here is providing are not assets but conditions in which the program is intended
to operate within and controlled.
- **B Matrix organization**
Incorrect. Matrix organizations are organizational constructs of a project. There are no
specific organizational structures being discussed in this question, only that there are
projects within a program.
- **C Enterprise environmental factors**
Correct. The program’s mission statement and authority relationships are outside the
immediate control of the project and the project team. Hence these are examples of
enterprise environmental factors.
- **D Project requirements**
Incorrect. Although not explicitly stated, some of the program’s mission and authority
relationships may equate into project requirements. There is no indication that all projects
are required to deliver on an authority relationship, for example.

**Reference:**

- **A Guide to the Project Management Body of Knowledge, (PMBOK® Guide) – Sixth Edition,**
Project Management Institute Inc., 2017, Page(s) 557
