Question 75 of 200
Question ID: 612535
- **A project is underway for the launch of a new tea. Before launch, the tea will be subjected to**
internal tests to ensure conformance to specific standards. After the initial tests are conducted,
recommendations to improve both the hand-picking technique and the way the tea is delivered
for processing are identified. The project manager is preparing a progress report and would like
to include information about the recommendations.
Where can the project manager find this information?
- **A Change log**
- **B Quality report**
- **C Issue log**
- **D Risk report**
Question answered incorrectly

**Hint:**

Which Knowledge Area deals with process improvements?
Correct Answer: B

**Explanation:**

In the scenario, the project manager is gathering information for a progress report that he wants
to share with the stakeholders, implying that the Manage Communications process is underway.
One of the inputs to the Manage Communications process is the quality report which is an output
of the Manage Quality process. The quality report contains information on quality issues and
process improvements. Since the project manager wants to include the recommendations for
process improvements in his progress report, he should consult the quality report.

---


**Details for Each Option:**

- **A Change log**
Incorrect. The change log is a list of changes submitted to the organization's change
control process during the project and their current status. The recommendations
mentioned in the scenario are process improvements and not changes, and, therefore,
would not be included in the change log.
- **B Quality report**
Correct. Information in the quality report includes quality issues, project and product
improvements, and process improvements. In the scenario, improvements to both the tea
picking and delivery processes were identified and would be documented in the quality
report, making the quality report the best place to find the information.
- **C Issue log**
Incorrect. The issue log contains information about problems, gaps, inconsistencies, or
conflicts that occur unexpectedly and require action. The recommendations identified in the
scenario are process improvements and not issues.
- **D Risk report**
Incorrect. The risk report presents information on both overall project risk and individual
project risk. While the implementation of the recommendations to improve the process may
introduce risk, the recommendations themselves are not considered risks and, therefore,
would not have been included in the risk report.

**Reference:**

- **A Guide to the Project Management Body of Knowledge, (PMBOK® Guide) – Sixth Edition,**
Project Management Institute Inc., 2017, Page(s) 382, 296

PMP Exam 4

Question 76 of 200
Question ID: 613765
Your project team has evaluated each identified risk and assigned an estimated dollar amount or
time impact to it. To determine which risks will require more detailed response plans, you ask
them to compare the risks and determine which ones could most impact the project. You want
the data in graph form, with the risks displayed in order from greatest to least potential impact on
the project.
What would be the best tool for the team to use in this case?
- **A Ishikawa diagram**
- **B Tornado diagram**
- **C Decision tree diagram**
- **D Bubble chart**
Question answered incorrectly

**Hint:**

Which diagram is named after the funnel shape of its bars and is used to analyze project
sensitivity to cost or other factors?
Correct Answer: B

**Explanation:**

In this scenario, you are looking for a diagram that will depict the relative potential impact of
each risk on project outcomes, with the risks ranked from greatest to least potential impact. A
tornado diagram is the best tool to accomplish that. The other answer choices are all tools used in
risk assessment or sensitivity analysis, but the tornado diagramming technique is perfectly suited
for this purpose.

---


**Details for Each Option:**

- **A Ishikawa diagram**
Incorrect. An Ishikawa diagram is used to perform root cause analysis. You would use this
technique if your goal were to discover the underlying causes of project risks and
determine preventive action.
- **B Tornado diagram**
Correct. As the project manager, you are requesting a diagram that depicts the relative
potential impact of each risk on project outcomes, with the risks ranked from greatest to
least potential impact. A tornado diagram is the best tool to accomplish that.
- **C Decision tree diagram**
Incorrect. Decision trees can be useful in determining the best of several alternative
courses of action by comparing their associated costs and related project risks (in other
words, quantifying the potential outcomes of risk scenarios). A tornado diagram, however,
is more suited for this purpose (analyzing project sensitivity to risk) and is, therefore, the
best answer choice.
- **D Bubble chart**
Incorrect. A bubble chart is a technique of the Perform Qualitative Risk Analysis process
used to display risks that have been categorized using more than two parameters.

**Reference:**

- **A Guide to the Project Management Body of Knowledge, (PMBOK® Guide) – Sixth Edition,**
Project Management Institute Inc., 2017, Page(s) 434-435, 425-426, 415

Question 77 of 200
Question ID: 613725
The project is behind schedule. A team member thinks activity A needs more resources, while
another wants the resources added to activity B. A third team member suggests a compromise by
adding resources to both activities and recovering a week from each. The project manager ends
the discussion and makes the unilateral decision to run activities D and E in parallel instead of
sequentially.
Which conflict management technique is the project manager using to resolve the issue?
- **A Force or direct**
- **B Compromise**
- **C Crashing**
- **D Fast tracking**
Question answered incorrectly

**Hint:**

Which conflict management technique is usually enforced through a power position to resolve a
conflict?
Correct Answer: A

**Explanation:**

The PMBOK® Guide describes five techniques for conflict management. These techniques
include withdraw/avoid, smooth/accommodate, compromise/reconcile, force/direct, and
collaboration/problem solve. In this scenario, the project manager used a position of power to
enforce a decision in order to resolve the conflict. Pushing one’s viewpoint at the expense of
others is known as a force/direct approach. Note, force/direct conflict resolution technique is
typically used to resolve an emergency. There is not enough information in the question to
determine if the two weeks delay is considered an emergency. However, among the choices

---

given, force/direct is the best answer to the question asked as it accurately describes the action
taken by the project manager.

**Details for Each Option:**

- **A Force or direct**
Correct. Force/direct is a conflict management technique defined by pushing one’s
viewpoint at the expense of others. It is usually enforced through a position of power to
resolve a conflict.
- **B Compromise**
Incorrect. In this scenario, a compromise was suggested, but the project manager made the
decision from a position of power.
- **C Crashing**
Incorrect. Crashing is a schedule compression technique which adds resources to an
activity on the critical path. However, this is not a conflict management technique.
- **D Fast tracking**
Incorrect. Fast tracking is a schedule compression technique where an activity is run in
parallel instead of sequentially. However, this is not a conflict management technique.

**Reference:**

- **A Guide to the Project Management Body of Knowledge, (PMBOK® Guide) – Sixth Edition,**
Project Management Institute Inc., 2017, Page(s) 348-349
Live FeedbackTM Back to Results
Prev Next

PMP Exam 4
Filtered Mode: Displaying 200 questions
Question 78 of 200
Question ID: 612415
You are leading a large and complex project. Due to the size and complexity of the project, you
have decided that a project management team will perform most of the planning, and the
remainder of the project team will be brought on when the initial planning is complete.
In this scenario, when is the best time to conduct the project kick-off meeting?
- **A During project execution**
- **B Shortly after project initiation**
- **C As part of pre-project work**
- **D During initial project planning**
Question answered incorrectly

**Hint:**

The kick-off meeting is held later in the project for large projects compared to smaller projects.
Correct Answer: A

**Explanation:**

The question describes a large and complex project. In large projects, a project management
team normally does the majority of the planning, and the remainder of the project team is
brought on when the initial planning is complete, at the start of the development/implementation.
In this instance, the kick-off meeting takes place with processes in the Execution Process Group.
Therefore, of the choices provided, conducting the kick-off meeting during project execution is
the best answer to the question asked.

---


**Details for Each Option:**

- **A During project execution**
Correct. A project management team typically does the majority of the planning for a large
project, and the remainder of the project team is brought on at the start of project
execution. Therefore, the kick-off meeting for a large project should take place with
processes in the Execution Process Group, making this the correct answer choice.
- **B Shortly after project initiation**
Incorrect. For small projects, the kick-off occurs shortly after initiation because the same
team usually performs planning and execution. However, the question describes the project
as being large and complex, making this an incorrect response.
- **C As part of pre-project work**
Incorrect. Pre-project work consists of creating the business case and benefits management
plan before project initiation. The project is not authorized until the project charter has
been approved. The kick-off meeting is held to communicate the start of the project, engage
stakeholders, and gain commitment. Communicating the start of the project, engaging
stakeholders, and gaining commitment to the project that has not been authorized does not
make sense.
- **D During initial project planning**
Incorrect. The scenario states that only the project management team will be involved in
the initial planning due to the size and complexity of the project. After initial planning is
complete, the remainder of the project team is typically brought on to complete the rest of
planning and start project execution. It is easier to gain commitment to the project from
individuals who were part of its planning. Since one of the project kick-off meeting’s goals
is to gain commitment, initial project planning is not the best time for the project kick-off
meeting to be conducted without having the remainder of the project team onboard.

**Reference:**

- **A Guide to the Project Management Body of Knowledge, (PMBOK® Guide) – Sixth Edition,**
Project Management Institute Inc., 2017, Page(s) 86
Live FeedbackTM Back to Results

Filtered Mode: Displaying 200 questions
Question 79 of 200
Question ID: 613790
The vendor selection process is underway for a natural gas pipeline project. The project manager
has received numerous proposals in response to a request for proposal (RFP). He wants to ensure
that the submitted proposals are complete and meet the requirements as specified in the
procurement documentation provided to the prospective vendors.
What tool or technique should the project manager use in this situation?
- **A Data analysis**
- **B Performance reviews**
- **C Audits**
- **D Inspection**
Question answered incorrectly

**Hint:**

Of the available choices, which is the only tool or technique that is typically used during the
Conduct Procurements process to evaluate the vendors’ proposals?
Correct Answer: A

**Explanation:**

The question implies that the Conduct Procurements process is being performed. To evaluate the
proposals of the prospective vendors during that process, a data analysis technique can be used.
Proposals are evaluated to ensure they are complete and respond in full to the bid documents,
procurement statement of work, source selection criteria, and any other documents that went out
in the bid package. Additionally, of the available choices, only data analysis is a tool or
technique used in the Conduct Procurements process.

---


**Details for Each Option:**

- **A Data analysis**
Correct. A data analysis technique that can be used during the Conduct Procurements
process includes proposal evaluation. Proposals are evaluated to ensure they are complete
and respond in full to the bid documents, procurement statement of work, source selection
criteria, and any other documents that went out in the bid package.
- **B Performance reviews**
Incorrect. Performance reviews analyze the performance of a vendor against the contract,
as opposed to analyzing the proposal submitted by the vendor.
- **C Audits**
Incorrect. Audits are a structured review of the procurement process. Since audits are used
to evaluate the procurement process rather than vendors’ proposals, this choice can be
eliminated as a correct answer.
- **D Inspection**
Incorrect. Inspection is a structured review of the work being performed by the vendor,
rather than an evaluation of the proposal submitted by the vendor.

**Reference:**

- **A Guide to the Project Management Body of Knowledge, (PMBOK® Guide) – Sixth Edition,**
Project Management Institute Inc., 2017, Page(s) 487
Live FeedbackTM Back to Results

PMP Exam 4
Filtered Mode: Displaying 200 questions
Question 80 of 200
Question ID: 612464
- **A project manager is leading a project to produce a new model of an x-ray machine. The quality**
assurance lead provides checklists that the team needs to use and follow at all times. Also,
rigorous reviews are required at the end of each stage of the manufacturing process.
What tool or technique should the project manager use to determine if project activities comply
with organizational and project policies, processes, and procedures?
- **A Process analysis**
- **B Quality audits**
- **C Design for X (DfX)**
- **D Quality reports**
Question answered incorrectly

**Hint:**

Which of the available options is a compliance tool?
Correct Answer: B

**Explanation:**

The question implies that the Manage Quality process is being conducted. A quality audit is a
tool used during the Manage Quality process to provide a structured, independent process to
determine if project activities comply with organizational and project policies, processes, and
procedures. Therefore, of the choices provided, the best tool or technique for the project manager
to use to ensure compliance is quality audits.

---


**Details for Each Option:**

- **A Process analysis**
Incorrect. Process analysis is an example of a data analysis tool and technique that can be
used in the Manage Quality process to identify opportunities for process improvements.
The question is asking about process compliance rather than process improvement.
- **B Quality audits**
Correct. A quality audit is a structured, independent process to determine if project
activities comply with organizational and project policies, processes, and procedures.
- **C Design for X (DfX)**
Incorrect. Design for X (DfX) is a set of technical guidelines that can be used as a tool or
technique in the Manage Quality process. The DfX may be applied during the design of a
product for the optimization of a specific aspect of the design. The question is related to
compliance with established policies, processes, and procedures, and not optimization of a
design aspect.
- **D Quality reports**
Incorrect. A quality report is a project document and not a tool or technique. Therefore,
this answer choice can be eliminated as a correct response.

**Reference:**

- **A Guide to the Project Management Body of Knowledge, (PMBOK® Guide) – Sixth Edition,**
Project Management Institute Inc., 2017, Page(s) 294

PMP Exam 4
Filtered Mode: Displaying 200 questions
Question 81 of 200
Question ID: 613712
During a status update meeting, you provide stakeholders with a chart that tracks the work that
remains to be completed against the time left in this period of the project. You point out that the
actual rate at which the work is being completed is close to the ideal rate at which the work is
planned to be completed.
What type of chart did you show the stakeholders?
- **A Burndown chart**
- **B Milestone chart**
- **C Gantt chart**
- **D Project schedule network diagram**
Question answered incorrectly

**Hint:**

This chart is common in agile methodologies.
Correct Answer: A

**Explanation:**

- **A burndown chart graphically depicts the work that remains to be completed versus the days in**
the iteration. It is typically used on agile projects and aimed to analyze the variance with respect
to an ideal burndown based on the work committed from iteration planning. A diagonal line
representing the ideal remaining work each day, or the ideal burndown, and a second diagonal
line representing the actual remaining work each day are plotted on the chart. The burndown
chart gives a visualization of how the ideal rate of work is comparing with the actual rate of
work. Therefore, among the available choices, a burndown chart is the best response.

---


**Details for Each Option:**

- **A Burndown chart**
Correct. A burndown chart is typically used in agile project management to track the work
that remains to be completed versus the time left in the iteration. A diagonal line
representing the ideal rate at which the work is being completed, or the burndown, is
plotted with another line representing the daily actual remaining work. The resulting
burndown chart visually depicts the variance between the ideal rate of work and the actual
rate of work.
- **B Milestone chart**
Incorrect. A milestone chart is a project schedule that shows the anticipated completion
dates of major project deliverables. A milestone has no duration, and therefore has no rate
of completion; thus, it cannot be the chart shared with the stakeholders.
- **C Gantt chart**
Incorrect. A Gantt chart is a bar chart of the project schedule that shows activities listed on
the vertical axis and dates on the horizontal axis. The activity durations are shown as
horizontal bars placed according to start and finish dates. The Gantt chart is a graphical
depiction of the project schedule; it does not show a rate of completion.
- **D Project schedule network diagram**
Incorrect. A project schedule network diagram shows the activities and the relationship
between activities for the project and not a rate of completion.

**Reference:**

- **A Guide to the Project Management Body of Knowledge, (PMBOK® Guide) – Sixth Edition,**
Project Management Institute Inc., 2017, Page(s) 226, 217-218
Live FeedbackTM Back to Results

PMP Exam 4
Filtered Mode: Displaying 200 questions
Question 82 of 200
Question ID: 612481
- **A project to develop a new online game is in execution. One key stakeholder is adamant that a**
feature, currently not included in the scope baseline, is added to allow the game to be played on
smartphones. Another key stakeholder is just as convinced that a smartphone is too small to
provide adequate gameplay experience, and, if the feature is added, she says she will no longer
support the project.
What is the best course of action for the project manager?
- **A Reject the feature since it represents scope creep**
- **B Meet with both stakeholders to negotiate a resolution**
- **C Instruct the project team to implement the feature**
- **D Reject the feature since the project is in execution**
Question answered incorrectly

**Hint:**

Which tools and techniques associated with the Manage Stakeholder Engagement process might
be helpful in this scenario?
Correct Answer: B

**Explanation:**

The question suggests that the Manage Stakeholder Engagement process is about to be carried
out. Meetings and negotiation are two of the tools and techniques associated with this process. It
is not known from the question whether or not the added functionality will provide sufficient
benefit warranting a change request to be submitted to update the project management plan,
including the baselines. Regardless of whether or not a change request is ultimately submitted,
the project manager must address the conflict between the two key stakeholders. Additionally,
more information regarding the proposed changes and the objections should be gathered before

---

submitting the change request, thus supporting the need for the meeting between the project
manager and the stakeholders. Therefore, of the available choices, the next logical step is to meet
with the stakeholders to better understand their positions and negotiate a resolution to mitigate
any negative effects on stakeholder engagement.

**Details for Each Option:**

- **A Reject the feature since it represents scope creep**
Incorrect. Scope creep is considered the uncontrolled expansion of product or project
scope without adjustments to time, cost, and resources. The added functionality can be
included with an approved change request to update the project management plan and
included baselines.
- **B Meet with both stakeholders to negotiate a resolution**
Correct. The best course of action is to meet with the stakeholders to better understand
their positions and negotiate a resolution to mitigate any negative effects on stakeholder
engagement. The meeting would allow gathering more information regarding the proposed
changes and the objections before taking further action.
- **C Instruct the project team to implement the feature**
Incorrect. According to the scenario, the project is in execution. A scope cannot be added
at will without applying proper change management procedures. A change request is
required to add scope to a project which is in execution.
- **D Reject the feature since the project is in execution**
Incorrect. Changes can be made at any point in the project life cycle using the
organization's change control process via a change request. Rejecting the feature just
because the project is in execution goes against project management best practices and
guidelines.

**Reference:**

- **A Guide to the Project Management Body of Knowledge, (PMBOK® Guide) – Sixth Edition,**
Project Management Institute Inc., 2017, Page(s) 525, 527-528

PMP Exam 4
Filtered Mode: Displaying 200 questions
Question 83 of 200
Question ID: 612338
- **A project manager has just presented the project management plan at a meeting to the project**
sponsor and other stakeholders who have signed off on the plan.
What should the project manager do next?
- **A Develop the project schedule**
- **B Have the project sponsor approve the project charter**
- **C Acquire the necessary resources for the project**
- **D Request approval from the project sponsor to proceed with project execution**
Question answered incorrectly

**Hint:**

Reviewing the planning domain of the Project Management Professional (PMP)® Examination
Content Outline may be helpful in correctly answering this question.
Correct Answer: C

**Explanation:**

The Project Management Professional (PMP)® Examination Content Outline contains a list of
tasks for each domain, with which PMP aspirants are expected to be familiar. Task #11 of the
planning domain states, "Present the project management plan to the relevant stakeholders
according to applicable policies and procedures in order to obtain approval to proceed with
project execution." Of the available choices, only acquiring project resources is part of project
execution, making this the correct answer.

---


**Details for Each Option:**

- **A Develop the project schedule**
Incorrect. The project schedule is developed during project planning. Once the project
management plan has been reviewed and approved, project planning is complete, and
project execution can begin. Based on the scenario described, the project schedule has
already been developed as part of the project management plan and is, therefore, not what
the project manager should do next.
- **B Have the project sponsor approve the project charter**
Incorrect. The project charter is drafted and approved during the Develop Project Charter
process, which is part of project initiation. The scenario states that the project management
plan has been completed and approved. The project charter serves as an input into the
development of the project management plan; therefore, the project charter was approved
before the creation of the project management plan.
- **C Acquire the necessary resources for the project**
Correct. The Acquire Resources process is part of project execution. Once the project
management plan has been reviewed and approved, project execution begins. Of the
available choices, only acquiring project resources is part of project execution, making this
choice the correct answer.
- **D Request approval from the project sponsor to proceed with project execution**
Incorrect. There is not enough information in the question to determine if approval from
the project sponsor is required to proceed with project execution. Therefore, since the
project management plan has been approved, project execution can begin without any
further approvals.

**Reference:**

- **A Guide to the Project Management Body of Knowledge, (PMBOK® Guide) – Sixth Edition,**
Project Management Institute Inc., 2017, Page(s) 25; see also Project Management Professional
(PMP)® Examination Content Outline, Project Management Institute Inc., June 2015, Domain 2,
Task 11

PMP Exam 4
Filtered Mode: Displaying 200 questions
Question 84 of 200
Question ID: 612177
You are leading a project to build a bridge that will span a deep gorge. You require the use of
safety harnesses which are tethered to the structure during construction. However, you are
concerned that these efforts may not be enough to ensure the safety of the crew. Therefore, you
take action by having a net secured under the bridge as an additional safety measure.
What best describes the action you have taken in this scenario?
- **A A preventive action to protect the workers**
- **B A corrective action to ensure safety**
- **C A defect repair to fix the safety systems**
- **D A reactive measure to prevent a tragedy**
Question answered incorrectly

**Hint:**

The correct answer is an intentional activity that ensures the future performance of the project
work is aligned with the project management plan.
Correct Answer: A

**Explanation:**

Preventive action is an intentional activity that ensures the future performance of the project
work is aligned with the project management plan. Preventive action is distinguished from a
corrective action in that a problem is identified ‘before’ it occurs and steps are taken proactively
to avoid the problem from occurring. In this scenario, the safety issue is proactively addressed
before an accident occurs. Therefore, the action taken in this scenario is best described as a
preventive action.

---


**Details for Each Option:**

- **A A preventive action to protect the workers**
Correct. Preventive action is an intentional activity that ensures the future performance of
the project work is aligned with the project management plan. In this scenario, the safety
issue is proactively addressed before an accident occurs. Therefore, the action taken is best
described as a preventive action.
- **B A corrective action to ensure safety**
Incorrect. Corrective action is an intentional activity that realigns the performance of the
project work with the project management plan. A corrective action is a reactive measure
that is taken after the fact (after a problem occurs) rather than proactive. In this case, an
action is proactively taken to avoid a safety issue even though a failure of the safety
equipment has not yet occurred.
- **C A defect repair to fix the safety systems**
Incorrect. Defect repair is an intentional activity that modifies a nonconforming product or
product component. Repairing or replacing a defective safety harness would be considered
a defect repair, but that is not the action described by the question. The action taken in the
scenario describes an activity to prevent a problem from occurring in the future.
- **D A reactive measure to prevent a tragedy**
Incorrect. In this scenario, a proactive measure is being taken to ensure the safety of those
working on the bridge. A reactive measure suggests a failure of the safety equipment
occurred and actions were taken to avoid the failure in the future. However, the actions
described in the question are proactive and not reactive measures.

**Reference:**

- **A Guide to the Project Management Body of Knowledge, (PMBOK® Guide) – Sixth Edition,**
Project Management Institute Inc., 2017, Page(s) 96
Live FeedbackTM Back to Results

Question 85 of 200
Question ID: 610048
Approximately halfway through your project, a team member accidentally deleted computer files
representing hundreds of hours of work. You want to ensure this situation does not recur on the
project.
Where should you capture the knowledge gained by recording the impact, recommendations, and
proposed actions associated with this situation?
- **A Lessons learned register**
- **B Lessons learned repository**
- **C Lessons learned log**
- **D Risk register**
Question answered incorrectly

**Hint:**

What output of the Manage Project Knowledge process contains details of the knowledge gained
during the project?
Correct Answer: A

**Explanation:**

The question suggests that the Manage Project Knowledge process is being performed. One
output of the Manage Project Knowledge process is the lessons learned register. The lessons
learned register is a project document used to record knowledge gained during a project so that it
can be utilized in the current project. At the end of the project or phase, the information is
transferred to an organizational process asset called the lessons learned repository. The
knowledge gained during the project should be captured in the lessons learned register.

---


**Details for Each Option:**

- **A Lessons learned register**
Correct. The lessons learned register is a project document used to record knowledge
gained during a project for use in the current project.
- **B Lessons learned repository**
Incorrect. Knowledge gained during the project is recorded in the lessons learned register
and transferred to the lessons learned repository at the end of the project or phase. The
question indicates that the project is only halfway complete.
- **C Lessons learned log**
Incorrect. 'Lessons learned log' is a fake term made up for this question.
- **D Risk register**
Incorrect. The risk register is a repository that contains details of identified project risks
rather than lessons learned during the project.

**Reference:**

- **A Guide to the Project Management Body of Knowledge, (PMBOK® Guide) – Sixth Edition,**
Project Management Institute Inc., 2017, Page(s) 104

PMP Exam 4
Filtered Mode: Displaying 200 questions
Question 86 of 200
Question ID: 612158
- **A project manager is leading the development of a new car model. During testing, it is**
discovered that the power seats failed before 1,000 cycles, which is an unacceptable failure rate.
The problem is traced to an interference issue with the wiring harness and the seat rail. The
wiring diagram is updated to reroute the wiring harness to avoid the interference issue for the
production cars and prevent it from occurring in the future.
What best describes the measure taken to solve the problem in this scenario?
- **A A preventive action was performed**
- **B A corrective action was taken**
- **C The defect was repaired**
- **D A component was replaced**
Question answered incorrectly

**Hint:**

The correct answer is an intentional activity that realigns the performance of the project work
with the project management plan.
Correct Answer: B

**Explanation:**

Corrective action is an intentional activity that realigns the performance of the project work with
the project management plan. In this scenario, the problem of interference between the power
seat wiring harness and seat rail was identified after a failure occurred and steps were taken to
prevent the problem from happening in the future. The action of updating the wiring harness
diagram to prevent the failure from occurring in the future is best described as a corrective
action.

---

It is important for PMP aspirants to understand the difference between corrective action and
preventive action. The fundamental difference between a corrective and preventive action is in
how the problem is identified. If the problem is proactively identified 'before' the problem even
occurs, then the action taken to avoid the problem from occurring in the future is a preventive
action. However, if the problem is discovered after the fact, like the example of the power seat
failure, then the action taken to avoid the issue from recurring in the future is considered a
corrective action.

**Details for Each Option:**

- **A A preventive action was performed**
Incorrect. Preventive action is an intentional activity that ensures the future performance of
the project work with the project management plan. Preventive action is distinguished from
a corrective action in that a problem is identified before it occurs and steps are taken
proactively to avoid the problem from occurring. In this scenario, the problem was not
identified until it was uncovered during product testing, making it a reactive rather than a
proactive measure.
- **B A corrective action was taken**
Correct. Corrective action is an intentional activity that realigns the performance of the
project work with the project management plan. In this case, a problem was identified after
a failure occurred and steps are taken to prevent the problem from happening in the future.
Therefore, the action of updating the wiring harness diagram is best described as a
corrective action.
- **C The defect was repaired**
Incorrect. Defect repair is an intentional activity that modifies a nonconforming product or
product component. Repairing and rerouting the broken wiring harness would be
considered a defect repair, but that is not the action described by the question. The action
taken in the scenario describes the update of a wiring diagram to prevent a problem from
occurring in the future which can be best described as a corrective action rather than
defect repair.
- **D A component was replaced**
Incorrect. Replacing a component is a type of defect repair, where a defect is identified,
and the deliverable is modified by replacing a component to repair the defect. The scenario
describes an action being taken to avoid a problem on the production of vehicles in the

---

future rather than replacing a defective component.

**Reference:**

- **A Guide to the Project Management Body of Knowledge, (PMBOK® Guide) – Sixth Edition,**
Project Management Institute Inc., 2017, Page(s) 96
Live FeedbackTM Back to Results

PMP Exam 4
Filtered Mode: Displaying 200 questions
Question 87 of 200
Question ID: 612606
- **A team member is comparing one of the project deliverables, a web user interface, to the scope**
baseline to determine if there is any variance in the actual results. The team member encounters a
function named ‘customer detail print’ and wants to understand where this requirement came
from.
What should the team member review to understand the origin of this requirement?
- **A Scope management plan**
- **B Scope baseline**
- **C Configuration management plan**
- **D Requirements traceability matrix**
Question answered incorrectly

**Hint:**

How are product requirements linked from their origin to the deliverables that satisfy them?
Correct Answer: D

**Explanation:**

Based on the scenario described, the project is in the Control Scope process, and the
requirements traceability matrix is an input to this process. The requirements traceability matrix
is a grid that links product requirements from their origin to the deliverables that satisfy them.
Therefore, reviewing the requirements traceability matrix would allow the team member to
understand where the ‘customer detail print’ function came from, making the requirements
traceability matrix the best answer to the question asked.

---


**Details for Each Option:**

- **A Scope management plan**
Incorrect. The scope management plan is a component of the project management plan that
describes how the scope will be defined, developed, monitored, controlled, and validated.
The scope management plan does not indicate what is in or out of scope, but rather
documents how the scope is managed.
- **B Scope baseline**
Incorrect. The scope baseline is the approved version of a scope statement, work
breakdown structure (WBS), and its associated WBS dictionary. Although the scope
baseline should encompass the entire scope of the project, it does not connect the detailed
features and functions back to the requirements as requested by the scenario.
- **C Configuration management plan**
Incorrect. The configuration management plan is a component of the project management
plan that describes how to identify and account for project artifacts under configuration
control. The configuration management plan does not provide insight into project
requirements.
- **D Requirements traceability matrix**
Correct. The requirements traceability matrix is a grid that links product requirements
from their origin to the deliverables that satisfy them.

**Reference:**

- **A Guide to the Project Management Body of Knowledge, (PMBOK® Guide) – Sixth Edition,**
Project Management Institute Inc., 2017, Page(s) 169

PMP Exam 4
Filtered Mode: Displaying 200 questions
Question 88 of 200
Question ID: 612970
You and appropriate stakeholders have conducted the project benefit analysis and developed the
business case for a project to build a new robotic production line. The business case indicates
that the total cost of the project will be $150,000 including installation and setup, and the cost
savings are expected to be $40,000 annually.
What can be said about this project?
- **A The $150,000 investment is considered a sunk cost at this point in the project**
- **B The opportunity cost is too high to continue with this project**
- **C The robot will pay for itself within three years**
- **D The payback period is 45 months**
Question answered incorrectly

**Hint:**

How long will it take to recover the initial investment?
Correct Answer: D

**Explanation:**

Payback period is the time it takes for the organization to earn back the initial investment (in
terms of monetary cost) to the project and begin making profits. In this case, the $150,000
investment divided by the cost savings of $40,000 annually is 3.75 years or 45 months.
Therefore, the payback period is 45 months, and the only correct answer among the available
choices.
While the topic of this question is just briefly mentioned in the PMBOK® Guide, the Project
Management Professional (PMP)® Examination Content Outline, June 2015, covers knowledge
and skills with which PMP aspirants are expected to be familiar. Project finance principles are

---

among these knowledge and skills.

**Details for Each Option:**

- **A The $150,000 investment is considered a sunk cost at this point in the project**
Incorrect. Sunk costs are the costs that have already been incurred which cannot be
recovered. The question states that the total cost of the robot’s acquisition 'will be'
$150,000. Therefore, the investment in the robot's acquisition has yet to be incurred and is
not considered a sunk cost.
- **B The opportunity cost is too high to continue with this project**
Incorrect. Opportunity cost is the value of the best alternative given up when a choice is
made. It is not known from the description provided by the question which alternative
investment options were considered when this project was selected. Therefore, there is no
way to determine if there was a more attractive investment opportunity.
- **C The robot will pay for itself within three years**
Incorrect. With a cost savings of $40,000 annually, the company will only have recouped
$120,000 of the original $150,000 investment after three years.
- **D The payback period is 45 months**
Correct. The question states that an investment of $150,000 will be required and will have
a cost savings of $40,000 annually. To calculate the payback period the $150,000
investment is divided by the cost savings of $40,000 annually which is 3.75 years or 45
months.

**Reference:**

- **A Guide to the Project Management Body of Knowledge, (PMBOK® Guide) – Sixth Edition,**
Project Management Institute Inc., 2017, Page(s) 34-35

PMP Exam 4
Filtered Mode: Displaying 200 questions
Question 89 of 200
Question ID: 612071
The sponsor has signed the project charter, and you have been assigned to manage the project.
Several employees have already been selected for the project team, and you have not worked
with any of them on previous projects.
Which of the following will help build relationships between the team members?
AError! Not a valid embedded object.Creating an issue log
BError! Not a valid embedded object.Colocation
CError! Not a valid embedded object.Team performance assessments
DError! Not a valid embedded object.Observation and conversation
Question answered incorrectly

**Hint:**

Which of the choices is a tool for the Develop Team process?
Correct Answer: B

**Explanation:**

Building relationships between the team members is an important part of team development, and
a cohesive team will enhance the project's performance. Many of your team members have been
pre-assigned enabling you to begin team building early in the project. Placing the team in the
same room, hence colocating, allows the team to build relationships with each other and develop
a sense of community. While colocation is not always feasible, of the choices provided, it is the
best answer to the question asked.

**Details for Each Option:**


---

AError! Not a valid embedded object.Creating an issue log
Incorrect. Issue logs are used to communicate issues on a project as well as who is
responsible for resolving them and in what time frame. Issue logs help project managers
effectively track and manage issues rather than assist with team building.
BError! Not a valid embedded object.Colocation
Correct. Colocation involves placing team members together in the same the same room.
Having a team colocated can help them develop a sense of community and improve their
communication, in turn, assist with team building. While colocation is not always feasible,
of the choices provided, it is the best answer to the question asked.
CError! Not a valid embedded object.Team performance assessments
Incorrect. Team performance assessments evaluate the team's effectiveness so that actions
can be taken to address any issues that may be affecting the team's efficacy. The project
manager may determine more team building is required as a result of an assessment of the
team, but the team performance assessments are not a team building activity.
DError! Not a valid embedded object.Observation and conversation
Incorrect. By observing the work and the project team, the project manager can proactively
speak to team members about issues that might be developing. Observation and
conversation are tools used to manage the team rather than develop the team.

- **A Guide to the Project Management Body of Knowledge, (PMBOK® Guide) – Sixth Edition,**
Project Management Institute Inc., 2017, Page(s) 340

PMP Exam 4
Filtered Mode: Displaying 200 questions
Question 90 of 200
Question ID: 613788
- **A project manager is in the process of selecting vendors for her project. She wants to ensure that**
individual vendors do not receive preferential treatment and that everyone has a clear and shared
understanding of the procurement.
What tool or technique will best address the project manager's need?
AError! Not a valid embedded object.Advertising
BError! Not a valid embedded object.Prequalified seller lists
CError! Not a valid embedded object.Pre-bid conferences
DError! Not a valid embedded object.Procurement management plan
Question answered incorrectly

**Hint:**

What type of meeting is conducted between the buyer and prospective sellers?
Correct Answer: C

**Explanation:**

Selecting vendors for a project implies the project manager is in the Conduct Procurements
process. Bidder conferences are one of the tools and techniques of this process. Bidder
conferences are also known as contractor conferences, vendor conferences, and pre-bid
conferences, are meetings between the buyer and prospective sellers prior to proposal submittal.
They are used to ensure that all prospective bidders have a clear and common understanding of
the procurement, and no bidders receive preferential treatment.

**Details for Each Option:**


---

AError! Not a valid embedded object.Advertising
Incorrect. Advertising can be used to expand the list of potential sellers and may be
required for pending government contracts. Although advertising may provide equal
treatment of prospective bidders in the notification of a pending contract, it is not the best
method of ensuring a clear and shared understanding of the procurement.
BError! Not a valid embedded object.Prequalified seller lists
Incorrect. Prequalified seller lists are lists of potential sellers who are previously
approved. A prequalified seller list is not intended to and will not facilitate a clear and
shared understanding of the procurement by the prospective bidders.
CError! Not a valid embedded object.Pre-bid conferences
Bidder conferences (also known as pre-bid conferences) are meetings between the buyer
and prospective vendors/sellers prior to proposal submittal. These meetings are used to
ensure that all prospective vendors/bidders have a clear and common understanding of the
procurement and nobody receives preferential treatment.
DError! Not a valid embedded object.Procurement management plan
Incorrect. The procurement management plan is a component of the project management
plan and not a tool or technique.

**Reference:**

- **A Guide to the Project Management Body of Knowledge, (PMBOK® Guide) – Sixth Edition,**
Project Management Institute Inc., 2017, Page(s) 487

PMP Exam 4
Filtered Mode: Displaying 200 questions
Question 91 of 200
Question ID: 612764
- **A project manager has written a charter but has been unable to get the charter approved by senior**
management. His manager has asked him to begin the project without the charter.
What is the best thing for the project manager to do?
AError! Not a valid embedded object.Proceed with the project, but document the lack of project
charter in the risk register
BError! Not a valid embedded object.Focus on other projects that have project charters
CError! Not a valid embedded object.Start working on the project management plan
DError! Not a valid embedded object.Refuse to proceed with the project
Question answered incorrectly

**Hint:**

The project charter formally initiates the project.
Correct Answer: D

**Explanation:**

The primary purpose of the charter is to formally authorize the project and, most importantly, to
provide the project manager with the authority to apply organizational resources to project
activities. Without an approved charter the scope and nature of the project may not be clearly
defined, or the project could progress in a direction that is not in alignment with the
organization's objectives. The act of creating an approved charter shows management support for
the project and the project manager. If the project starts without the project charter, the project
may suffer from the lack of resources throughout its entire life cycle. The lack of resources is
likely to lead to project failure which will likely be perceived as the project manager's fault. A
better answer choice would be “refuse to proceed with the project and explain the impact of
proceeding without an approved charter.” However, this option is not given. Therefore, of those
provided, refusing to begin the project is the best answer to the question asked.

---


**Details for Each Option:**

AError! Not a valid embedded object.Proceed with the project, but document the lack of
project charter in the risk register
Incorrect. Beginning the project without a charter can lead to later issues since the primary
purpose of the charter is to formally authorize the project and most importantly, to provide
the project manager with the authority to apply organizational resources to project
activities. Documenting the lack of the project charter in the risk register will not resolve
the central issue described in the scenario. Therefore, starting the project without a charter
is not the best answer.
BError! Not a valid embedded object.Focus on other projects that have project charters
Incorrect. This response is an avoidance tactic, which is typically not an advisable way to
handle problems, especially when the chances of project success are at stake.
CError! Not a valid embedded object.Start working on the project management plan
Incorrect. The project manager and the project team use the project charter as a starting
point for initial project planning; therefore, the project charter is an input to the Develop
Project Management Plan process. Since the charter is not approved, the project manager
doesn't know if the information he included in the charter was accurate. It would be
counterproductive to start the development of the project management plan with
information that may be incorrect or incomplete. Additionally, beginning the development
of the project management plan would constitute starting the project, which is not formally
authorized without the approved project charter.
DError! Not a valid embedded object.Refuse to proceed with the project
Correct. While refusing to proceed the project may sound like an extreme action that could
even cost the project manager his job, it is the project manager’s professional
responsibility to accept only those assignments that can be reasonably completed. If the
project starts without the project charter, the project may suffer from the lack of resources
throughout its entire life cycle leading to project failure which would most likely be
considered the project manager’s fault. Therefore, it is better for the project manager to
fight now for the project charter rather than start the project knowing it has low chances of
success.

**Reference:**

- **A Guide to the Project Management Body of Knowledge, (PMBOK® Guide) – Sixth Edition,**
Project Management Institute Inc., 2017, Page(s) 75-77, 81; see also The PMI Code of Ethics

---

and Professional Conduct, Responsibility

PMP Exam 4
Filtered Mode: Displaying 200 questions
Question 92 of 200
Question ID: 610088
- **A team building a radio tower has determined that the current transmitter only has a 75-mile**
range and requests that a more powerful transmitter be purchased to achieve the 100-mile range
that is required. There is considerable pressure from stakeholders to maintain the current
schedule, and the project manager knows that going through the formal, lengthy change control
process would cause significant schedule delays.
What should the project manager do next?
AError! Not a valid embedded object.Purchase the required transmitter
BError! Not a valid embedded object.Submit a change request
CError! Not a valid embedded object.Re-do the equipment test
DError! Not a valid embedded object.Crash the project schedule
Question answered incorrectly

**Hint:**

It is a formal proposal to modify a document, deliverable, or baseline.
Correct Answer: B

**Explanation:**

Monitoring project work is about collecting, measuring, and assessing project information with
respect to actual status, budget, and schedule. Control project work is about determining what, if
any, action is needed to correct or prevent any variance in the project plan. In this scenario, the
project manager has learned of a variance that will affect the project's ability to meet the
approved scope which in this case is the radio tower with a 75-mile range instead of the required
100-miles range. By submitting a change request, the project manager is ensuring that only
official changes are made to the scope and, when approved by the authorized body such as the
change control board, only these changes are implemented. Regardless of the pressure from
stakeholders to maintain the current schedule and the fact the formal change control process is
lengthy, the project manager should ensure changes are handled properly according to the

---

organization's change control process via a change request. Hence, of the choices offered,
submitting a change request is what the project manager should do next and is, therefore, the best
answer to the question asked.

**Details for Each Option:**

AError! Not a valid embedded object.Purchase the required transmitter
Incorrect. There is not enough information in the question to determine if the project
manager has the authority to approve and make this purchase.
BError! Not a valid embedded object.Submit a change request
Correct. Problems and obstacles on projects are normal. The project manager is already
doing the right thing by continuously monitoring project work at regular intervals. In this
instance, a variance based on measurement has occurred, and a corrective action to
replace the transmitter has been recommended. Therefore, of the choices provided,
submitting a change request to replace the transmitter is what the project manager should
do next.
CError! Not a valid embedded object.Re-do the equipment test
Incorrect. While re-doing the equipment test may be a good idea to confirm or invalidate
the test results before making such seemingly an expensive purchase, it should be assumed
that the tests were properly conducted and the results are valid. Additionally, the question
indicates that the engineering team has already confirmed the test results, making this
answer choice a redundant and unnecessary action.
DError! Not a valid embedded object.Crash the project schedule
Incorrect. Crashing is a schedule compression technique used to shorten the schedule
duration for the least incremental cost by adding resources. Crashing the schedule would
not address the main problem described in the scenario which is the lower than specified
transmitter's range.

**Reference:**

- **A Guide to the Project Management Body of Knowledge, (PMBOK® Guide) – Sixth Edition,**
Project Management Institute Inc., 2017, Page(s) 96-97, 107, 112

PMP Exam 4
Filtered Mode: Displaying 200 questions
Question 94 of 200
Question ID: 612724
You are assigned to a software development project. The product requirements are not clearly
defined upfront. Therefore, it has been decided to develop the product using an agile framework.
Other aspects of the project will be managed using the traditional waterfall project management
approach.
Which of the following might you spend less time developing and/or implementing for this
project?
AError! Not a valid embedded object.The project charter
BError! Not a valid embedded object.The issue log
CError! Not a valid embedded object.The change management plan
DError! Not a valid embedded object.The Validate Scope process
Question answered incorrectly

**Hint:**

What is the fundamental difference between how projects are executed with an agile framework
with vague requirements versus a traditional waterfall approach with requirements defined
upfront?
Correct Answer: C

**Explanation:**

The process of change management is fundamentally different in projects where requirements
are not defined upfront warranting the use of agile methodologies to develop the product. With a
waterfall approach, the requirements are typically defined upfront and, therefore, scope changes
are discouraged. For such projects, a rigorous change management process is in place to ensure
that change is minimized, and only the most important changes are incorporated into the project.
Agile takes a different approach to change management. To provide the best value for the client,
in projects where deliverables are produced using agile practices, change is anticipated and
welcomed. Instead of relying on a formal process for managing change, the product owner,

---

which is a role responsible for managing customer requirements (backlog items), is much more
involved in the planning of each iteration by providing a prioritized backlog of features for the
development team to produce. A change management plan, if it is used at all, will be of little
value for an agile project compared with a project using a traditional waterfall approach. The
scenario presents a hybrid project where most of the project aspects are managed using the
traditional project management approach, while the development of the product is carried out
using agile. Agile has been selected because the requirements were not defined upfront.
Therefore, of the available choices, the project team will likely spend less time developing and/or
implementing the change management plan so that the frequent changes required by the
customer will be easier accommodated.

**Details for Each Option:**

AError! Not a valid embedded object.The project charter
Incorrect. The project charter is a document issued by the project initiator or sponsor that
formally authorizes the existence of a project and provides the project manager with the
authority to apply organizational resources to project activities. The complexity of the
project charter (and thus the time spent in development) is more closely related to the size
and importance of the project rather than the methodology that will be used. The project
charter is not fundamentally different in an agile project compared to a hybrid or
traditional waterfall project.
BError! Not a valid embedded object.The issue log
Incorrect. The issue log is a project document where information about issues is recorded
and monitored. Issues will occur on projects regardless of the methodology that is being
used. It is equally important for issues to be addressed on agile projects as it is for projects
using a hybrid or waterfall approach. Therefore, there is not likely to be a significant
difference in the time spent developing and implementing the issue log.
CError! Not a valid embedded object.The change management plan
Correct. The change management plan is the component of the project management plan
that establishes the change control board, documents the extent of its authority, and
describes how the change control system will be implemented. Projects in which
deliverables are build using agile practices do not typically use a change control board or
have formal procedures for processing change requests. Changes are made at the
discretion of the product owner rather than being controlled through a formal change
management process.
DError! Not a valid embedded object.The Validate Scope process
Incorrect. The Validate Scope process is the process of formalizing acceptance of the

---

completed project deliverables. The process of gaining acceptance for deliverables is
considerably different for pure agile projects compared with those using a waterfall
approach. Agile projects hold an iteration (sprint) review at the end of each iteration
(sprint) to demonstrate the increment of the product that was developed during the iteration
(sprint) and gain the approval of the product owner. A waterfall approach may only seek
the acceptance of deliverables at the end of the project when the product of the project is
complete. Therefore, a project team is more likely to spend more, not less, time performing
the Validate Scope process in an agile project compared with a waterfall approach.

**Reference:**

- **A Guide to the Project Management Body of Knowledge, (PMBOK® Guide) – Sixth Edition,**
Project Management Institute Inc., 2017, Page(s) 131-133; see also
https://www.projectmanagement.com/articles/355615/Scope-Changes-Within-the-Agile-Scrum-
Framework

Question 95 of 200
Question ID: 614009
Following is an illustration of a project network activity node that includes some information
about activity B.
Assuming that work starts on day one (not day zero) and given the information provided, what is
the late finish of activity B?
AError! Not a valid embedded object.40
BError! Not a valid embedded object.39
CError! Not a valid embedded object.37
DError! Not a valid embedded object.38
Question answered incorrectly

**Hint:**

Since the early finish date and total float are provided, you could use the relevant total float
formula.

---

Correct Answer: B

**Explanation:**

To answer this question and compute the late finish, the first step is to understand the meaning of
the values displayed on the network activity node. The accepted convention is shown below,
where:
• ES = early start
• EF = early finish
• LS = late start
• LF = late finish
The next step is to select a formula that can be rearranged to calculate the late finish.
Total Float = LF - EF
LF = Total Float + EF = 16 + 23 = 39
Another way to calculate the LF is by simply using the given duration of the task:
LF = LS + Duration - 1 = 37 + 3 - 1 = 39
The subtruction of 1 accounts for the approach of work that starts on day 1 (not 0)

---


**Details for Each Option:**

AError! Not a valid embedded object.40
Incorrect. You might have chosen this answer if you did not account for the convention of
starting work on day one, where the forward pass and backward pass formulas either add
one or subtract one.
BError! Not a valid embedded object.39
Correct. You can use the values provided for both EF and Total Float in the formula Total
Float = LF - EF to rearrange solve for LF.
CError! Not a valid embedded object.37
Incorrect. This answer choice represents the late start value.
DError! Not a valid embedded object.38
Incorrect. You may have chosen this answer if you incorrectly remembered the formula,
subtracting one instead of adding one to account for starting work on day one.

---


**Reference:**

- **A Guide to the Project Management Body of Knowledge, (PMBOK® Guide) – Sixth Edition,**
Project Management Institute Inc., 2017, Page(s) 210-211; see also PMI® Practice Standard for
Scheduling – Second Edition
Live FeedbackTM Back to Results

PMP Exam 4
Filtered Mode: Displaying 200 questions
Question 96 of 200
Question ID: 612619
During execution of an agile project, a key stakeholder has been regularly contacting the
development team offering suggestions. While the stakeholder's support is vital to the success of
the project, the suggestions have not been particularly helpful and are distracting to the
development team.
What would be the best approach for the project manager to address the issue with the key
stakeholder?
AError! Not a valid embedded object.Invite the stakeholder to attend the regularly scheduled sprint
planning meetings instead of contacting the development team directly
BError! Not a valid embedded object.Explain your concerns to the stakeholder and politely ask the
stakeholder to discontinue all contact with the project team
CError! Not a valid embedded object.Update the stakeholder engagement assessment matrix to reflect
the stakeholder's current level of engagement
DError! Not a valid embedded object.Capture the issue in the issue log and submit a change request to
update the communication management plan
Question answered incorrectly

**Hint:**

What tool or technique associated with the Manage Stakeholder Engagement process would be
most helpful in addressing the issue described by the question?
Correct Answer: A

**Explanation:**

Meetings are one of the tools and techniques that a project manager can use to manage
stakeholder engagement. Inviting the stakeholder to attend the sprint planning meeting rather
than contacting the development team directly provides a resolution which will likely help
ensure the continued support of the stakeholder while removing the distraction from the project
team. Sprint planning is a meeting typically used in agile projects where the determination of

---

what will be delivered in the upcoming sprint is made and how the work needed to deliver
product increment will be achieved. Of the choices provided, the sprint planning meeting is the
best place where the project team and the relevant stakeholders can get together and discuss any
items related to the upcoming sprint. Suggestions from the stakeholders, such as those described
in the scenario, can be best addressed at the sprint planning meeting, making this choice the best
answer to the question asked.

**Details for Each Option:**

AError! Not a valid embedded object.Invite the stakeholder to attend the regularly scheduled
sprint planning meetings instead of contacting the development team directly
Correct. Meetings are one of the tools and techniques that a project manager can use to
manage stakeholder engagement. Inviting the stakeholder to attend the sprint planning
meeting rather than contacting the development team directly provides a potential
resolution which may help ensure the continued support of the stakeholder while removing
the distraction from the project team, thus making this choice the best answer to the
question asked.
BError! Not a valid embedded object.Explain your concerns to the stakeholder and politely
ask the stakeholder to discontinue all contact with the project team
Incorrect. While the action represented by this answer choice will likely resolve the
distraction issue for the project team, it is likely to create friction with the key stakeholder.
The question states that stakeholder's support is vital to the success of the project. It is
better to negotiate with the stakeholder to find a more productive way for the stakeholder to
be engaged with the project rather than asking the stakeholder to discontinue 'all' contact
with the project team, no matter how politely this has been requested.
CError! Not a valid embedded object.Update the stakeholder engagement assessment matrix
to reflect the stakeholder's current level of engagement
Incorrect. The stakeholder engagement assessment matrix is a matrix that compares
current and desired stakeholder engagement levels. While the stakeholder engagement
assessment matrix should be updated to reflect any changes in stakeholder engagement
levels, this action will do nothing to address the issue presented in the scenario.
DError! Not a valid embedded object.Capture the issue in the issue log and submit a change
request to update the communication management plan
Incorrect. The issue described by the question should be captured in the issue log.
However, the question is asking for the best approach to address the issue with the key
stakeholder. Capturing the information in the issue log will not, by itself, address the issue.
If the question had asked what the project manager should do 'first', then this choice could

---

have been a plausible option. Updating the communication management plan is a
premature action as it is not clear yet what (if at all) should be updated.

**Reference:**

- **A Guide to the Project Management Body of Knowledge, (PMBOK® Guide) – Sixth Edition,**
Project Management Institute Inc., 2017, Page(s) 528

PMP Exam 4
Filtered Mode: Displaying 200 questions
Question 97 of 200
Question ID: 613665
- **A development project is behind schedule, and the project manager finds a way to bring the**
schedule back into alignment with the plan. The testing of the software code is scheduled to start
one week after the coding is complete, so the project manager adjusts the timeline to have the
software testing begin immediately after the coding is complete.
What tool or technique has the project manager used to get the schedule back on track?
AError! Not a valid embedded object.Crashing
BError! Not a valid embedded object.Fast tracking
CError! Not a valid embedded object.Leads and lags
DError! Not a valid embedded object.Earned value management
Question answered incorrectly

**Hint:**

What technique is exemplified by reducing or eliminating the time between the finish of one
activity and the start of the subsequent activity?
Correct Answer: C

**Explanation:**

The question implies that the project team is performing the Control Schedule process. One of
the tools and techniques that may be used during the Control Schedule process is the adjustment
of leads and lags. Adjusting leads and lags can bring project activities that are behind into
alignment with the plan. The question describes a scenario in which the lag time between the
completion of the software code and the start of the testing has been eliminated. In this case, the
elimination of the lag time is the technique that brings the schedule back into alignment with the
plan.

---


**Details for Each Option:**

AError! Not a valid embedded object.Crashing
Incorrect. Crashing is a schedule compression technique which adds resources to an
activity on the critical path to shorten the duration. There is no indication from the
question that any resources are being added to address the schedule issue.
BError! Not a valid embedded object.Fast tracking
Incorrect. Fast tracking is a schedule compression technique in which activities normally
done in sequence are performed in parallel for at least a portion of their duration. In this
situation, the writing of the software code and the testing are scheduled sequentially.
However, the lag time is being eliminated rather than running the activities in parallel.
CError! Not a valid embedded object.Leads and lags
Correct. Adjusting leads and lags is a technique which can be used to bring project
activities that are behind into alignment with the plan. The question describes a situation in
which the lag time between the completion of the software code and the start of the testing
has been eliminated.
DError! Not a valid embedded object.Earned value management
Incorrect. The question implies that an earned value analysis has been performed. It was
the elimination of lag time that addressed the problem with the schedule.

**Reference:**

- **A Guide to the Project Management Body of Knowledge, (PMBOK® Guide) – Sixth Edition,**
Project Management Institute Inc., 2017, Page(s) 228

PMP Exam 4
Filtered Mode: Displaying 200 questions
Question 98 of 200
Question ID: 613655
- **A project manager is estimating the length of time the project will take. The project manager**
worked on a comparable project two years ago that installed 10 miles of guardrails at a rate of
one mile a day in similar weather conditions, using the same size crew on the same type of
highway.
What estimating technique would be the appropriate option for the project manager to use for his
duration estimate?
AError! Not a valid embedded object.Parametric estimating
BError! Not a valid embedded object.Analogous estimating
CError! Not a valid embedded object.Bottom-up estimating
DError! Not a valid embedded object.Three-point estimating
Question answered incorrectly

**Hint:**

What technique uses variables (e.g., units of output) to calculate estimates?
Correct Answer: A

**Explanation:**

Since the project manager has duration data from a similar project with definitive parameters, he
can extrapolate the rate of producing the guardrails from the previous project to arrive at an
estimate for the new project. This estimation technique is called parametric estimating.
Parametric estimating can be used during the Estimate Activity Durations process, which is what
is described in the question scenario. For example, since the previous project was able to install
one mile of guardrail over 10 days, he could estimate that five miles of guardrail will take 50
days to install.

---


**Details for Each Option:**

AError! Not a valid embedded object.Parametric estimating
Correct. Parametric estimating uses an algorithm to calculate duration based on historical
data and project parameters. Since the project manager has the duration parameters from
previous projects, he can use them to calculate a duration estimate for this project.
Parametric estimating can provide high levels of accuracy depending on the complexity of
the variables.
BError! Not a valid embedded object.Analogous estimating
Incorrect. A good option, but parametric estimating is a better choice because the project
manager has comparable parameters to more accurately calculate the estimate. Analogous
estimating is a gross-level estimating technique which relies on the actual duration of
previous, similar projects. Also, analogous estimating is generally less accurate than other
estimating techniques.
CError! Not a valid embedded object.Bottom-up estimating
Incorrect. Bottom-up estimating is a method of estimating duration by aggregating the
estimates of the lower level components of the work breakdown structure. Bottom-up
estimating is typically used when estimates cannot be made with a high degree of
confidence. Since the project manager has duration data from a similar project with
definitive parameters that allow him to provide estimates with a high degree of confidence,
bottom-up estimating is not the best answer in this scenario.
DError! Not a valid embedded object.Three-point estimating
Incorrect. Three-point estimating helps determine an estimated range using most likely,
optimistic and pessimistic values. This method is usually used when there is insufficient
historical data or when using judgmental data. Parametric estimating is a better choice
because the project manager does have definitive parameters that allow him to provide an
estimate with a high degree of confidence.

**Reference:**

- **A Guide to the Project Management Body of Knowledge, (PMBOK® Guide) – Sixth Edition,**
Project Management Institute Inc., 2017, Page(s) 200
Live FeedbackTM Back to Results
Prev Next

---

PMP Exam 4
Filtered Mode: Displaying 200 questions
Question 99 of 200
Question ID: 612134
- **A project team will work in a noisy environment requiring hearing protection. To communicate**
in this type of environment, your employer has a mandatory proprietary instant messaging
mobile phone application that will be installed on the phone of every project team member for
the duration of the project.
This application is an example of which of the following?
AError! Not a valid embedded object.Pull communication
BError! Not a valid embedded object.Push communication
CError! Not a valid embedded object.Enterprise environmental factors
DError! Not a valid embedded object.Communication model
Question answered incorrectly

**Hint:**

The instant messaging application is a mandatory communication tool.
Correct Answer: C

**Explanation:**

The scenario describes the use of a proprietary instant messaging application that, according to
your organization, is a mandatory tool to be used for communications under certain
circumstances, for example when the employees perform project work in a noisy remote
environment. While the use of the instant messaging application on the mobile phones may lead
you to think the question is talking about communication technology, communication models, or
communication methods, the word ‘mandatory’ should trigger the thought of enterprise
environmental factors. Any condition, not under the immediate control of the team that
influences, constraints, or directs the project is an enterprise environmental factor (EEF).
Established communication channels, tools, and systems are an example of the EEF. Since the
instant messaging application is defined as ‘mandatory’ by your organization, meaning it is
outside the project team's control, the application qualifies as an EEF, in particular as an

---

established communication tool. Therefore, of the choices provided, enterprise environmental
factors is the best answer to the question asked. Please read the questions carefully to choose the
best answer. It is easy to miss one word which might be the keyword in selecting the correct
answer.

**Details for Each Option:**

AError! Not a valid embedded object.Pull communication
Incorrect. Pull communication is a type of communication method that requires recipients
to access content at their discretion. This method is typically used for large audiences or
complex data sets. The instant messaging application described in the scenario does not
represent a pull communication method.
BError! Not a valid embedded object.Push communication
Incorrect. Push communication is a type of communication method where information is
distributed to specific recipients. This method ensures the information is sent but does not
guarantee the information was received or understood by the recipient. The instant
messaging application described in the scenario provides an exchange of information in
real time allowing prompt feedback and is, therefore, not a type of push communication.
CError! Not a valid embedded object.Enterprise environmental factors
Correct. The scenario implies you are carrying out the Plan Communications Management
process. Enterprise environmental factors are an input to that process. Enterprise
environmental factors are conditions, not under the immediate control of the team, that
influence, constrain, or direct the project. The scenario describes an instant messaging
application that is mandated by your organization to be used for communication.
‘Mandatory’ means the application is not under the immediate control of the team, making
the application an enterprise environmental factor.
DError! Not a valid embedded object.Communication model
Incorrect. Communication models represent the communication process in general, rather
than a specific communication application described in the scenario.

**Reference:**

- **A Guide to the Project Management Body of Knowledge, (PMBOK® Guide) – Sixth Edition,**
Project Management Institute Inc., 2017, Page(s) 368, 370
Live FeedbackTM Back to Results
