PMP Exam 4
Filtered Mode: Displaying 200 questions
Question 123 of 200
Question ID: 613787
During the vendor selection process, a start-up company has submitted a bid with a significantly
lower price than the well-established vendor that you have always used in the past.
If you decide to award the contract to the start-up company, which project document is the most
likely to be updated?
AError! Not a valid embedded object.Risk register
BError! Not a valid embedded object.Source selection criteria
CError! Not a valid embedded object.Prequalified seller list
DError! Not a valid embedded object.Procurement statement of work
Question answered incorrectly

**Hint:**

Which project document should be updated when an unproven vendor is selected for a project?
Correct Answer: A

**Explanation:**

The question indicates that a new vendor is being considered with whom the company has no
prior experience. If this vendor is selected, an additional risk will be introduced into the project
since the performance of the vendor has yet to be established. Each approved seller comes with
its own unique set of risks. Changes are made to the risk register during the contracting process,
which reflects the specific risks of each seller. Based on the risk of contracting with an unproven
supplier, the risk register should be updated to account for this added risk. Of the available
options, the risk register is the most likely project document to be updated if you decide to award
the contract to the start-up company.

---


**Details for Each Option:**

AError! Not a valid embedded object.Risk register
Correct. Each approved seller comes with its own unique set of risks. Changes are made to
the risk register during the contracting process, which reflects the specific risks of each
seller.
BError! Not a valid embedded object.Source selection criteria
Incorrect. The source selection criteria describe how bidder proposals will be evaluated,
including evaluation criteria and weights. The source selection criteria are determined
before the bidding process and are not likely to change based on vendor selection.
CError! Not a valid embedded object.Prequalified seller list
Incorrect. Once the project is complete, the vendor, depending on their performance on the
project, may or may not be added to the prequalified seller list. However, the prequalified
seller list is an organizational process asset and not a project document as asked by the
question.
DError! Not a valid embedded object.Procurement statement of work
Incorrect. The procurement statement of work provides sellers with a clearly stated set of
goals, requirements, and outcomes from which they can provide a quantifiable response.
The procurement statement of work is developed before the bidding process takes place and
is unlikely to be updated when a vendor is selected.

**Reference:**

- **A Guide to the Project Management Body of Knowledge, (PMBOK® Guide) – Sixth Edition,**
Project Management Institute Inc., 2017, Page(s) 485

PMP Exam 4
Filtered Mode: Displaying 200 questions
Question 124 of 200
Question ID: 625083
- **A project manager has rejected a defective lot of A-frames. The contract with the vendor states**
that payment must be made upon delivery and does not explicitly contain a clause dictating
whether payments should be released or held back in such instances. However, the project
manager firmly believes that if she does not hold back the payment for the shipment of this
particular lot, the vendor will not take timely corrective actions for further shipments.
What should the project manager do?
AError! Not a valid embedded object.Hold back the payment
BError! Not a valid embedded object.Release the payment
CError! Not a valid embedded object.Terminate the contract
DError! Not a valid embedded object.Release a partial payment
Question answered incorrectly

**Hint:**

According to the PMI Code of Ethics and Professional Conduct, what must Jill do in this
scenario?
Correct Answer: B

**Explanation:**

The contract between the vendor and the project manager's company is a mutually binding
agreement representing a legal relationship between them and obligating the vendor to provide
the A-frames and the company to compensate the vendor for the deliverables. In the absence of a
clause addressing the withholding of payments for the poor quality, the project manager has an
ethical responsibility to release the payment to the vendor as provided by the contract. When
errors or omissions are discovered either due to the project manager's fault or at the fault of
someone else, the project manager must either accept the responsibility of their own mistakes or
report the issue to the appropriate authority if the error resulted from someone else.

---

It would be wise to amend the contract to include a clause that allows payment to be held back in
such instances and enact a penalty clause that requires the vendor to compensate the buyer for
delays caused by the vendor. While it is rare that a contract is written without such a clause, this
question is included to provide a situation that 'feels' like the buyer should have a right to
withhold payment. However, procurement contracts must be honored as they are written, and the
values outlined in the PMI Code of Ethics and Professional Conduct should be upheld.

**Details for Each Option:**

AError! Not a valid embedded object.Hold back the payment
Incorrect. The contract is a mutually binding agreement that obligates the vendor to
provide the A-frames and the project manager's company to compensate the vendor. Since
the contract does not contain any clauses addressing withholding of payment for poor
quality, the project manager has an ethical and contractual responsibility to make the
payment and find other ways to get the corrective actions on the A-frames.
BError! Not a valid embedded object.Release the payment
Correct. The contract with the vendor is a mutually binding agreement that requires the
vendor to provide the A-frames and the company to compensate the vendor. The contract
does not account for poor quality, so the project manager has the responsibility to fulfill
the terms and conditions of the agreement and release the payment.
CError! Not a valid embedded object.Terminate the contract
Incorrect. The contract with the vendor obligates the company to compensate the vendor
for the A-frames in light of the fact a clause addressing the poor quality does not exist.
Terminating the contract is a premature action and could prevent the project manager from
ever receiving the correct deliverables she needs. Therefore, terminating the contract is not
the best answer.
DError! Not a valid embedded object.Release a partial payment
Incorrect. The contract obligates the company to compensate the vendor for the delivered
product. Without a clause addressing poor quality, releasing a partial payment has the
same effect as withholding payment and is not an acceptable solution to this problem.

**Reference:**

- **A Guide to the Project Management Body of Knowledge, (PMBOK® Guide) – Sixth Edition,**
Project Management Institute Inc., 2017, Page(s) 492-494, 489; see also PMI Code of Ethics
and Professional Conduct, Responsibility

---

PMP Exam 4
Filtered Mode: Displaying 200 questions
Question 125 of 200
Question ID: 612610
You are the project manager for a consulting firm. After obtaining formal acceptance and
receiving final payment, you are preparing the final project report. The report includes an
assessment of whether the results achieved the benefits that the project was undertaken to
address. You have already collected the performance results, and you now need to gain a better
understanding of the intended project benefits.
What should you do next to accomplish this objective?
AError! Not a valid embedded object.Look at the agreements with the client
BError! Not a valid embedded object.Check the business documents
CError! Not a valid embedded object.Survey relevant project stakeholders
DError! Not a valid embedded object.Review the procurement management plan
Question answered incorrectly

**Hint:**

Where would you find the benefits management plan?
Correct Answer: B

**Explanation:**

The question implies that the Close Project or Phase process is underway. All of the answer
choices may provide information that will be useful in this process. However, the question is
specifically asking for a source of information for the intended project benefits. Business
documents, such as the business case and the benefits management plan are among the inputs to
the Close Project or Phase process. The benefits management plan outlines the target benefits of
the project and perfectly addresses the need expressed in the question. Since the benefits
management plan is not listed as an answer choice, the business documents become the best
answer to the question asked.
One may argue that a seller should not have access to the business documents of the buyer. This

---

is typically true. And the question does not suggest otherwise. The thing is that both the buyer
and the seller manage the engagement between them as a project. Therefore, both would have
had created business documents. The benefits of the project for the buyer would be documented
in the business documents of the buyer, and the benefits of the project for the seller would be
documented in the business documents of the seller.

**Details for Each Option:**

AError! Not a valid embedded object.Look at the agreements with the client
Incorrect. Looking at the agreements with the client might provide some useful information
on the intended benefits of the project. However, the question is taken from the perspective
of the organization that was contracted to perform the project work. Therefore, looking at
the agreements with the client is unlikely to provide ‘your’ organization with the
information about the target benefits of ‘your’ project. There is another document which
specifically documents the target benefits of the project which is a better answer to the
question asked.
BError! Not a valid embedded object.Check the business documents
Correct. The business documents include the business case and the benefits management
plan. The benefits management plan outlines the target benefits of the project, making this
choice the best answer to the question asked.
CError! Not a valid embedded object.Survey relevant project stakeholders
Incorrect. The project stakeholders may have some information on the intended benefits of
the project. However, the target benefits are documented in the benefits management plan
during pre-project work. It is best to use the target benefits that were established at the
start of the project. Stakeholder perceptions of what the project should have achieved can
become distorted by personal biases and agendas. Additionally, this action is not the best
use of time and available resources.
DError! Not a valid embedded object.Review the procurement management plan
Incorrect. The procurement management plan is a component of the project management
plan that describes how a project team will acquire goods and services from outside of the
performing organization. In this case, the question is taken from the perspective of the
organization that was procured to perform the project work. It is not known from the
question if some of the work was subcontracted out by the vendor. Regardless, even if there
is a procurement management plan with some relevant information, there is another
document which specifically captures the target benefits of the project which is a better
answer choice.

---


**Reference:**

- **A Guide to the Project Management Body of Knowledge, (PMBOK® Guide) – Sixth Edition,**
Project Management Institute Inc., 2017, Page(s) 125, 127-128
Live FeedbackTM Back to Results

Question 126 of 200
Question ID: 612962
You are facilitating a meeting with key stakeholders to discuss a new project that will be
conducted using an agile project management approach. One of the stakeholders is concerned
about how the project fits in with the company's overall organizational strategy.
What would you recommend to the stakeholder to address their concern?
AError! Not a valid embedded object.Look at the benefits management plan
BError! Not a valid embedded object.Review the assumption log
CError! Not a valid embedded object.Examine the work breakdown structure
DError! Not a valid embedded object.Ask the project sponsor
Question answered incorrectly

**Hint:**

What project document describes the processes for creating, maximizing, and sustaining the
benefits provided by a project?
Correct Answer: A

**Explanation:**

The project benefits management plan is the document that describes how and when the benefits
of the project will be delivered. It also describes the mechanisms that should be in place to
measure those benefits. For example, on projects conducted using an agile project management
approach, the benefits could be realized as the project progresses. This is possible because on
agile projects, the product is typically developed incrementally and is delivered with each
consecutive iteration, thus providing value to the customer and a revenue stream (realized
benefits) to the organization. A properly prepared benefits management plan describes the key
elements of the benefits, including how well the project benefits align with the business
strategies of the organization. Among the available choices, only the benefits management plan
specifically addresses the concern raised by the stakeholder.

---


**Details for Each Option:**

AError! Not a valid embedded object.Look at the benefits management plan
Correct. A properly prepared benefits management plan describes the key elements of the
benefits including how well the project benefits align with the business strategies of the
organization.
BError! Not a valid embedded object.Review the assumption log
Incorrect. The assumption log is a project document used to record all assumptions and
constraints throughout the project life cycle. The assumption log does not describe how the
project fits in with the company's overall organizational strategy.
CError! Not a valid embedded object.Examine the work breakdown structure
Incorrect. The work breakdown structure (WBS) is a hierarchical decomposition of the
total scope of work to be executed by the project. Since the project is still new, it may not
yet have a WBS. Even if a WBS were to exist, it would not describe how the project fits in
with the company's overall organizational strategy.
DError! Not a valid embedded object.Ask the project sponsor
Incorrect. The project sponsor is responsible for approving the project charter, securing
funding for the project, and supporting the project manager with issues beyond the project
manager's scope of authority. The project sponsor may have some information regarding
the project's alignment with organizational strategy, but there is a readily available
document which lists this information as a key element, which is a more appropriate
source.

**Reference:**

- **A Guide to the Project Management Body of Knowledge, (PMBOK® Guide) – Sixth Edition,**
Project Management Institute Inc., 2017, Page(s) 33

Question 127 of 200
Question ID: 612721
You have been working with the project initiator to develop a document that authorizes the
existence of the project you are about to manage. You have just obtained approval of the
document and want to ensure there is a common understanding by the stakeholders of the key
deliverables, milestones, and the roles and responsibilities of everyone involved in the project.
What should you do next?
AError! Not a valid embedded object.Obtain project charter approval from the project sponsor
BError! Not a valid embedded object.Facilitate a focus group with the stakeholders
CError! Not a valid embedded object.Share the approved project charter with the stakeholders
DError! Not a valid embedded object.Share the approved project management plan with the
stakeholders
Question answered incorrectly

**Hint:**

The project charter documents the high-level information on the project and on the product that
the project is intended to produce.
Correct Answer: C

**Explanation:**

The document described in the scenario that you have been working on with the project initiator
is the project charter. Chartering a project confirms the alignment of the project to the strategy
and ongoing work of the organization. High-level information on the project is documented in
the project charter. Therefore, if you want to ensure the stakeholders have a common
understanding of the deliverables, milestones, and roles and responsibilities of everyone involved
in the project, you should share the approved project charter with them.

---


**Details for Each Option:**

AError! Not a valid embedded object.Obtain project charter approval from the project sponsor
Incorrect. The document you have been working on with the project initiator is the project
charter. You have already secured an approved charter, as described in the scenario,
making this choice an incorrect answer.
BError! Not a valid embedded object.Facilitate a focus group with the stakeholders
Incorrect. The scenario implies you have been developing a project charter which then has
been approved by the project sponsor. Focus groups are an example of the data gathering
technique that can be used as a tool or technique during the Develop Project Charter
process to bring stakeholders together to learn about the project in a conversational way.
Since the project charter has already been approved, it can be assumed that the focus
groups have already been facilitated.
CError! Not a valid embedded object.Share the approved project charter with the stakeholders
Correct. The project charter documents high-level information on the project such as key
deliverables, summary milestone schedule, key stakeholder list, and project approval
requirements. Therefore, sharing the approved project charter with the stakeholders will
provide them with the information described in the scenario.
DError! Not a valid embedded object.Share the approved project management plan with the
stakeholders
Incorrect. The project management plan describes how the project will be executed,
monitored and controlled, and closed. While the project management plan will provide the
stakeholders with the information described in the scenario, it likely has not been
developed yet since you just received an approved charter.

PMP Exam 4
Filtered Mode: Displaying 200 questions
Question 128 of 200
Question ID: 650109
You are leading a software development project using agile methodologies. If the project is
successful, it will open up vast opportunities for future revenue and growth. The project has a
high risk of failure, but the potential benefits outweigh the risks. These risks and rewards must be
considered when selecting the content of each iteration.
Which features should be prioritized and developed first in this scenario?
AError! Not a valid embedded object.High-value and low-risk features
BError! Not a valid embedded object.Low-value and low-risk features
CError! Not a valid embedded object.High-value and high-risk features
DError! Not a valid embedded object.Low-value and high-risk features
Question answered incorrectly

**Hint:**

An important concept in agile is 'fast failure' which suggests that if a project is going to fail, it is
better to fail early in the project life cycle when fewer resources have been expended.
Correct Answer: C

**Explanation:**

In agile projects, a backlog is a list of features, or requirements, to be developed. The features are
first prioritized and then developed accordingly. When prioritizing a backlog, risks and value are
typically the primary considerations (aside from legal or other requirements). The backlog must
be prioritized and reprioritized throughout the project to determine what to include in each
iteration. High-value features should be prioritized first as not all features are likely to be
developed due to project constraints. Agile projects generate revenue by releasing product
increments to the market with the high-value features first while lower priority features are still
being developed.
Risks must also be considered when prioritizing the product backlog. High-risk features should

---

be prioritized over lower risk ones. When there is a risk of failure, as in this case, it is better to
fail earlier in the project rather than later when more project resources have been expended.
Additionally, the development of high-risk features is more likely to cause rework. Developing
high-risk features earlier may reduce the amount of rework required.
It is important to remember that a feature’s risk and value profile may change during the project
life cycle and will require monitoring for possible reprioritization.
Therefore, of the available choices, the high-value and high-risk features should be prioritized
and developed first in this scenario.

**Details for Each Option:**

AError! Not a valid embedded object.High-value and low-risk features
Incorrect. High-value and low-risk features should be prioritized after the high-value and
high-risk features. Although these features might provide as much value as the high-value
and high-risk features, they have less risk. High-risk features carry an inherent risk of
failure for the project and it is more cost effective to fail early rather than later in the
project.
BError! Not a valid embedded object.Low-value and low-risk features
Incorrect. Low-value features are prioritized after all high-value features. With agile
projects, it is likely that some features will not be developed given the project constraints. It
is best to give these features a lower priority because of the greater likelihood that they will
generate less revenue and, therefore, would not be included in the final product.
CError! Not a valid embedded object.High-value and high-risk features
Correct. High-value and high-risk features should be developed first. These features deliver
the most value to the project. Additionally, the high-risk features should be prioritized over
low-risk features because, among other reasons, high-risk features are far more likely to
cause the project to fail. If a project is going to fail, it is better to fail earlier in the project
when fewer resources have been expended.
DError! Not a valid embedded object.Low-value and high-risk features
Incorrect. Low-value and high-risk features should be avoided whenever possible. If there
is little value in a feature, it does not make sense to assume a substantial risk in developing
it.

**Reference:**


---

- **A Guide to the Project Management Body of Knowledge, (PMBOK® Guide) – Sixth Edition,**
Project Management Institute Inc., 2017, Page(s) 400
PMI-ACP Exam Prep 2nd edition by Mike Griffiths and Agile Estimating and Planning, Mike
Cohn, 2005, Risk Management.

PMP Exam 4
Filtered Mode: Displaying 200 questions
Question 129 of 200
Question ID: 612482
You recently received an email from a client, which states, "Thanks. We have received the goods
you just shipped." You begin to close out the project, send the final invoice to the client, and
release all of your staff. As you are preparing to leave for the day, you receive a voicemail from
the client stating that the deliverables do not meet the required specifications. This information
comes as a shock because you are sure the client has accepted the deliverables.
What should you do now?
AError! Not a valid embedded object.Call the client and tell them that they have accepted the
deliverables and should now pay the final invoice
BError! Not a valid embedded object.Call the client to understand why they think the deliverables do
not meet the required specifications
CError! Not a valid embedded object.Contact the legal department to check the contract and ask them
to suggest a course of action
DError! Not a valid embedded object.Ignore the voicemail from the client since their email indicates
that they have already accepted the deliverables
Question answered incorrectly

**Hint:**

What is required from the buyer before a procurement can be closed?
Correct Answer: B

**Explanation:**

Based on the scenario described, the client has not accepted the deliverables; they only
acknowledged receipt of the goods. Your actions of beginning the closing process of the project
are premature. Closed procurements are required to close the project. The procurement cannot be
closed until the buyer, your client, provides the seller, you, with formal written notice that the
contract has been completed. Therefore, since the client has not yet accepted the deliverables,
you should contact the client to understand why they believe the deliverables do not meet the

---

terms and conditions of the agreement.

**Details for Each Option:**

AError! Not a valid embedded object.Call the client and tell them that they have accepted the
deliverables and should now pay the final invoice
Incorrect. Your actions of starting the closing process of the project are premature. The
email states that the goods were received but does not indicate that the client has accepted
the deliverables. The verbiage contained in the email does not meet the criteria of formal
written notice that the contract has been completed.
BError! Not a valid embedded object.Call the client to understand why they think the
deliverables do not meet the required specifications
Correct. Based on the scenario, the client has not accepted the deliverables; the client has
only acknowledged receipt of the goods. The procurement should not be closed until your
client provides you with formal written notice that the contract has been completed. At this
point, all you have received is a notice of receipt of the deliverables. Therefore, you should
contact the client to understand why they think the deliverables do not meet the terms and
conditions of the agreement.
CError! Not a valid embedded object.Contact the legal department to check the contract and
ask them to suggest a course of action
Incorrect. Contacting the legal department is a premature action. First, you need to
understand what aspect of the deliverables, according to your client, does not meet the
terms and conditions as outlined in the contract.
DError! Not a valid embedded object.Ignore the voicemail from the client since their email
indicates that they have already accepted the deliverables
Incorrect. Your client never indicated that the deliverables met the contractual
requirements. Your client only acknowledged that they received the goods. Ignoring the
client is never a good idea.

**Reference:**

- **A Guide to the Project Management Body of Knowledge, (PMBOK® Guide) – Sixth Edition,**
Project Management Institute Inc., 2017, Page(s) 499

PMP Exam 4
Filtered Mode: Displaying 200 questions
Question 130 of 200
Question ID: 612065
- **A project manager was asked to prepare a document, which the project sponsor will sign to**
authorize a new software development project.
Which of the following will the project manager want to include in this document?
AError! Not a valid embedded object.A work breakdown structure (WBS)
BError! Not a valid embedded object.The key project deliverables
CError! Not a valid embedded object.A project schedule
DError! Not a valid embedded object.The project budget
Question answered incorrectly

**Hint:**

The project manager has been asked to create the project charter.
Correct Answer: B

**Explanation:**

The question suggests that the project manager has been asked to develop the project charter.
The project charter is a document issued by the project initiator or sponsor that formally
authorizes the existence of a project and provides the project manager with the authority to apply
organizational resources to project activities. The key deliverables for the project is an element,
which should be included as a component of the project charter. The incorrect answer choices
represent outputs of various processes of the Planning Process Group. The project charter is an
output of the Develop Project Charter process, which is part of the Initiating Process Group.
Therefore, of the available choices, the project manager should list the key project deliverables in
the project charter.

---


**Details for Each Option:**

AError! Not a valid embedded object.A work breakdown structure (WBS)
Incorrect. The work breakdown structure (WBS) is a hierarchical decomposition of the
total scope of work to be carried out by the project team to accomplish the project
objectives and create the required deliverables. The WBS is created as an output of the
Create WBS process, which occurs during project planning and not project initiation, as
suggested by the question.
BError! Not a valid embedded object.The key project deliverables
Correct. The question suggests that the project manager has been asked to develop the
project charter. The key deliverables for the project is an element, which should be
included as a component of the project charter.
CError! Not a valid embedded object.A project schedule
Incorrect. A summary milestone schedule might be included in the project charter.
However, the project schedule is not created until the Develop Schedule process is
performed during project planning.
DError! Not a valid embedded object.The project budget
Incorrect. The project budget is the cost baseline plus the management reserve. The project
budget is an output of the Determine Budget process, which is part of project planning. The
question suggests that the project charter is being developed, which occurs during project
initiation. Therefore, a project budget would not be available at this point in the project.

**Reference:**

- **A Guide to the Project Management Body of Knowledge, (PMBOK® Guide) – Sixth Edition,**
Project Management Institute Inc., 2017, Page(s) 81
Live FeedbackTM Back to Results

PMP Exam 4
Filtered Mode: Displaying 200 questions
Question 131 of 200
Question ID: 625010
In preparation for creating the change management plan for the project, the project manager
reviews the organizational process assets (OPAs).
Which of the following is the project manager least likely to use in this situation?
AError! Not a valid embedded object.A template for the project management plan
BError! Not a valid embedded object.Change control procedures
CError! Not a valid embedded object.Historical information from similar past projects
DError! Not a valid embedded object.The lessons learned register
Question answered incorrectly

**Hint:**

Which of the available responses does not represent an organizational process asset?
Correct Answer: D

**Explanation:**

The lessons learned register is a project document used to record knowledge gained during a
project so that it can be used in the current project. The lessons learned register would only have
information concerning the current project. The lessons learned register is not likely to have been
created at this stage of the project, and, even if it did exist, it is unlikely to contain any pertinent
information with the project still in the planning stage. The incorrect answer choices represent
examples of the OPAs used as inputs to the Develop Project Management Plan process implied
by the scenario where the change management plan is also developed. However, the question is
asking to find an item that is 'least' likely to be used in this scenario. The lessons learned register
is not an input to the Develop Project Management Plan process and, therefore, of the choices
given, would provide the least value in this situation.

---


**Details for Each Option:**

AError! Not a valid embedded object.A template for the project management plan
Incorrect. The change management plan is a component of the project management plan.
Therefore, a project management plan template should also contain a template for the
change management plan.
BError! Not a valid embedded object.Change control procedures
Incorrect. Change control procedures include the steps by which official organizational
standards, policies, plans, procedures, or any project documents will be modified and how
any changes will be approved and validated
CError! Not a valid embedded object.Historical information from similar past projects
Incorrect. Historical information from similar past projects should be archived in the
lessons learned repository. Understanding the effectiveness of the change management
process from past projects may yield useful information that can be incorporated into the
change management plan for the current project.
DError! Not a valid embedded object.The lessons learned register
Correct. The lessons learned register will only have information concerning the current
project, and with the project still in the planning stage, will have little, if any, pertinent
information.

**Reference:**

- **A Guide to the Project Management Body of Knowledge, (PMBOK® Guide) – Sixth Edition,**
Project Management Institute Inc., 2017, Page(s) 84, 88

PMP Exam 4
Filtered Mode: Displaying 200 questions
Question 132 of 200
Question ID: 614002
The following table contains information about the duration in days and predecessor activities on
a project schedule.
What is the duration of the critical path?
AError! Not a valid embedded object.6 days
BError! Not a valid embedded object.10 days

---

CError! Not a valid embedded object.17 days
DError! Not a valid embedded object.31 days
Question answered incorrectly

**Hint:**

Use the critical path method (CPM) to determine all network paths through the schedule, then
calculate the longest one.
Correct Answer: C

**Explanation:**

The critical path is the sequence of activities that represents the longest path on a project, which
also represents the shortest possible duration of a project. The first step to correctly answer this
question is to determine the critical path. This requires the creation of a project schedule network
diagram, where you map the values from the activity list table provided by the question.
Following is the network diagram for this question's scenario.
Once you have created the project schedule network diagram, you can determine the specific
paths that exist for the activities on the project. This requires following each path that is mapped
and calculating the length of each path based on the number of days for each activity in the path.
Following are the paths for this scenario.

---

Now that you know each of the project schedule network paths and their respective lengths,
determining the critical path is easy since you simply select the longest path. In this scenario, the
critical path is Start-D-E-F-G-Finish, and it has a length of 17 days.

**Details for Each Option:**

AError! Not a valid embedded object.6 days
Incorrect. You might choose this if you chose the shortest path, Start-H-I-Finish. But the
critical path is the longest in duration.
BError! Not a valid embedded object.10 days
Incorrect. You might choose this if you chose the middle of the three paths, Start-A-B-C-G-
Finish. But the critical path is the longest in duration.
CError! Not a valid embedded object.17 days
Correct. The critical path is the longest in duration, and after identifying all possible paths,
the longest path is Start-D-E-F-G-Finish, and its duration is 17 days.
DError! Not a valid embedded object.31 days
Incorrect. You might get this answer if you added up all the durations for all activities. But
you need to see all possible network paths through the sequence of activities, and that
requires using the critical path method.

**Reference:**


---

- **A Guide to the Project Management Body of Knowledge, (PMBOK® Guide) – Sixth Edition,**
Project Management Institute Inc., 2017, Page(s) 210-211; see also PMI® Practice Standard for
Scheduling – Second Edition

PMP Exam Simulator
PMP Exam 4
Filtered Mode: Displaying 200 questions
Question 133 of 200
Question ID: 613629
In the fourth week of a 10-month project, a new project manager takes over and notices that
earned value is consistently below planned value projections. The project manager is interested
to know if the indirect costs were included in the cost estimates but not accounted for in the
earned value assessment.
What project document would the project manager look at to determine how indirect costs are
dealt with in the project budget?
AError! Not a valid embedded object.Basis of estimates
BError! Not a valid embedded object.Cost forecasts
CError! Not a valid embedded object.Cost baseline
DError! Not a valid embedded object.Project funding requirements
Question answered incorrectly

**Hint:**

What output of the Estimate Costs process shows proof of and describes the logic behind how
the estimates are generated?
Correct Answer: A

**Explanation:**

Indirect costs are costs of doing business. They may benefit other projects as well, such as
executive salaries, office utility expenses, etc. Indirect costs may or may not be included in the
project budget. Each project is unique and, therefore, the decision to include/exclude indirect
costs in/from the project budget is made at the project level as part of its Estimate Costs process.
The decision is then documented in the basis of estimates document which is one of the outputs
of that process. Indirect costs may be included on an activity level or for the project as a whole.

---

To understand if the project manager's hunch is correct, he would need to look at the basis of
estimates to determine how indirect costs are handled across the project. Actual cost needs to
correspond in definition to what was budgeted in the planned value and measured in earned
value, for example, direct hours only, direct costs only, or all costs including indirect costs.

**Details for Each Option:**

AError! Not a valid embedded object.Basis of estimates
Correct. Supporting detail for cost estimates contained in the basis of estimates should
specify any basic assumptions dealing with the inclusion or exclusion of indirect or other
costs in the project budget.
BError! Not a valid embedded object.Cost forecasts
Incorrect. Cost forecasts are monetary values that represent either a calculated estimate at
completion (EAC) or a bottom-up EAC. Cost forecasts do not provide information on how
indirect costs are dealt with in the project budget.
CError! Not a valid embedded object.Cost baseline
Incorrect. The cost baseline is not a project document, but a component of the project
management plan. Furthermore, it does not include the logic on how the cost estimates
were determined.
DError! Not a valid embedded object.Project funding requirements
Incorrect. Project funding requirements is not a project document. They are projected costs
to be paid to fund the project. Usually, large companies schedule payments to fund projects
over the course of the year. These payments are known as the project funding requirements.
The project funding requirements do not have information on how indirect costs are
handled.

**Reference:**

- **A Guide to the Project Management Body of Knowledge, (PMBOK® Guide) – Sixth Edition,**
Project Management Institute Inc., 2017, Page(s) 250, 261, 246-247; see also
https://www.projectmanagement.com/blog-post/6753/5-Types-of-Project-Cost
Live FeedbackTM Back to Results

PMP Exam 4
Filtered Mode: Displaying 200 questions
Question 134 of 200
Question ID: 613711
Your current project has a 12-month timeline and a budget of $100,000. You are 6 months into
the project, and you have spent $60,000, but only 40% of the work is complete. You do not
anticipate that the cost performance will change and you estimate that the project will eventually
spend $150,000 at its completion.
Which of these statements is true about your project?
AError! Not a valid embedded object.The estimate to complete this project is $150,000.
BError! Not a valid embedded object.There is not enough information given to evaluate the project.
CError! Not a valid embedded object.To complete the remaining work, your team needs to have a cost
performance of 67%.
DError! Not a valid embedded object.The schedule efficiency of your team is 70% of the rate originally
planned.
Question answered incorrectly

**Hint:**

Determining the cost performance that must be maintained in order to complete the current
estimate at completion (EAC) is the TCPI.
Correct Answer: C

**Explanation:**

The total budget or BAC = $100,000. A budget for the project can be seen as its planned value
(PV). The cost so far or AC is $60,000. You have completed 40% of the work which is the EV or
40% of $100,000 or $40,000. To find the correct answer, you will have to calculate the earned
value analysis parameters provided in three out of the four answer choices. The correct answer is
the calculation of the TCPI. Based on the scenario, "you estimate that the project will eventually
spend $150,000 at its completion" implying the estimate at completion (EAC) is $150,000.
Therefore, the calculations are as follows:

---

TCPI = (BAC - EV) / (EAC - AC) = (100,000 - 40,000) / (150,000 - 60,000) = 60,000 / 90,000 =
0.67 meaning your team needs to maintain a cost performance of 67% to complete the project
with the current EAC.

**Details for Each Option:**

AError! Not a valid embedded object.The estimate to complete this project is $150,000.
Incorrect. This answer choice represents the estimate at completion (EAC), not the estimate
to complete (ETC). The ETC is calculated as: ETC = EAC - AC = $150,000 - $60,000 =
$90,000
BError! Not a valid embedded object.There is not enough information given to evaluate the
project.
Incorrect. The total budget or BAC = $100,000. The cost so far or AC is $60,000. You have
completed 40% of the work which is the EV or 40% of $100,000 or $40,000. You are 6
months, or 50%, into a 12-month project with a $100,000 budget so the planned value, or
PV, is 50% of $100,000 or $50,000. These values can be used to calculate any of the
earned value analysis calculations.
CError! Not a valid embedded object.To complete the remaining work, your team needs to
have a cost performance of 67%.
Correct. The to-complete performance index, or the TCPI, is the estimate of the future cost
performance that you need to complete the project within the approved budget. This budget
may be your initial approved budget, BAC, or a newly calculated budget/estimate at
completion, EAC. The TCPI is calculated using the formula: TCPI = (BAC - EV) / (EAC -
AC) = 0.67 which means that to complete the remaining work, your team needs to have a
cost performance of 67%.
DError! Not a valid embedded object.The schedule efficiency of your team is 70% of the rate
originally planned.
Incorrect. This answer suggests an SPI = 0.7. The SPI in this question is 0.8 using the
following formula: SPI = EV / PV = 40,000 / 50,000 = 0.8

**Reference:**

- **A Guide to the Project Management Body of Knowledge, (PMBOK® Guide) – Sixth Edition,**
Project Management Institute Inc., 2017, Page(s) 266-267
Live FeedbackTM Back to Results

Question 135 of 200
Question ID: 612436
You have just been hired to take over a software development project which is about halfway
complete. On your first day, you attend the daily standup meeting where you learn that one of the
developers has just quit without notice. You want to find out if this possibility was previously
identified and, if so, who was assigned the responsibility of following up on this situation.
What is your best course of action?
AError! Not a valid embedded object.Review the issue log
BError! Not a valid embedded object.Check the risk register
CError! Not a valid embedded object.Look at the risk report
DError! Not a valid embedded object.Ask the project sponsor
Question answered incorrectly

**Hint:**

Which project document records the agreed-upon risk responses for each identified risk and the
nominated owners for each response plan?
Correct Answer: B

**Explanation:**

The question indicates that a risk has been realized and it is unknown if the risk was previously
identified, analyzed, and documented. The risk register records the agreed-upon risk responses
for each identified risk and the nominated owners for each response plan. The risk register is
created as an output of the Identify Risks process and can serve as an input to the Implement
Risk Responses process, among others. Therefore, you should check the risk register to see if the
risk described by the question had been previously documented along with a nominated risk
owner.

---


**Details for Each Option:**

AError! Not a valid embedded object.Review the issue log
Incorrect. The issue log is a project document where information about issues is recorded
and monitored. The problem described in the question should be captured in the issue log.
However, issues are only recorded in the issue log once they have occurred. The question is
asking if the possibility of losing a member of the development team was previously
documented. The issue log documents actual issues rather than potential issues which may
or may not occur.
BError! Not a valid embedded object.Check the risk register
Correct. The risk register records the agreed-upon risk responses for each identified risk
and the nominated owners for each response plan.
CError! Not a valid embedded object.Look at the risk report
Incorrect. The risk report is a project document developed progressively throughout the
project life cycle which summarizes information on individual project risks and the level of
overall project risk. The risk of losing a member of the development may or may not have
been captured in the risk report. However, the risk report does not identify risk owners
associated with individual risks as asked by the question.
DError! Not a valid embedded object.Ask the project sponsor
Incorrect. The project sponsor may or may not be aware of identified project risks and
associated risk owners. However, you, as the project manager, should seek to use the
resources which are readily available to you before consulting with the project sponsor.

**Reference:**

- **A Guide to the Project Management Body of Knowledge, (PMBOK® Guide) – Sixth Edition,**
Project Management Institute Inc., 2017, Page(s) 450

PMP Exam 4
Filtered Mode: Displaying 200 questions
Question 136 of 200
Question ID: 612265
- **A project you are leading is approaching its end. One of the risk management subject matter**
experts assigned to the project calls you and recommends a change to the Implement Risk
Responses process.
What should you do first?
AError! Not a valid embedded object.Call a meeting with all project stakeholders to gain their
consensus on the change
BError! Not a valid embedded object.Instruct the team to implement the change as recommended by
the subject matter expert
CError! Not a valid embedded object.Document the recommendation as a formal proposal to modify
the requested process
DError! Not a valid embedded object.Tell the subject matter expert that changes are not accepted, as
the project is approaching closure
Question answered incorrectly

**Hint:**

What should be done first when a change is requested?
Correct Answer: C

**Explanation:**

Whenever a change is requested, the first step to take is to write and submit a change request. A
change request is a formal proposal to modify a document, deliverable, or baseline. The change
recommended by the subject matter expert will impact the process, Implement Risk Responses,
documented in the risk management plan, which is part of the project management plan. To
modify the plan, a change request is required. Therefore, the first thing to do when a change is
requested is to document the change as a formal proposal or, in other words, to submit a change
request. Once the change request is submitted, the Perform Integrated Change Control process
begins in which the change request is analyzed across all project constraints (scope, time, cost,

---

quality, risk, etc.). Later, a change control board or an authorized member of the project team
will decide on whether to accept or reject the change request based on the results of the analysis.

**Details for Each Option:**

AError! Not a valid embedded object.Call a meeting with all project stakeholders to gain their
consensus on the change
Incorrect. Having all project stakeholders agreed on a change sounds like an ideal
situation. However, calling a meeting with all project stakeholders is unlikely to be a
reasonable or realistic option. Even if the consensus can be reached, a submission of a
formal change request should precede the gathering of such a meeting. Otherwise, on what
basis would a project manager ask the stakeholders to spend time evaluating a request that
is not even documented?
BError! Not a valid embedded object.Instruct the team to implement the change as
recommended by the subject matter expert
Incorrect. The Implement Risk Responses process is documented in the risk management
plan, which is a component of the project management plan. To modify the plan, a change
request is required.
CError! Not a valid embedded object.Document the recommendation as a formal proposal to
modify the requested process
Correct. Despite the fact that the project is closing soon, the first step in this scenario is to
write and submit a change request, or, as phrased in this choice, to "document the
recommendation as a formal proposal to modify..." which is the definition of a change
request. The risk management plan, which is a component of the project management plan,
describes, among the others, the process of how risk responses will be implemented on the
project. Therefore, to modify the process, a change request should be submitted first,
making this choice the best answer to the question asked.
DError! Not a valid embedded object.Tell the subject matter expert that changes are not
accepted, as the project is approaching closure
Incorrect. This is not the correct first step to take as it does not take the subject matter
expert's suggestion into consideration. Regardless of when the project will be closing,
change requests should be submitted and analyzed according to the change management
plan. Simply telling the subject matter expert that the change cannot be reviewed may
result in an important and potentially beneficial suggestion on risk management being
missed or even cause a risk event to happen just days before project closure.

---


**Reference:**

- **A Guide to the Project Management Body of Knowledge, (PMBOK® Guide) – Sixth Edition,**
Project Management Institute Inc., 2017, Page(s) 96, 87, 405
Live FeedbackTM Back to Results
Prev Next

Question 137 of 200
Question ID: 613785
You have been hired by the Department of Natural Resources to lead a project for the
construction of new facilities at a local park. As the project manager, you are in the process of
selecting the various vendors which will be required to complete the work.
In this situation, the use of what tool or technique is most likely to be legally mandated by the
government agency?
AError! Not a valid embedded object.Agreements
BError! Not a valid embedded object.Requirements documentation
CError! Not a valid embedded object.Advertising
DError! Not a valid embedded object.Prequalified seller lists
Question answered incorrectly

**Hint:**

What tool or technique enhances transparency in awarding government contracts?
Correct Answer: C

**Explanation:**

Existing lists of potential sellers often can be expanded by placing advertisements in general
circulation publications such as newspapers or specialty trade publications. Most government
jurisdictions require public advertising or online posting of pending government contracts.
Advertising is likely to be legally mandated, and it is the only tool or technique of the available
answer choices.

**Details for Each Option:**


---

AError! Not a valid embedded object.Agreements
Incorrect. Contracts are likely to be required for a government project. However,
agreements are an output of the Conduct Procurements process and not a tool or a
technique.
BError! Not a valid embedded object.Requirements documentation
Incorrect. Requirements documentation is a description of how individual requirements
meet the business need for the project. Requirements documentation is a project document
rather than a tool or a technique.
CError! Not a valid embedded object.Advertising
Correct. Existing lists of potential sellers often can be expanded by placing advertisements
in general circulation publications. Most government jurisdictions require public
advertising or online posting of pending government contracts.
DError! Not a valid embedded object.Prequalified seller lists
Incorrect. Prequalified seller lists may be used during the Conduct Procurement process,
but they are an organizational process asset and not a tool or technique as the question is
asking.

**Reference:**

- **A Guide to the Project Management Body of Knowledge, (PMBOK® Guide) – Sixth Edition,**
Project Management Institute Inc., 2017, Page(s) 487

Question 138 of 200
Question ID: 612380
During a project to develop a new robot, a previously identified risk is realized. The risk
response plan calls for a project team member specially trained in robotics to address the
problem, but the individual named in the response plan has left the project. You reassign another
project team member with the required training to address the issue.
Which project document should be updated first?
AError! Not a valid embedded object.The quality management plan
BError! Not a valid embedded object.The risk response report
CError! Not a valid embedded object.The lessons learned repository
DError! Not a valid embedded object.The project team assignments
Question answered incorrectly

**Hint:**

Which of the available choices is a project document that may be updated as part of the
Implement Risk Responses process?
Correct Answer: D

**Explanation:**

The question suggests that the Implement Risk Responses process is being performed. Project
team assignments are one of the project documents that may be updated as a result of this
process. In the scenario, a previously identified risk has been realized. The risk response requires
the reassignment of a project team member to address the problem. Once the risk responses are
confirmed, the necessary resources should be allocated to each action associated with the risk
response plan. These resources include suitably qualified and experienced personnel to execute
the agreed-upon action (usually within the project team), a specific budget and time allowance
for the action, and any required technical resources to complete the action. Of the available
choices, only the project team assignments should be updated as the result of implementing risk

---

responses.

**Details for Each Option:**

AError! Not a valid embedded object.The quality management plan
Incorrect. The quality management plan is a component of the project management plan
that describes how applicable policies, procedures, and guidelines will be implemented to
achieve the quality objectives set for the project. The fact the team member initially
assigned to address the problem is unavailable does not change the contents of the quality
management plan nor its objectives.
BError! Not a valid embedded object.The risk response report
Incorrect. 'Risk response report' is a fake term made up for this question
CError! Not a valid embedded object.The lessons learned repository
Incorrect. The lessons learned repository is a store of historical information about lessons
learned from projects. The lessons learned repository is not updated until project closure
began when the information contained in the lessons learned register is transferred to the
lessons learned repository.
DError! Not a valid embedded object.The project team assignments
Correct. Resources associated with the implementation of the risk response plans should be
allocated to each action specified in the risk register. As a result, the project team
assignments document should be updated accordingly to reflect the changes in the team
members' assignments, making this choice the best answer to the question asked.

**Reference:**

- **A Guide to the Project Management Body of Knowledge, (PMBOK® Guide) – Sixth Edition,**
Project Management Institute Inc., 2017, Page(s) 452

Question 139 of 200
Question ID: 613727
Two project team members have had frequent clashes, which have at times resulted in shouting
matches during team meetings. The project manager has intervened, asked them to resolve their
differences, and even facilitated a meeting between them, but things have gotten worse. The
project manager is concerned that the situation is negatively affecting team cohesion and is
placing the successful completion of the project at risk.
What should the project manager do next?
AError! Not a valid embedded object.Use formal procedures including disciplinary actions
BError! Not a valid embedded object.Allow the team members to resolve their differences on their own
CError! Not a valid embedded object.Facilitate another meeting between the two team members
DError! Not a valid embedded object.Request that the other project team members intercede as a form
of peer pressure
Question answered incorrectly

**Hint:**

What is the proper escalation path in this scenario?
Correct Answer: A

**Explanation:**

Project team members are initially responsible for resolving their own conflicts. If the conflict
escalates, the project manager should help facilitate a satisfactory resolution. If the disruptive
conflict persists, formal procedures may be used, including disciplinary action. In this scenario,
the project manager has already given the team members the opportunity to resolve their own
issues and attempted to facilitate a resolution. The project manager should not allow conflict to
put the success of the project at risk. The project manager should use formal procedures
including disciplinary actions to resolve the issue.

---


**Details for Each Option:**

AError! Not a valid embedded object.Use formal procedures including disciplinary actions
Correct. Formal procedures may be used including disciplinary actions in order to prevent
the project from being put at risk.
BError! Not a valid embedded object.Allow the team members to resolve their differences on
their own
Incorrect. The first step is to allow the team members to resolve the conflict on their own.
However, that has failed to resolve the issue, and the project is at risk.
CError! Not a valid embedded object.Facilitate another meeting between the two team
members
Incorrect. The second step is for the project manager to facilitate a resolution between the
parties. However, that has failed to resolve the issue, and the project is at risk.
DError! Not a valid embedded object.Request that the other project team members intercede
as a form of peer pressure
Incorrect. Conflict should be addressed privately and confidentially. It is inappropriate to
involve the other team members in conflict resolution.

**Reference:**

- **A Guide to the Project Management Body of Knowledge, (PMBOK® Guide) – Sixth Edition,**
Project Management Institute Inc., 2017, Page(s) 348

PMP Exam 4
Filtered Mode: Displaying 200 questions
Question 140 of 200
Question ID: 612508
During a procurement audit, it is discovered that a vendor's project team is spending an
inordinate amount of time using a group review technique which was not stipulated in the
contract, thus causing a delay to the project. A corrective action has been taken to address the
issue.
What should the project manager document in the lessons learned register regarding the vendor?
AError! Not a valid embedded object.A record indicating that the vendor should not be considered for
future projects
BError! Not a valid embedded object.Recommendation to include the vendor for future projects
CError! Not a valid embedded object.Effectiveness of corrective actions used to improve vendor's
performance
DError! Not a valid embedded object.Procurement information is not captured in lessons learned
register
Question answered incorrectly

**Hint:**

What type of procurement information may be useful for the current project or future projects?
Correct Answer: C

**Explanation:**

- **A procurement audit is a structured review of the procurement process, and the lessons learned**
register is updated with relevant information on procurements. For example, when variance
occurs, and the corrective action is taken to address variance, the lessons learned register should
be updated with the description of the situation and the actions taken to address it along with the
indication on how effective those actions were. At the end of the project, the lessons learned are
transferred to the lessons learned repository to serve future projects in improving their
procurement efforts. Of the available answer choices, only the effectiveness of corrective actions

---

would be recorded in the lessons learned register.

**Details for Each Option:**

AError! Not a valid embedded object.A record indicating that the vendor should not be
considered for future projects
Incorrect. Based on poor performance, the vendor may be removed from consideration for
future projects. However, removing the vendor from consideration for future work requires
an update to the prequalified seller lists and the seller performance evaluation
documentation rather than the lessons learned register.
BError! Not a valid embedded object.Recommendation to include the vendor for future
projects
Incorrect. The vendor ran behind schedule by performing work not specified in the
contract. Based on the limited information presented in the scenario, it is unlikely that the
vendor would be recommended for use on future projects. While the recommendation not to
include the vendor for future projects could be documented in the lessons learned register,
the right place for such a recommendation is the seller performance evaluation
documentation.
CError! Not a valid embedded object.Effectiveness of corrective actions used to improve
vendor's performance
Correct. A procurement audit is a structured review of the procurement process. The
lessons learned register is updated with relevant information on procurements. Where
variances occurred, the register should show the corrective actions that were used to
respond to variances and how effective those actions were. The project manager works
with the vendor to address the variance. Any corrective actions that resulted from this
interaction, as well as the effectiveness of the actions, should be documented in the lessons
learned register.
DError! Not a valid embedded object.Procurement information is not captured in lessons
learned register
Incorrect. Any pertinent information regarding procurements which may be useful later in
the current project, or on future projects, is documented in the lessons learned register. If
there have been any claims, information should be documented to avoid recurrences.
Additional information on how to improve the procurement process can also be recorded in
the lessons learned register.

**Reference:**


---

- **A Guide to the Project Management Body of Knowledge, (PMBOK® Guide) – Sixth Edition,**
Project Management Institute Inc., 2017, Page(s) 498, 500

PMP Exam 4
Filtered Mode: Displaying 200 questions
Question 141 of 200
Question ID: 613691
- **A project is in planning. The project has many unknown components making it hard to**
decompose and schedule adequately. You are a senior project manager, and in a project like this,
you would typically plan the schedule to a higher level first and wait until the project has begun
to plan the lower levels. However, this project has been assigned to a junior project manager. She
is in the process to develop the schedule management plan and approaches you for advice on
how to better accomplish this task.
By looking for your advice, what tool is the junior project manager using to plan her project?
AError! Not a valid embedded object.Rolling wave planning
BError! Not a valid embedded object.Expert judgment
CError! Not a valid embedded object.On-demand scheduling
DError! Not a valid embedded object.Iterative scheduling
Question answered incorrectly

**Hint:**

What tools and techniques are used in the Plan Schedule Management process?
Correct Answer: B

**Explanation:**

It can be implied that the junior project manager is performing the Plan Schedule Management
process which will result in the schedule management plan. The scenario also describes rolling
wave planning as one of the tools that you, as a senior project manager, typically use on projects
with many unknowns. However, this question is not asking for a scheduling methodology. The
junior project manager has approached you, a senior project manager, for help in planning her
project. In other words, she is looking for your expertise or expert judgment. This question is an
example of a scenario that has some extraneous information which may purposefully or not
mislead prospective PMP aspirants. Always read the full question.

---


**Details for Each Option:**

AError! Not a valid embedded object.Rolling wave planning
Incorrect. Rolling wave planning is a scheduling technique where the schedule in the near
term is planned in detail, while the schedule in the future is planned to a higher level first
and then detailed as the project progresses. However, this question is not asking for a
scheduling technique. The junior project manager has approached you, a senior project
manager, for help in planning her project.
BError! Not a valid embedded object.Expert judgment
Correct. Expert judgment is one of the tools and techniques that can be used as part of the
Plan Schedule Management process described in the scenario. The junior project manager
asking for advice from the senior project manager is an example of expert judgment.
CError! Not a valid embedded object.On-demand scheduling
Incorrect. On-demand scheduling is an approach which is typically used on projects where
the workflow is managed in a Kanban system. There is not enough information in the
scenario to determine if Kanban system is used on the project. Additionally, the essence of
the question surrounds the way the junior project manager approaches schedule planning
rather than a specific scheduling methodology.
DError! Not a valid embedded object.Iterative scheduling
Incorrect. Iterative scheduling is a form of rolling wave planning based on adaptive project
life cycles. However, the question is not asking for a scheduling method. The question asks
for the tool used by the junior project manager when she approaches the senior project
manager.

**Reference:**

- **A Guide to the Project Management Body of Knowledge, (PMBOK® Guide) – Sixth Edition,**
Project Management Institute Inc., 2017, Page(s) 181, 177

PMP Exam 4
Filtered Mode: Displaying 200 questions
Question 142 of 200
Question ID: 612460
- **A project team is comprised of former military and non-military team members. The team**
members without a military background view the former military team members as overly
structured and rigid in their approach to the project. The former military members view the other
team members' more casual approach as an indication that they are less committed to the project.
What tool or technique will be the most useful for the project manager and the team members to
communicate effectively?
AError! Not a valid embedded object.Political awareness
BError! Not a valid embedded object.Team charter
CError! Not a valid embedded object.Conflict management
DError! Not a valid embedded object.Cultural awareness
Question answered incorrectly

**Hint:**

What tool or technique is most helpful when dealing with groups or individuals with different
backgrounds and values?
Correct Answer: D

**Explanation:**

The question describes a project team made of two distinct groups of individuals (military and
non-military). It is apparent from the description in the question that these groups have different
backgrounds and values. Cultural awareness is used to help the project manager and team to
communicate effectively by considering cultural differences and the requirements of
stakeholders. Of the available choices, understanding these cultural differences will be most
valuable to the project manager and the team in fostering effective communication.

---


**Details for Each Option:**

AError! Not a valid embedded object.Political awareness
Incorrect. Political awareness is achieved through understanding the power relationships
within and around the project. The question describes two groups within the project team
with different backgrounds. There is no indication from the question that there is a
difference in the power and influence of one group over the other. Therefore, power
relationships are unlikely to be a factor in this scenario.
BError! Not a valid embedded object.Team charter
Incorrect. The team charter is a project document that establishes the team values,
agreements, and operating guidelines for the team. As such, the team charter can be helpful
in the scenario described. However, the team charter is a project document and not a tool
or technique and is, therefore, not the best answer to the question asked.
CError! Not a valid embedded object.Conflict management
Incorrect. Cultural differences may or may not lead to conflict. The question describes two
distinct groups of individuals with different backgrounds and values. However, the question
does not indicate whether or not there is an actual conflict between these two groups.
Therefore, conflict management is not the most useful tool or technique in the scenario
described.
DError! Not a valid embedded object.Cultural awareness
Correct. Cultural awareness is an example of the interpersonal and team skill that can be
used as a tool or technique in various project management processes. Cultural awareness
is used to help the project manager and team to communicate effectively by considering
cultural differences and the requirements of stakeholders.

- **A Guide to the Project Management Body of Knowledge, (PMBOK® Guide) – Sixth Edition,**
Project Management Institute Inc., 2017, Page(s) 376, 386, 527, 534, 552

PMP Exam 4
Filtered Mode: Displaying 200 questions
Question 143 of 200
Question ID: 650503
- **A project team member provides the project manager with duration estimates for one of her**
tasks. The team member specifies a pessimistic estimate of 75 days, an optimistic estimate of 30
days, and a most likely estimate of 60 days. The project manager requests that the team member
provide a single estimate by using a beta distribution formula.
What estimate should the team member provide?
AError! Not a valid embedded object.55 days
BError! Not a valid embedded object.60 days
CError! Not a valid embedded object.47.5 days
DError! Not a valid embedded object.57.5 days
Question answered incorrectly

**Hint:**

This question requires you to have memorized the beta distribution formula.
Correct Answer: D

**Explanation:**

The scenario involves the project manager asking that a team member to use a beta distribution
to provide a single value estimate for the duration of the task.
Therefore, to answer the question correctly, one should use the appropriate formula:
D= (O + 4*M + P) / 6 = (30 + 4*60 + 75) / 6 = 345 / 6 = 57.5 days

**Details for Each Option:**


---

AError! Not a valid embedded object.55 days
Incorrect. You may have chosen this answer if you used the simple triangular distribution
formula, where D = (O + M + P) / 3 = (30 + 60 + 75) / 3 = 165 / 3 = 55. However, the
beta distribution formula is required.
BError! Not a valid embedded object.60 days
Incorrect. This answer choice represents the most likely estimate. The question is asking
about the estimate calculated using the beta distribution formula.
CError! Not a valid embedded object.47.5 days
Incorrect. You may have chosen this answer if you incorrectly used the formula: D = (O
+3M + P) / 6 = (30 + 3*60 + 75) / 6 = 47.5. In other words, you multiplied the most likely
estimate 60 by 3 instead of 4.
DError! Not a valid embedded object.57.5 days
Correct. This answer choice represents cost estimate correctly calculated using weighted
beta distribution formula as required by the question: D = (O + 4M + P) / 6 = (30 + 4*60
+ 75) / 6 = 345 / 6 = 57.5 days.

**Reference:**

- **A Guide to the Project Management Body of Knowledge, (PMBOK® Guide) – Sixth Edition,**
Project Management Institute Inc., 2017, Page(s) 201, 245; see also the PMI Practice Standard
for Scheduling.

PMP Exam 4
Filtered Mode: Displaying 200 questions
Question 144 of 200
Question ID: 613671
- **A project manager is planning a project to construct a new multiplex movie theater. As she starts**
the process of estimating the costs associated with the project, she is unsure whether to use an
analogous or bottom-up approach. The company has built similar movie theaters in the past, but
senior management has a preference for the highest level of detail.
What is the best resource to determine the estimating method that should be used for the project?
AError! Not a valid embedded object.Basis of estimates
BError! Not a valid embedded object.Resource management plan
CError! Not a valid embedded object.Cost management plan
DError! Not a valid embedded object.Scope baseline
Question answered incorrectly

**Hint:**

Which component of the project management plan describes estimating methods that can be used
during the Estimate Costs process?
Correct Answer: C

**Explanation:**

It can be inferred from the question that the Estimate Costs process is being performed. The cost
management plan is the component of the project management plan that describes how costs will
be planned including the estimating methods that can be used. The cost management plan is the
best resource for the project manager to determine how the Estimate Costs process should be
performed.

**Details for Each Option:**


---

AError! Not a valid embedded object.Basis of estimates
Incorrect. The basis of estimates provides supporting documentation for cost estimates but
does not provide guidance on estimating methods. Additionally, the basis of estimates is an
output from, not an input to, the Estimate Costs process.
BError! Not a valid embedded object.Resource management plan
Incorrect. The resource management plan describes how project resources are acquired,
allocated, monitored, and controlled, but it does not provide guidance on how costs are to
be estimated.
CError! Not a valid embedded object.Cost management plan
Correct. The cost management plan is the component of the project management plan that
describes how costs will be planned, structured, and controlled. The cost management plan
is the document that describes the estimating methods that can be used during the Estimate
Costs process, which is what the question asks.
DError! Not a valid embedded object.Scope baseline
Incorrect. The scope baseline is the approved version of a scope statement, work
breakdown structure (WBS), and its associated WBS dictionary. The scope baseline is not a
resource for cost estimating methods.

**Reference:**

- **A Guide to the Project Management Body of Knowledge, (PMBOK® Guide) – Sixth Edition,**
Project Management Institute Inc., 2017, Page(s) 241

PMP Exam 4
Filtered Mode: Displaying 200 questions
Question 145 of 200
Question ID: 613786
- **A project manager evaluates sellers' proposals for the deliverables the company wants to**
outsource and selects sellers who are in a competitive range for the work required. Since the
company considers this work to be complex and bear high value and risk, the project manager
submits these sellers to senior management for approval before awarding the contract.
Which of the following would be the most likely result of the project manager's efforts?
AError! Not a valid embedded object.Prescribed sellers
BError! Not a valid embedded object.Advertising
CError! Not a valid embedded object.Prequalified sellers
DError! Not a valid embedded object.Agreements
Question answered incorrectly

**Hint:**

The sellers have been selected. Once the approval is gained for a specific seller(s), what happens
next?
Correct Answer: D

**Explanation:**

The scenario suggests the project manager is carrying out the Conduct Procurements process.
Among the others, selected sellers and agreements (contracts) are outputs from this process. The
selected sellers are those who have been judged to be in a competitive range based on the
outcome of the proposal or bid evaluation. A contract is a mutually binding agreement that
obligates the seller to provide the specified products, services, or results; obligates the buyer to
compensate the seller; and represents a legal relationship that is subject to remedy in the courts.
However, for complex, high-value, high-risk procurements as the one described in the scenario,
before an agreement (contract) can be awarded to a seller, final approval of the organizational
senior management will typically be required. Once this approval is gained, a contract
(agreement) can be awarded. Therefore, of the choices provided, agreements would be the most

---

likely result of the project manager's efforts in the scenario described.
Note, one may argue that if no approval is gained from the senior management, no
agreements/contracts will be awarded. While this scenario is possible, none of the answer
choices addresses this option. Therefore, an assumption has to be made that approval is gained
resulting in a contract and thus making "agreements" the best answer to the question asked.

**Details for Each Option:**

AError! Not a valid embedded object.Prescribed sellers
Incorrect. 'Prescribed sellers' is a fake term made up for this question.
BError! Not a valid embedded object.Advertising
Incorrect. Advertising is communicating with users or potential users of a product, service,
or result. Advertising is one of the tools and techniques that can be used as part of the
Conduct Procurements process suggested by the scenario. However, according to the
scenario, sellers' responses have already been received, implying advertising has already
taken place earlier in the project.
CError! Not a valid embedded object.Prequalified sellers
Incorrect. Prequalified sellers are specified in the prequalified seller lists. A prequalified
seller list is a list of sellers which have been pre-approved by the procuring organization.
The question does not specify whether or not a prequalified seller list has been used.
Additionally, prequalified seller lists are more likely to be used to solicit proposals, while
the question is asking about the result of the proposal evaluations.
DError! Not a valid embedded object.Agreements
Correct. Agreements define the initial intentions of a project and can take the form of a
contract, memorandum of understanding (MOU), letters of agreement, verbal agreements,
email, etc. According to the scenario, the sellers have been selected. Therefore, once
approval is provided by the senior management, an agreement (contract) will likely be
awarded.

**Reference:**

- **A Guide to the Project Management Body of Knowledge, (PMBOK® Guide) – Sixth Edition,**
Project Management Institute Inc., 2017, Page(s) 488-489
Live FeedbackTM Back to Results
