PMP Exam 4
Filtered Mode: Displaying 200 questions
Question 146 of 200
Question ID: 612357
- **A construction project has experienced weather-related delays as well as performance issues with**
several key vendors, and the risk responses have been implemented with varying degrees of
success. A senior executive has asked the project manager for an update on the current overall
project risk exposure.
What should the project manager do?
AError! Not a valid embedded object.Provide the senior executive a copy of the updated risk register
BError! Not a valid embedded object.Make sure the risk report is updated and provide it to the senior
executive
CError! Not a valid embedded object.Refer the senior executive to the risk management plan
DError! Not a valid embedded object.Send an updated copy of the risk exposure report to the senior
executive
Question answered incorrectly

**Hint:**

What may be updated with information on overall project risks as the result of the Implement
Risk Responses process?
Correct Answer: B

**Explanation:**

The question suggests that the Implement Risk Responses process has been performed multiple
times to address high-level project risks that were realized throughout project execution. The risk
report is typically updated to reflect any changes to the previously agreed-upon risk responses to
overall project risk exposure that are subsequently made as a result of the Implement Risk
Responses process. Of the available choices, only the risk report provides information on overall
project risks. Therefore, to address the senior executive’s request, the project manager should
make sure the risk report is updated with the latest information and provide the report to the

---

senior executive.

**Details for Each Option:**

AError! Not a valid embedded object.Provide the senior executive a copy of the updated risk
register
Incorrect. The risk register may be updated to reflect any changes to the previously agreed-
upon risk responses for ‘individual’ project risks that are subsequently made as a result of
the Implement Risk Responses process. However, the question is asking about overall
project risks and not individual project risks. Overall project risks are not recorded in the
risk register. Additionally, senior executives are typically looking for summary information
(which is available in a risk report) rather than details (which are available in the risk
register).
BError! Not a valid embedded object.Make sure the risk report is updated and provide it to the
senior executive
Correct. The risk report may be updated to reflect any changes to the previously agreed-
upon risk responses to overall project risk exposure that are subsequently made as a result
of the Implement Risk Responses process. Therefore, the project manager should update
the risk report and provide a copy to the senior executive.
CError! Not a valid embedded object.Refer the senior executive to the risk management plan
Incorrect. The risk management plan is a component of the project management plan that
describes how risk management activities will be structured and performed. However, the
risk management plan does not provide insight into overall project risk exposure.
DError! Not a valid embedded object.Send an updated copy of the risk exposure report to the
senior executive
Incorrect. 'Risk exposure report' is a fake term made up for this question.

**Reference:**

- **A Guide to the Project Management Body of Knowledge, (PMBOK® Guide) – Sixth Edition,**
Project Management Institute Inc., 2017, Page(s) 418, 452

PMP Exam 4
Filtered Mode: Displaying 200 questions
Question 147 of 200
Question ID: 612538
Once a quarter, a project manager invites managers from various departments to the project team
meetings. Although these managers are not involved in the project, the project manager invites
them because this is what she was doing in her previous organization. However, when any of
these managers attend the meetings, their questions cause the meeting to run late.
What should have been done differently?
AError! Not a valid embedded object.Starting the meeting by stating the objectives
BError! Not a valid embedded object.Following up the meeting with minutes
CError! Not a valid embedded object.Preparing and distributing an agenda
DError! Not a valid embedded object.Inviting the appropriate participants
Question answered incorrectly

**Hint:**

Which step for effective meeting planning is not being followed in the scenario?
Correct Answer: D

**Explanation:**

The scenario implies that the Manage Communications process is being carried out. Meeting
management is among the interpersonal and team skills that can be used as a tool or technique
during this process. Effective meeting management involves taking steps to ensure meetings
achieve their intended objectives effectively and efficiently. All of the answer choices are steps
that should be used for meeting planning. However, the scenario mentions one step that the
project manager is not following: ensuring appropriate participants are invited. The managers
from the various departments are not involved in the current project and therefore are not
considered appropriate participants. Just because inviting irrelevant to the project managers was
a practice in one organization does not mean this practice will work or should be implemented in
another organization or even in a different project in the same organization. The matter of fact is
that in the current organization in the current project the meetings only run long when the

---

irrelevant managers attend. Therefore, the best course of action to prevent the meetings from
running late is not to invite those managers going forward.

**Details for Each Option:**

AError! Not a valid embedded object.Starting the meeting by stating the objectives
Incorrect. While starting a meeting by stating the objectives is always a good practice for
managing a meeting, the scenario doesn't provide any details on how the project manager
leads meetings. Additionally, starting the meeting by stating the meeting objectives would
not prevent the managers from asking questions, which is the reason the meetings run late.
BError! Not a valid embedded object.Following up the meeting with minutes
Incorrect. Following-up a meeting with minutes is good practice. However, minutes will
have no impact on the length of the meeting.
CError! Not a valid embedded object.Preparing and distributing an agenda
Incorrect. Preparing and distributing an agenda for meetings is an essential step in
meeting management. The scenario does not supply enough information about how the
meetings are managed except that the meetings run long whenever the managers from the
various departments attend. However, even an effective agenda by itself would not prevent
the managers from asking questions, which is the reason the meetings run late.
DError! Not a valid embedded object.Inviting the appropriate participants
Correct. Inviting the appropriate participants will help ensure meetings meet their
objectives efficiently. Since the managers from the various departments are not involved in
the current project, they likely do not offer anything of value at the team meetings and only
cause the meetings to run longer than planned. Therefore, the best course of action to
prevent the meetings from running late is to discontinue inviting these managers to the
meetings.

**Reference:**

- **A Guide to the Project Management Body of Knowledge, (PMBOK® Guide) – Sixth Edition,**
Project Management Institute Inc., 2017, Page(s) 386
Live FeedbackTM Back to Results
Prev Next

PMP Exam 4
Filtered Mode: Displaying 200 questions
Question 148 of 200
Question ID: 612248
When closing out a project, who is responsible for transferring the ownership of deliverables to
the customer?
AError! Not a valid embedded object.The project manager
BError! Not a valid embedded object.The project sponsor
CError! Not a valid embedded object.The project management office
DError! Not a valid embedded object.Anyone on the project team
Question answered incorrectly

**Hint:**

When does a project manager's responsibility for a project end?
Correct Answer: A

**Explanation:**

- **A project manager's responsibility for a project does not end until all the closing processes are**
complete, including transitioning the project deliverables to the recipient defined in the project
management plan. The project manager would be responsible for transferring the project
deliverables to the customer during the Close Project or Phase process.

**Details for Each Option:**

AError! Not a valid embedded object.The project manager
Correct. When closing out a project, the project manager would be responsible for
transferring ownership of the project deliverables to the assigned stakeholders.

---

BError! Not a valid embedded object.The project sponsor
Incorrect. A project sponsor is an individual or a group that authorizes the project and the
project manager thru the project charter. The project sponsor would not typically be the
one who transfers the ownership of deliverables to the customer.
CError! Not a valid embedded object.The project management office
Incorrect. A project management office (PMO) is an organizational structure that
standardizes the project-related governance processes and facilitates the sharing of
resources, methodologies, tools, and techniques. The PMO is unlikely to be the one to
transfer the ownership of deliverables to the customer.
DError! Not a valid embedded object.Anyone on the project team
Incorrect. This answer choice could be a plausible option because the procedure to
transfer the ownership of the project deliverables to the customer or assigned stakeholders
are specified in the project management plan. Therefore, theoretically, any team member
can be specified in the plan to perform the role. However, since the question does not
provide any details on the plan, a more generic choice, i.e. the project manager, would be a
better answer to the question asked.

**Reference:**

Project Management Professional (PMP)® Examination Content Outline, Project Management
Institute Inc., June 2015, Domain V, Task 2

PMP Exam 4
Filtered Mode: Displaying 200 questions
Question 149 of 200
Question ID: 612564
You are using expert judgment to develop high-level requirements and identify high-level risks
for the project you are currently managing. As part of this effort, you have already documented a
list of key stakeholders and preapproved financial resources.
All of the following are considered inputs to this process except:
AError! Not a valid embedded object.Business case
BError! Not a valid embedded object.Enterprise environmental factors
CError! Not a valid embedded object.Organizational process assets
DError! Not a valid embedded object.Project management plan
Question answered incorrectly

**Hint:**

The document you are working on contains high-level information.
Correct Answer: D

**Explanation:**

In the scenario, you are documenting high-level requirements and high-level risks for the project
you are managing. Therefore, it is reasonable to assume you are in the Develop Project Charter
process. Inputs for that process are business documents, including the business case, enterprise
environmental factors, organizational process assets, and agreements. The project management
plan is not an input to the Develop Project Charter process. Since the question is asking which of
the answer choices is 'not' used as an input to that process, the project management plan the
correct answer.

**Details for Each Option:**


---

AError! Not a valid embedded object.Business case
Incorrect. The business case is a document that represents the information required from a
business perspective to justify the existence of the project. The scenario implies you are in
the Develop Project Charter process. The business case is among the business documents
used as an input to that process. Therefore, the business case is not the correct answer.
BError! Not a valid embedded object.Enterprise environmental factors
Incorrect. Since the scenario describes the development of high-level requirements and an
identification of high-level risks, you are in the Develop Project Charter process.
Enterprise environmental factors are conditions, not under the immediate control of the
team, that influence, constrain, or direct the project. Enterprise environmental factors,
such as stakeholders' risk tolerances, are an input to the Develop Project Charter process
and, therefore, is an incorrect answer.
CError! Not a valid embedded object.Organizational process assets
Incorrect. According to the scenario, you are in the Develop Project Charter process. The
question is asking which of the answer choices is 'not' an input to the Develop Project
Charter process. Organizational process assets are an input to the process and is,
therefore, an incorrect answer.
DError! Not a valid embedded object.Project management plan
Correct. The project management plan is the document that describes how the project will
be executed, monitored and controlled, and closed. Based on the scenario described, the
project is in the Develop Project Charter process. The project management plan is
developed later in the project life cycle and cannot be the input to the Develop Project
Charter process. Therefore, since the question is asking which document is 'not' an input to
the Develop Project Charter process, project management plan is the correct answer.

**Reference:**

- **A Guide to the Project Management Body of Knowledge, (PMBOK® Guide) – Sixth Edition,**
Project Management Institute Inc., 2017, Page(s) 75-79

PMP Exam 4
Filtered Mode: Displaying 200 questions
Question 150 of 200
Question ID: 650410
The total planned cost for your project at this stage is $5,000,000. The actual work that has been
completed is worth $4,000,000. You have already spent $10,000,000 on the project.
What is the CPI and status of your project?
AError! Not a valid embedded object.0.4 and under planned costs
BError! Not a valid embedded object.0.8 and behind schedule
CError! Not a valid embedded object.0.4 and over planned costs
DError! Not a valid embedded object.0.8 and ahead of schedule
Question answered incorrectly

**Hint:**

CPI = EV / AC
Correct Answer: C

**Explanation:**

In this scenario, the earned value (EV) is $4,000,000, the actual costs (AC) are $10,000,000, and
the planned value (PV) is $5,000,000. The question is asking you to calculate the cost
performance index (CPI) and determine the project status. The CPI is calculated as EV / AC or
CPI = $4,000,000 / $10,000,000 which is 0.4. Since the CPI is less than 1.0, the project is over
planned costs. Note that the PV of $5,000,000 is not needed to answer the question correctly.

**Details for Each Option:**

AError! Not a valid embedded object.0.4 and under planned costs
Incorrect. The CPI is calculated as EV / AC or CPI = $4,000,000 / $10,000,000 which is

---

0.4. Even though the CPI was calculated correctly with this answer choice, the project is
over planned costs and not under planned costs.
BError! Not a valid embedded object.0.8 and behind schedule
Incorrect. The SPI for the project is 0.8, and the project is behind schedule. SPI = EV / PV
or SPI = $4,000,000 / $5,000,000. However, the question is asking for the CPI and not the
SPI.
CError! Not a valid embedded object.0.4 and over planned costs
Correct. The CPI is calculated as EV / AC or CPI = $4,000,000 / $10,000,000 which is 0.4.
Since the CPI is less than 1.0, the project is over planned costs.
DError! Not a valid embedded object.0.8 and ahead of schedule
Incorrect. The SPI for the project is 0.8, and the project is behind schedule rather than
ahead of schedule. SPI = EV / PV or SPI = $4,000,000 / $5,000,000. Additionally, the
question is asking for the CPI and not the SPI.

**Reference:**

- **A Guide to the Project Management Body of Knowledge, (PMBOK® Guide) – Sixth Edition,**
Project Management Institute Inc., 2017, Page(s) 263; see also https://www.project-
management-prepcast.com/pmp-formulas

PMP Exam 4
Filtered Mode: Displaying 200 questions
Question 151 of 200
Question ID: 613325
As the project manager working on a large, multi-year project, you have conducted an extensive
series of training and development activities for the team. This has greatly benefited both the
team and the productivity of the project, resulting in a very successful initial year.
What should you use to ensure that your team members will be recognized for their performance
after they leave the project?
AError! Not a valid embedded object.Lessons learned register
BError! Not a valid embedded object.Project team assignments
CError! Not a valid embedded object.Personnel assessment
DError! Not a valid embedded object.Team charter
Question answered incorrectly

**Hint:**

Which answer choice focuses on individual performance?
Correct Answer: C

**Explanation:**

The scenario implies that you are concerned with the Develop Team process. On longer-term
projects, the project manager will either write or contribute to her team members' corporate
personnel assessments. Because personnel assessments are organizational process assets, as an
output of the Develop Team process, they will have an impact beyond the life of the project and
have the potential to directly impact your team members' career prospects.

**Details for Each Option:**


---

AError! Not a valid embedded object.Lessons learned register
Incorrect. Although the lessons learned register is used to record knowledge gained during
the project, it is not the most effective way to recognize individual performance.
BError! Not a valid embedded object.Project team assignments
Incorrect. Project team assignments is a document that specifies the team members and
their roles and responsibilities for the project. This document does not provide information
on the performance of the team members and, therefore, would not help ensure that they
will be recognized for their performance after they leave the project.
CError! Not a valid embedded object.Personnel assessment
Correct. Writing detailed, positive assessments can directly contribute to your team
members career success. Because of the long-term nature of this project and the extensive
amount of training and development activity, the project manager may very well be the
primary contributor to the team's regular assessments.
DError! Not a valid embedded object.Team charter
Incorrect. The team charter is used to specify team values and operating guidelines; it will
not include details of individual performance.

**Reference:**

- **A Guide to the Project Management Body of Knowledge, (PMBOK® Guide) – Sixth Edition,**
Project Management Institute Inc., 2017, Page(s) 344

PMP Exam 4
Filtered Mode: Displaying 200 questions
Question 152 of 200
Question ID: 612958
Who has the responsibility to monitor, record, and report the realized benefits throughout the
project?
AError! Not a valid embedded object.Human resources manager
BError! Not a valid embedded object.Project manager
CError! Not a valid embedded object.Project sponsor
DError! Not a valid embedded object.Benefits owner
Question answered incorrectly

**Hint:**

The responsible party for tracking and reporting project benefits is recorded in the benefits
management plan.
Correct Answer: D

**Explanation:**

The project benefits management plan is the document that specifies how and when the benefits
of the project will be delivered. The plan describes the mechanisms that should be in place to
measure those benefits. A well-thought-out benefits management plan would specify a benefits
owner who is the individual or group responsible for monitoring, recording, and reporting the
realized benefits throughout the project.

**Details for Each Option:**

AError! Not a valid embedded object.Human resources manager
Incorrect. Human resources (HR) managers oversee department functions and managing
employees. The question is asking about project benefits and not employee benefits. HR

---

resource managers may handle employee benefits but not necessarily project benefits.
BError! Not a valid embedded object.Project manager
Incorrect. A project manager is a person assigned by the performing organization to lead
the team and is responsible for achieving the project objectives. While a project manager
may be responsible for monitoring, recording, and reporting the realized benefits of the
project, another answer choice more accurately addresses the question asked.
CError! Not a valid embedded object.Project sponsor
Incorrect. A project sponsor is an individual who formally authorizes the project. A project
sponsor is typically a senior manager or executive and is unlikely to be assigned to
monitor, record, and report the realized benefits of the project.
DError! Not a valid embedded object.Benefits owner
Correct. A properly prepared benefits management plan identifies a benefits owner that has
the responsibility of monitoring, recording, and reporting the realized benefits throughout
the project.

**Reference:**

- **A Guide to the Project Management Body of Knowledge, (PMBOK® Guide) – Sixth Edition,**
Project Management Institute Inc., 2017, Page(s) 33

PMP Exam 4
Filtered Mode: Displaying 200 questions
Question 153 of 200
Question ID: 612965
During a status meeting, a team member states that he is having trouble getting the necessary
information from the customer, and as a result will not get an important deliverable completed on
time. You have not previously heard of any issues with this customer and suspect the team
member is simply making excuses for poor work performance.
What is your best course of action?
AError! Not a valid embedded object.Tell the team member not to make any further excuses and get
the job done or risk disciplinary action
BError! Not a valid embedded object.Contact the customer right away to discuss the issue
CError! Not a valid embedded object.Schedule a one-on-one meeting with the team member to discuss
the issue and possible next steps
DError! Not a valid embedded object.Escalate this issue to the team member's supervisor
Question answered incorrectly

**Hint:**

Conflict should be addressed early and usually in private, using a direct, collaborative approach.
Correct Answer: C

**Explanation:**

Conflict management is one of the tools and techniques of the Manage Team process. Successful
conflict management involves addressing conflict early using a direct, collaborative approach. In
this scenario, the conflict involves a project team member, who may or may not be having a
performance issue. Before involving the customer or the employee's supervisor, the project
manager should meet with the employee in private to discuss the issue and gather facts before
deciding on a course of action.

---


**Details for Each Option:**

AError! Not a valid embedded object.Tell the team member not to make any further excuses
and get the job done or risk disciplinary action
Incorrect. The project manager is jumping to conclusions and accusing the team member of
making excuses before knowing all the facts. Perhaps the team member is telling the truth,
in which case the project manager will need to figure out a solution. Even if the project
manager's suspicions are correct and it is a performance issue on the employee's part, this
is best addressed by the project manager in a private meeting with the employee.
BError! Not a valid embedded object.Contact the customer right away to discuss the issue
Incorrect. The project manager should not jump to the step of involving the customer
before gathering all the facts. Otherwise, the project manager risks damaging their
relationship with the customer. Instead, the project manager should meet one-on-one with
the team member to discuss the issue, gather facts, and then decide on the appropriate
course of action.
CError! Not a valid embedded object.Schedule a one-on-one meeting with the team member
to discuss the issue and possible next steps
Correct. Project managers should aim to address issues with team members as early as
possible and in private, making a one-on-one meeting the best answer choice here. In doing
so, the project manager can gather more information from the employee to determine the
facts and decide on the best course of action.
DError! Not a valid embedded object.Escalate this issue to the team member's supervisor
Incorrect. Even when a project manager is not in a direct supervisory position over the
team members, project managers must exercise problem-solving and conflict management
skills as part of their project management responsibilities. Project managers should
address issues as early as possible and usually in private, using a direct, collaborative
approach. Only if this approach fails, or when formal disciplinary action is needed, should
the project manager resort to pulling rank.

**Reference:**

- **A Guide to the Project Management Body of Knowledge, (PMBOK® Guide) – Sixth Edition,**
Project Management Institute Inc., 2017, Page(s) 348
Live FeedbackTM Back to Results

PMP Exam 4
Filtered Mode: Displaying 200 questions
Question 154 of 200
Question ID: 613723
During project execution, some of the project team members are working in different cities. It
has come to the attention of the project manager that these team members are multitasking
during video conference calls and missing vital information. As a result, team cohesion is lacking
which has caused the project to fall behind schedule.
What tool or technique could the project manager use to address the issue and get the project
back on schedule?
AError! Not a valid embedded object.Colocation
BError! Not a valid embedded object.Virtual team
CError! Not a valid embedded object.Communication technology
DError! Not a valid embedded object.Cross-functional team
Question answered incorrectly

**Hint:**

What technique brings the team together to enhance face-to-face communication and team
cohesion?
Correct Answer: A

**Explanation:**

The problem described in the question requires a tool from the Develop Team process to
improve the team's productivity. Of the choices provided, only colocation would bring the team
together in order to improve team performance. Although colocation is not always possible, the
question does not provide enough information to determine if colocation is or is not practical.
Therefore it can not be assumed that colocation is impractical. More importantly, the other
choices are either not a tool or technique or would not result in improved team cohesion or
improved productivity.

---


**Details for Each Option:**

AError! Not a valid embedded object.Colocation
Correct. Colocation would bring the project team together in one physical location and
enhance the team members' ability to perform more productively as a team.
BError! Not a valid embedded object.Virtual team
Incorrect. The scenario described in the question implies the project team members are
currently organized as a virtual team and using video conferencing to interact. Bringing
the team members together in one physical location is the best way to address the issue.
CError! Not a valid embedded object.Communication technology
Incorrect. The project team is currently utilizing video conferencing as their primary
method of communication. Other than face-to-face communication, using another type of
communication technology is unlikely to make the team more cohesive and productive.
DError! Not a valid embedded object.Cross-functional team
Incorrect. A cross-functional team is a term borrowed from agile project management
which describes a team that includes practitioners with all the skills necessary to deliver
product increments. The problem presented in the question describes multitasking during
video conference rather than lack of particular skills required to deliver the product.
Therefore, making the team cross-functional is unlikely to resolve the issue.

**Reference:**

- **A Guide to the Project Management Body of Knowledge, (PMBOK® Guide) – Sixth Edition,**
Project Management Institute Inc., 2017, Page(s) 340

PMP Exam 4
Filtered Mode: Displaying 200 questions
Question 155 of 200
Question ID: 612579
As a project manager, you want to establish a culture of continuous improvement with your
project team, so you encourage the team to look for and implement small incremental
improvements in the development process.
Which of the following are you recommending to the team?
AError! Not a valid embedded object.Kaikaku
BError! Not a valid embedded object.Decomposition
CError! Not a valid embedded object.Ishikawa
DError! Not a valid embedded object.Kaizen
Question answered incorrectly

**Hint:**

The correct answer is the Japanese word for improvement.
Correct Answer: D

**Explanation:**

Kaizen is the Japanese word for improvement. A kaizen approach makes incremental change
through small steps, thereby establishing a process of continuous improvement. By applying
kaizen, a development team can optimize efficiency and quality. While the topic of this question
is only briefly mentioned in the PMBOK® Guide, the Project Management Professional (PMP)®
Examination Content Outline, June 2015, covers knowledge and skills with which PMP aspirants
are expected to be familiar. Continuous improvement processes are among these knowledge and
skills. Of the available choices, only the kaizen approach would establish a continuous
improvement process by encouraging the development team to look for and implement small
incremental improvements in the development process.

---


**Details for Each Option:**

AError! Not a valid embedded object.Kaikaku
Incorrect. Kaikaku is a Japanese word, which means radical change. While kaizen is
focused on incremental improvements, kaikaku is focused on radical improvements.
BError! Not a valid embedded object.Decomposition
Incorrect. Decomposition is a technique used for dividing and subdividing the project
scope and project deliverables into smaller, more manageable parts. Decomposition is a
technique that can be used to create the work breakdown structure (WBS) but is not related
to continuous improvement.
CError! Not a valid embedded object.Ishikawa
Incorrect. Cause-and-effect diagrams are also known as Ishikawa diagrams. This type of
diagram breaks down the causes of the problem statement identified into discrete branches.
This technique is helpful in identifying the main or root cause of an identified problem but
is not used for continuous improvement.
DError! Not a valid embedded object.Kaizen
Correct. Kaizen is the Japanese word for improvement. A kaizen approach makes
incremental change through small steps.

**Reference:**

- **A Guide to the Project Management Body of Knowledge, (PMBOK® Guide) – Sixth Edition,**
Project Management Institute Inc., 2017, Page(s) 310; see also
https://www.projectmanagement.com/articles/435560/Lean--Agile-and-Kaizen-in-Project-
Quality-Management

PMP Exam 4
Filtered Mode: Displaying 200 questions
Question 156 of 200
Question ID: 612363
The computer system is hit with a denial-of-service attack for the second time during a project,
and the development team is unable to continue working. The project manager immediately
reviews the recorded risk response plans and provides the risk owner with an update about this
recurring issue.
What else should the project manager do in this scenario?
AError! Not a valid embedded object.Examine the risk register
BError! Not a valid embedded object.Check the lessons learned matrix
CError! Not a valid embedded object.Review the risk management plan
DError! Not a valid embedded object.Research the lessons learned register
Question answered incorrectly

**Hint:**

The question indicates that a similar event occurred earlier in the project.
Correct Answer: D

**Explanation:**

The question indicates that a similar event occurred earlier in the project and also suggests that
this risk was identified and recorded in the risk register. The realized risk described by the
question should trigger the Implement Risk Responses process. One of the inputs of the
Implement Risk Responses process is the lessons learned register. The lessons learned earlier in
the project with regard to implementing risk responses can be used to improve the effectiveness
of the Implement Risk Responses process. It would be beneficial for the project manager to
review the lessons learned register to understand the effectiveness of the response in the previous
situation and update the response if and when necessary. Therefore, of the available choices,
researching the lessons learned register would be the best action to take in this scenario.

---


**Details for Each Option:**

AError! Not a valid embedded object.Examine the risk register
Incorrect. The question states that the project manager has reviewed the recorded risk
response plans which implies that the project manager has already read the risk register,
making this action redundant and unnecessary.
BError! Not a valid embedded object.Check the lessons learned matrix
Incorrect. 'Lessons learned matrix' is a fake term made up for this question. Prospective
PMP aspirants should keep in mind that not all terms thrown by the PMI onto their exam
will represent factual terminology used in project management or specified in the
PMBOK® Guide.
CError! Not a valid embedded object.Review the risk management plan
Incorrect. The risk management plan describes how risk management activities will be
structured and performed. Reviewing the risk register for the risk response plan is likely
one of the activities specified in the risk management plan to be performed when an
identified risk is realized. Based on the scenario provided, you have already reviewed the
risk register. Therefore, it is reasonable to assume that the project manager has already
reviewed the risk management plan.
DError! Not a valid embedded object.Research the lessons learned register
Correct. The question suggests that a similar event occurred earlier in the project. It would
be beneficial for the project manager to review the lessons learned register to understand
the effectiveness of the risk response implemented in the previous situation.

**Reference:**

- **A Guide to the Project Management Body of Knowledge, (PMBOK® Guide) – Sixth Edition,**
Project Management Institute Inc., 2017, Page(s) 450

Question 157 of 200
Question ID: 612490
- **A project manager is leading a product development project and is currently in the process of**
developing a plan for how the project costs will be planned, structured, and controlled.
Which of the following is least likely to be developed during this process and included in the
plan?
AError! Not a valid embedded object.The documented economic feasibility study which will be used to
help measure project success at the end of the project
BError! Not a valid embedded object.The units of measure for each resource used on the project such
as meters, liters, tons, kilometers, or cubic years for quantity measures
CError! Not a valid embedded object.The degree to which cost estimates will be rounded up or down,
based on the scope of the activities and magnitude of the project
DError! Not a valid embedded object.The acceptable range used in determining realistic cost estimates,
and, if applicable, an amount for contingencies
Question answered incorrectly

**Hint:**

Which answer choice describes an activity that is performed as part of the pre-project work?
Correct Answer: A

**Explanation:**

The project business case is a documented economic feasibility study used to establish the
validity of the benefits of a selected component lacking sufficient definition and that is used as a
basis for the authorization of further project management activities. The business case lists the
objectives and reasons for project initiation. It helps to measure the project success at the end of
the project against the project objectives. The question suggests that the cost management plan is
being developed which occurs during the Plan Cost Management process. The project business
case is developed during pre-project work and not the Plan Cost Management process. Units of
measure, level of precision, and level of accuracy are all established by the cost management

---

plan. Note, the question is asking which answer choice is 'least' likely to be developed during this
process. Hence, of the available choices, the business case is least likely to be developed during
the Plan Cost Management process and is, therefore, the best answer to the question asked.

**Details for Each Option:**

AError! Not a valid embedded object.The documented economic feasibility study which will
be used to help measure project success at the end of the project
Correct. This answer choice describes the project business case which is developed during
pre-project work and not the Plan Cost Management process as implied by the question.
BError! Not a valid embedded object.The units of measure for each resource used on the
project such as meters, liters, tons, kilometers, or cubic years for quantity measures
Incorrect. The question suggests that the cost management plan is being developed. Units
of measure are established in the cost management plan.
CError! Not a valid embedded object.The degree to which cost estimates will be rounded up
or down, based on the scope of the activities and magnitude of the project
Incorrect. This answer choice describes the level of precision which will be used for the
cost estimates. The level of precision is established in the cost management plan, as implied
by the question.
DError! Not a valid embedded object.The acceptable range used in determining realistic cost
estimates, and, if applicable, an amount for contingencies
Incorrect. The question suggests that the Plan Cost Management process is being
performed with the development of the cost management plan. The level of accuracy is
established as part of the cost management plan.

Question ID: 613127
- **A new project manager takes over a project and holds a team meeting to introduce himself and**

independently, and that he will allow the team to make their own decisions and establish their
own goals.
What leadership style does the project manager demonstrate?
AError! Not a valid embedded object.Service-oriented
BError! Not a valid embedded object.Avoiding
CError! Not a valid embedded object.Referent
DError! Not a valid embedded object.Laissez-faire
Question answered incorrectly

**Hint:**

Which of the available choices is a hands-off leadership style?
Correct Answer: D

**Explanation:**

Of the available choices, only laissez-faire is a leadership style. Laissez-faire is a leadership style
characterized by allowing the team to make their own decisions and establish their own goals. It
is also referred to as a hands-off approach.

AError! Not a valid embedded object.Service-oriented

---

Incorrect. Service-oriented is a personality characteristic and not a leadership style.
BError! Not a valid embedded object.Avoiding
Incorrect. Avoiding is a form of power as opposed to a leadership style.
CError! Not a valid embedded object.Referent
Incorrect. Referent is a form of power rather than a leadership style.
DError! Not a valid embedded object.Laissez-faire
Correct. Laissez-faire is a leadership style characterized by allowing the team to make
their own decisions and establish their own goals.

PMP Exam 4
Filtered Mode: Displaying 200 questions
Question 159 of 200
Question ID: 613202
- **A project manager is assigned to a project that involves many vendors. During project execution,**
business priorities shift, and the sponsor informs the project manager that the project needs to be
terminated.
What should the project manager do first?
AError! Not a valid embedded object.Allow the vendors to complete their work since there is a legally
binding contract
BError! Not a valid embedded object.Reject all vendors' deliverables to avoid paying for something that
is no longer needed
CError! Not a valid embedded object.Notify the vendors that the project has been terminated
DError! Not a valid embedded object.Begin the Close Procurements process
Question answered incorrectly

**Hint:**

Which answer choice represents the most reasonable action that should be taken when a project
that involves vendors is terminated prematurely?
Correct Answer: C

**Explanation:**

The question states that a project has been terminated during project execution. Regardless of the
fact that the project has been terminated prematurely, the activities that are associated with the
Control Procurements process and Close Project or Phase process still need to be performed. The
project manager, or an authorized procurement administrator, provides the seller with formal
written notice that the contract has been completed, or in this case, terminated prematurely.
Notifying the vendors that the project was terminated is consistent with the project manager
engaging all the proper stakeholders in the process. The actual termination procedure(s) will be
specified in the terms and conditions of the contracts signed with each vendor.

---


**Details for Each Option:**

AError! Not a valid embedded object.Allow the vendors to complete their work since there is
a legally binding contract
Incorrect. The terms and conditions of the contract should provide guidance on legal
obligations in the event the project is terminated prematurely. Even if the performing
organization decided to allow some or all of the vendors to finish their work, it would be a
business decision and not just because of the existence of a contract. Since the contents of
the termination clause are unknown from the scenario, it is not clear if the vendors should
be allowed to complete their work.
BError! Not a valid embedded object.Reject all vendors' deliverables to avoid paying for
something that is no longer needed
Incorrect. Rejecting deliverables for the sole purpose of avoiding payment for work that
has been completed but no longer needed would violate the spirit if not the letter of the
contract. Additionally, such action would conflict with the aspirational standard of honesty
as covered in the PMI Code of Ethics and Professional Conduct. The terms and conditions
of the contract (which are unknown from the scenario) should provide guidance on legal
obligations in the event the project is terminated early.
CError! Not a valid embedded object.Notify the vendors that the project has been terminated
Correct. During the Control Procurements process, notifying the vendors that the project
was terminated is consistent with the best project management practices. Later on, as part
of the Close Project or Phase process, the reasons for any action taken when a project is
terminated before completion should be investigated and documented.
DError! Not a valid embedded object.Begin the Close Procurements process
Incorrect. Close Procurements is not a process specified in the PMBOK® Guide.

**Reference:**

- **A Guide to the Project Management Body of Knowledge, (PMBOK® Guide) – Sixth Edition,**
Project Management Institute Inc., 2017, Page(s) 499, 123, 128, 489, 542
Live FeedbackTM Back to Results

PMP Exam 4
Filtered Mode: Displaying 200 questions
Question 160 of 200
Question ID: 612087
- **A project manager is in the process of implementing the communications management plan for a**
project to construct a new hydroelectric plant. The performing organization is based in the
United States, and the hydroelectric plant will be built in a remote region of Brazil.
As it relates to project communications, which of the following tailoring considerations is the
least relevant?
AError! Not a valid embedded object.Physical location
BError! Not a valid embedded object.Language
CError! Not a valid embedded object.Communication technology
DError! Not a valid embedded object.Policy compliance and auditing
Question answered incorrectly

**Hint:**

Which answer choice represents a tailoring consideration that is more typically associated with
the Project Quality Management processes?
Correct Answer: D

**Explanation:**

The question suggests that the project manager is conducting the Manage Communications by
implementing the communications management plan. All but one of the answer choices
represent tailoring considerations associated with the communications management processes.
Keep in mind that the question is asking which of the provided options is 'least' relevant to
tailoring considerations for communications management. Policy compliance and auditing
represents a tailoring consideration more typically associated with the Project Quality
Management processes rather than Project Communications Management. Therefore, policy
compliance and auditing is 'least' relevant to the tailoring considerations of the communications
management processes. The incorrect answer choices represent tailoring considerations which
are important to managing communications between locations where different languages are

---

typically spoken.

**Details for Each Option:**

AError! Not a valid embedded object.Physical location
Incorrect. The significant distance between the performing organization and the project
location must be a consideration for the project. Will the project team be co-located at the
project site or will some team members be located at the performing organization's
corporate office necessitating the use of a virtual team? How will the different time zones
affect virtual meetings or other communications?
BError! Not a valid embedded object.Language
Incorrect. There is likely to be a language barrier among stakeholders between the English
and Portuguese languages. Will the project require the use of translators? Will project
documents need to be recorded in multiple languages?
CError! Not a valid embedded object.Communication technology
Incorrect. Communications technology may be a factor as the hydroelectric plant is located
in a remote region. Is cellular service available or will satellite phones be required? How
will data be transmitted between the project site and the performing organization's
corporate office?
DError! Not a valid embedded object.Policy compliance and auditing
Correct. Policy compliance and auditing represents a tailoring consideration more
typically associated with the Project Quality Management processes rather than the
Project Communications Management processes.

- **A Guide to the Project Management Body of Knowledge, (PMBOK® Guide) – Sixth Edition,**
Project Management Institute Inc., 2017, Page(s) 365

PMP Exam 4
Filtered Mode: Displaying 200 questions
Question 161 of 200
Question ID: 613050
An organization has initiated a large project. As the project manager completes the Identify
Stakeholder process, the sponsor informs the project manager that the project charter is
approved.
What should the project manager do next?
AError! Not a valid embedded object.Develop a project schedule network diagram
BError! Not a valid embedded object.Hold a project kick-off meeting
CError! Not a valid embedded object.Inform stakeholders of the approved project charter
DError! Not a valid embedded object.Hold a bidder conference
Question answered incorrectly

**Hint:**

Keep stakeholders apprised of project status.
Correct Answer: C

**Explanation:**

Task 8 of Domain I in the Project Management Professional (PMP)® Examination Content
Outline reads, "Inform stakeholders of the approved project charter to ensure a common
understanding of the key deliverables, milestones, and their roles and responsibilities." The
question states the project charter has been approved while the project manager completes the
Identify Stakeholders process. The next logical step would be informing the identified
stakeholders of the approved project charter. By doing this, all those involved with the project
will be aware that the project is proceeding and understand the key deliverables, milestones, and
their roles and responsibilities. It is important for the prospective PMP aspirants to be familiar
with the Examination Content Outline because the PMBOK® Guide is not the only source used
by the Project Management Institute (PMI)® to design their questions.

---


**Details for Each Option:**

AError! Not a valid embedded object.Develop a project schedule network diagram
Incorrect. A project schedule network diagram is a graphical representation of the logical
relationships among the project schedule activities. The diagram is an output of the
Sequence Activities process, which belongs to the Planning Process Group, while the
scenario implies the project is in initiation.
BError! Not a valid embedded object.Hold a project kick-off meeting
Incorrect. Typically, for large projects (as the one described in the scenario), kick-off
meetings take place at the end of planning and the start of executing. Since the project
manager has just completed the Identify Stakeholders process in the Initiating Process
Group, having a kick-off meeting would be premature, making this answer incorrect. Note,
while it is true that kick-off meetings typically occur with the end of planning and the start
of executing, for small projects, where there is one team performing both the project
planning and execution, the kick-off meeting often takes place after initiation as the first
action that begins the Planning Process Group.
CError! Not a valid embedded object.Inform stakeholders of the approved project charter
Correct. The approved project charter formally authorizes the existence of a project and
provides the project manager with the authority to use company resources. The project
charter includes high-level information, such as project objectives, milestones, and the
roles and responsibilities of key stakeholders and its approval should be communicated to
all the stakeholders before project planning starts, making this choice the best answer to
the question asked.
DError! Not a valid embedded object.Hold a bidder conference
Incorrect. A bidder conference is a meeting between the buyer and prospective sellers that
is held prior to proposal submittal. According to the scenario, the project is in initiation.
Bidder conferences are typically conducted during project execution.

**Reference:**

- **A Guide to the Project Management Body of Knowledge, (PMBOK® Guide) – Sixth Edition,**
Project Management Institute Inc., 2017, Page(s) 53, 81, 561; see also Project Management
Professional (PMP)® Examination Content Outline, Project Management Institute Inc., June
2015, Domain 1, Task 8

PMP Exam 4
Filtered Mode: Displaying 200 questions
Question 162 of 200
Question ID: 612228
You are leading a project to build drones capable of flying at ultra-high altitudes. One day during
project execution, your technical lead informs you that they went ahead and made a change to
the drone's navigation system, making the drone capable of flying faster and higher. You check
project documents but find no evidence of this new capability.
What should you do immediately?
AError! Not a valid embedded object.Inform the project sponsor of the new flight capabilities
BError! Not a valid embedded object.Update the project development approach to better manage
changes
CError! Not a valid embedded object.Record the change in the change log
DError! Not a valid embedded object.Recommend that the technical lead will be rewarded for their
effort
Question answered incorrectly

**Hint:**

Your technical lead has just introduced updates to a critical component of the product; you
should make a note.
Correct Answer: C

**Explanation:**

When changes are made on a project, they must be in consideration of a range of factors such as
project scope, schedule, cost, quality, risk, etc. As part of the Perform Integrated Change Control
process, all changes, whether approved, denied, or postponed, must be recorded in the change
log. This document serves as a repository for changes that have occurred during the project or
phase, as well as their current status. According to the scenario, you (as the project manager)
checked project documents but found no evidence of the new capability, implying the technical
lead did not apply the proper change management process while implementing the change.
Therefore, to avoid any further discrepancies on the project resulting from this undocumented

---

change, the first immediate step to take is to record the change in the change log for tracking and
follow-up. Actions described in other answer choices represent plausible options; however, they
could be taken only after the change is documented.
Note, the scenario describes gold plating or scope creep, a practice that should be avoided.

**Details for Each Option:**

AError! Not a valid embedded object.Inform the project sponsor of the new flight capabilities
Incorrect. This answer choice is incorrect because it does not address the main issue of the
question, which is the fact that the change introduced by the technical lead has not been
documented. One of the primary responsibilities of a project manager is to have and
maintain control over the Perform Integrated Change Control process. Simply going to the
sponsor and informing them of new flight capabilities would disregard the fact an
unauthorized change has been implemented. Doing so could undermine the credibility of
the project manager, no matter if the change was positive or not. As such, this is not the
best answer choice of those provided.
BError! Not a valid embedded object.Update the project development approach to better
manage changes
Incorrect. Immediately updating or switching the development approach should not be
taken to better manage changes that occur on a project. This is because the project
development approach is an additional component of the project management plan that
describes the product, service, or result development approach. These include predictive,
iterative, agile, or hybrid-based approaches. As part of the project management plan,
which is a controlled document, the project development approach cannot be updated at-
will by the project manager.
CError! Not a valid embedded object.Record the change in the change log
Correct. The technical lead has altered a critical component of the product, and this needs
to be documented immediately. By doing so, a record of the changes that have occurred on
the project is maintained. This allows a project manager to better track and follow-up on
the results of changes as the project moves through execution towards completion.
Moreover, recording the change in the change log helps to emphasize and convey to the
team the necessity for proper change control on a project. Despite what may appear to be
positive effects from an unauthorized change given in the scenario, a change control
process is mandatory for every project. Without it, scope creep, or the uncontrolled
expansion of product or project scope without adjustments to time, cost, and resources is
likely to occur.
DError! Not a valid embedded object.Recommend that the technical lead will be rewarded for

---

their effort
Incorrect. Instead of rewarding the technical lead for their effort, it is likely that the
technical lead should be reprimanded for implementing an unauthorized change and
reminded of the importance of the change control process.

**Reference:**

- **A Guide to the Project Management Body of Knowledge, (PMBOK® Guide) – Sixth Edition,**
Project Management Institute Inc., 2017, Page(s) 120
Live FeedbackTM Back to Results

PMP Exam 4
Filtered Mode: Displaying 200 questions
Question 163 of 200
Question ID: 613211
An executive steering committee meeting is scheduled for tomorrow, and you are required to
make a presentation about your project's progress.
Which of the following presentation formats is best used in this type of meeting?
AError! Not a valid embedded object.Detailed Gantt bar chart
BError! Not a valid embedded object.Project schedule network diagram
CError! Not a valid embedded object.Master schedule of milestones
DError! Not a valid embedded object.Hammock activity summary chart
Question answered incorrectly

**Hint:**

In management meetings, you are looking for a chart that gives a high-level overview.
Correct Answer: C

**Explanation:**

Milestone charts, also known as master schedules, are regarded as an effective way to
communicate project progress to senior executives. When reporting on a project in progress, the
milestone chart includes a line often called a data date, or the point in time when the status of the
project is recorded. To help executives and key stakeholders make decisions about the project,
the milestone charts provide just enough detail about major deliverables and key handoffs among
operational departments or external organizations.

**Details for Each Option:**

AError! Not a valid embedded object.Detailed Gantt bar chart

---

Incorrect. Henry Gantt invented a bar chart of schedule information, listing activities on
the vertical axis, showing dates on the horizontal axis, and activity durations as horizontal
bars placed according to start and finish dates. Modern Gantt charts show the dependency
relationships between activities and current schedule status with arrows. The Gantt chart
shows too much technical detail for an executive or key stakeholder presentation.
BError! Not a valid embedded object.Project schedule network diagram
Incorrect. A project schedule network diagram is used by both the precedence
diagramming method and the critical path method to develop a viable schedule. It displays
the milestones at the beginning and end, all the activities and diverging paths, the logical
relationships, durations, start and end days, and float. However, the project schedule
network has far too much technical detail for an executive or key stakeholder presentation.
CError! Not a valid embedded object.Master schedule of milestones
Correct. The summary form of the project schedule's milestones is often called the master
schedule or milestone schedule. This summary level of detail is most suitable for executives
and key stakeholders who are more concerned about the scheduled start or completion of
major deliverables and key external interfaces.
DError! Not a valid embedded object.Hammock activity summary chart
Incorrect. A comprehensive summary activity, which is sometimes called a hammock
activity, may be used in schedule bar chart reports. The hammock represents a series of
activities between milestones or across multiple interdependent work packages. Bar chart
schedule models may use hammock activities for the purpose of control and management
communications. However, 'hammock activity summary chart' is a made-up term.

**Reference:**

- **A Guide to the Project Management Body of Knowledge, (PMBOK® Guide) – Sixth Edition,**
Project Management Institute Inc., 2017, Page(s) 217-219

PMP Exam 4
Filtered Mode: Displaying 200 questions
Question 164 of 200
Question ID: 612419
- **A project manager is leading a new product development project. During project execution, the**
competitive advantage of this new product is threatened when another company is first to market
with a similar product. This risk had been identified during initial planning and placed on a
watch list.
What should the project manager do next?
AError! Not a valid embedded object.Analyze the impact of the risk on the project objectives
BError! Not a valid embedded object.Risks on the watch list do not have planned responses and can be
ignored
CError! Not a valid embedded object.Apply the contingency response plan developed for this risk
DError! Not a valid embedded object.Terminate the project since the competitive advantage has been
lost
Question answered incorrectly

**Hint:**

Risks placed on the watch list do not have an associated risk response plan.
Correct Answer: A

**Explanation:**

The question implies that the project manager needs to perform the Implement Risk Response
process for an identified risk that has been placed on the watch list. The risk register may include
a watch list for low priority risks or risks, which require further analysis. While the competitive
threat may be considered a high-priority risk or a risk requiring a prompt analysis and
appropriate response plan, the scenario suggests this risk was placed on the watch list (for
reasons not specified in the question text). A response plan is not developed for risks placed on
the watch list; rather these risks are just monitored throughout the project. In case their potential
impact on the project changes, further analysis is required to develop a risk response. Since an
identified project risk has occurred in this scenario, and there is no response planned for this risk,

---

the most logical next step for the project manager is, among the available choices, to analyze the
impact of this risk to the project objectives to determine the best course of action.

**Details for Each Option:**

AError! Not a valid embedded object.Analyze the impact of the risk on the project objectives
Correct. Risks placed on the watch list do not have an associated risk response plan. Since
an identified project risk has occurred without an agreed-upon response plan, the most
logical next step for the project manager is to analyze the impact of this risk on the project
objectives to determine the best course of action.
BError! Not a valid embedded object.Risks on the watch list do not have planned responses
and can be ignored
Incorrect. While it is true that risks placed on the watch list do not have planned responses,
these risks cannot simply be ignored. When a risk is realized, a risk analysis should be
conducted to understand the impact of the risk in order to determine the best course of
action.
CError! Not a valid embedded object.Apply the contingency response plan developed for this
risk
Incorrect. Risks placed on the watch list do not have responses developed. Instead, these
risks are just monitored throughout the project. When their potential impact on the project
changes, further analysis is required to develop a risk response.
DError! Not a valid embedded object.Terminate the project since the competitive advantage
has been lost
Incorrect. It would be premature to terminate the project solely on the basis that another
company has introduced a competing product. If an adequate response cannot be
developed for the risk, further analysis of the situation should be done and appropriate
actions taken (including a possibility of terminating the project).

**Reference:**

- **A Guide to the Project Management Body of Knowledge, (PMBOK® Guide) – Sixth Edition,**
Project Management Institute Inc., 2017, Page(s) 427, 440, 450; see also
https://www.pmi.org/learning/library/project-risk-management-success-tool-6078

Question 165 of 200
Question ID: 612178
You are planning a highway construction project, and you have just completed the development
of the quality management plan. Your organization requires that the project management office
(PMO) review and approve all components of project management plans. You submit the quality
management plan to the PMO for review, and a few days later they indicate that an element was
missing.
What element of the quality management plan might you have most likely missed?
AError! Not a valid embedded object.Release and iteration length
BError! Not a valid embedded object.High-level project description, boundaries, and key deliverables
CError! Not a valid embedded object.Process that specifies how formal acceptance of the completed
project deliverables will be obtained
DError! Not a valid embedded object.Procedures that deal with nonconformance, corrective actions
procedures, and continuous improvement procedures
Question answered incorrectly

**Hint:**

The quality management plan is an output of the Plan Quality Management process.
Correct Answer: D

**Explanation:**

Major procedures relevant to the project, such as dealing with nonconformance, corrective
actions procedures, and continuous improvement procedures are included in the quality
management plan. The other options are elements of other project documents including the
schedule management plan, scope management plan, and project charter.

---


**Details for Each Option:**

AError! Not a valid embedded object.Release and iteration length
Incorrect. The release and iteration length are specified in the schedule management plan
as opposed to the quality management plan.
BError! Not a valid embedded object.High-level project description, boundaries, and key
deliverables
Incorrect. High-level project description, boundaries, and key deliverables are captured in
the project charter and not the quality management plan.
CError! Not a valid embedded object.Process that specifies how formal acceptance of the
completed project deliverables will be obtained
Incorrect. The process that specifies how formal acceptance of the completed project
deliverables will be obtained is part of the scope management plan rather than the quality
management plan.
DError! Not a valid embedded object.Procedures that deal with nonconformance, corrective
actions procedures, and continuous improvement procedures
Correct. Major procedures relevant to the project, such as dealing with nonconformance,
corrective actions procedures, and continuous improvement procedures are included in the
quality management plan.

Question 166 of 200
Question ID: 612298
You are leading a multi-phase project.
What should you do at the end of each phase?
AError! Not a valid embedded object.Monitor stakeholder engagement
BError! Not a valid embedded object.Transfer ownership of the deliverables
CError! Not a valid embedded object.Verify the deliverables
DError! Not a valid embedded object.Update business documents
Question answered incorrectly

**Hint:**

What process group is described in the scenario?
Correct Answer: B

**Explanation:**

Transferring ownership of the deliverables is an action that must be done at the end of each
phase and at the end of the project; otherwise, the benefits of the project would not be realized.
Typically, a project's product, service, or result is transferred to the next phase of the project or to
production and/or operations.

**Details for Each Option:**

AError! Not a valid embedded object.Monitor stakeholder engagement
Incorrect. Monitoring the engagement of stakeholders is done as part of the Monitor
Stakeholder Engagement process and is performed in the Monitoring and Controlling
Process Group, while the question is asking what should be done at the end of each phase,

---

implying to select an activity performed in a Close Project or Phase process.
BError! Not a valid embedded object.Transfer ownership of the deliverables
Correct. Transferring ownership of deliverables to the assigned stakeholders according to
the project management plan facilitates project closure. At the end of each phase, the
project manager should ensure the output is handed over to the responsible party of the
next phase, making this choice the best answer to the question asked.
CError! Not a valid embedded object.Verify the deliverables
Incorrect. Verified deliverables are an output of the Control Quality process, but the
question asks what should be done at the end of each phase, implying to select an activity
performed in the Close Project or Phase process, making this choice an incorrect answer.
DError! Not a valid embedded object.Update business documents
Incorrect. Business documents, such as the business case and the benefits management
plan, are an input to the Close Project or Phase process and used to determine whether the
expected outcomes from the economic feasibility study used to justify the project or phase
occurred and whether the benefits of the project or phase were achieved as planned.
However, these documents are not updated at the end of each phase.

**Reference:**

- **A Guide to the Project Management Body of Knowledge, (PMBOK® Guide) – Sixth Edition,**
Project Management Institute Inc., 2017, Page(s) 123

PMP Exam 4
Filtered Mode: Displaying 200 questions
Question 167 of 200
Question ID: 610049
As a project execution begins, high winds prevent a team from installing the windows as
scheduled. These weather conditions were accounted for in planning, but no one anticipated that
the speed of the wind would be that strong.
What tool or technique would the project manager use to determine if he will be able to complete
the project according to the project management plan?
AError! Not a valid embedded object.Quality audit
BError! Not a valid embedded object.Reserve analysis
CError! Not a valid embedded object.Pareto diagram
DError! Not a valid embedded object.Tornado diagram
Question answered incorrectly

**Hint:**

Consider the difference between tools or techniques that help identify, analyze, and monitor
project risks.
Correct Answer: B

**Explanation:**

The scenario implies the project manager is performing the Monitor Risks process. Reserve
analysis is among the tools and techniques of this process and can be used to assess project risk
contingency reserves that will be used to alleviate the impact of identified risks in a project such
as a schedule estimate uncertainty or any other identified project risk. Reserve analysis allows
the project team to ensure that proper contingencies are available to mitigate or address risks
identified during the project's planning or execution. In this case, the project manager would
perform a reserve analysis to determine if there is sufficient "reserve" in the project schedule to
accommodate the delays due to the high winds.

---


**Details for Each Option:**

AError! Not a valid embedded object.Quality audit
Incorrect. A quality audit, which is typically used in the Manage Quality process, is a
structured independent process to determine if project activities comply with
organizational and project policies, processes, and procedures. While the results of the
quality audit may and often do help to identify project risks, they are not a technique that is
used to assess contingency reserves, which is required in this case.
BError! Not a valid embedded object.Reserve analysis
Correct. Reserve analysis determines if adequate reserves have been set aside to address
identified risks as well as uncertainty in schedule duration, budget, estimated cost or funds
for the project. Reserve analysis ensures that the proper amount of contingency reserves
are available to address risk in a project. The project manager conducts a reserve analysis
to see if the plan's schedule reserve (i.e., contingency reserve) is adequate to sustain the
schedule delays at the rate his team is experiencing high winds.
CError! Not a valid embedded object.Pareto diagram
Incorrect. A Pareto diagram is a special form of a histogram or vertical bar chart, which is
used primarily to display the frequency or consequences of defects that are determined
during the Control Quality process. It is not a technique that is used to assess contingency
reserves but instead a tool to identify the likely source of issues that have occurred.
DError! Not a valid embedded object.Tornado diagram
Incorrect. A tornado diagram is used in a sensitivity analysis to characterize a number of
risks and to determine which risk is likely to have the greatest impact or to assess the
impact of variables that have a high degree of uncertainty and compare them to other
variables, which are more stable. A tornado diagram is used in the analysis of identified
risks and is not a tool or technique in assessing contingency reserves.

**Reference:**

- **A Guide to the Project Management Body of Knowledge, (PMBOK® Guide) – Sixth Edition,**
Project Management Institute Inc., 2017, Page(s) 456, 202
Live FeedbackTM Back to Results
Prev Next

PMP Exam 4
Filtered Mode: Displaying 200 questions
Question 168 of 200
Question ID: 610085
During a presentation to your project sponsor, you mention the code of accounts. She is
unfamiliar with the term and asks for clarification.
Which of the following would you use to explain the code of accounts?
AError! Not a valid embedded object.Risk breakdown structure
BError! Not a valid embedded object.Project budget
CError! Not a valid embedded object.Work breakdown structure
DError! Not a valid embedded object.Risk register
Question answered incorrectly

**Hint:**

Your sponsor needs to know what helps identify work packages in an organized and numerical
fashion.
Correct Answer: C

**Explanation:**

- **A code of accounts is a numbering system that is used to uniquely identify each component of a**
work breakdown structure (WBS), which in turn helps to better monitor and control the project.
- **A code of accounts assigned to work packages in a WBS may also be linked to an organization’s**
accounting department to help the team track and report the actual costs of work package to their
planned costs.

**Details for Each Option:**

AError! Not a valid embedded object.Risk breakdown structure

---

Incorrect. A risk breakdown structure (RBS) is a hierarchical representation of potential
sources of risk for the project. An RBS is used to help a project team consider the full range
of sources from which individual project risks may arise but typically does not contain a
code of accounts.
BError! Not a valid embedded object.Project budget
Incorrect. The project budget is the approved cost estimate for the project and is created as
part of the Determine Budget process. Most often, a project budget is created by
aggregating the costs of all activities, work packages, control accounts, any contingency
reserves, and any management reserves without the use of a code of accounts.
CError! Not a valid embedded object.Work breakdown structure
Correct. A code of accounts is a numbering system that is used to uniquely identify each
component of a work breakdown structure (WBS), which in turn helps to better monitor and
control the project. The WBS and its code of accounts are developed during the Create
WBS process and are used frequently throughout the project life cycle.
DError! Not a valid embedded object.Risk register
Incorrect. A risk register is an output of the Identify Risks process. It contains information
such as a list of identified risks, a list of risk responses, and the risk owners responsible for
implementing risk responses. Although a risk register may contain additional information
such as risk title, risk category, and current risk status, a risk register typically not contain
a code of accounts.

**Reference:**

- **A Guide to the Project Management Body of Knowledge, (PMBOK® Guide) – Sixth Edition,**
Project Management Institute Inc., 2017, Page(s) 161-162, 701

Question 169 of 200
Question ID: 613710
- **A project manager has just been informed that critical materials are on back order, which**
threatens the project's deadline. After investigating the problem, the project manager decides that
escalating the issue internally is the best solution.
The escalation procedure is an example of what part of the project management framework?
AError! Not a valid embedded object.Requirements management
BError! Not a valid embedded object.Enterprise environmental factors
CError! Not a valid embedded object.Change management
DError! Not a valid embedded object.Organizational process assets
Question answered incorrectly

**Hint:**

Procedures, policies, and, processes that are specific to an organization are known as what?
Correct Answer: D

**Explanation:**

The project manager in this scenario chose to escalate the issue internally as the solution to the
problem of the back ordered materials. Each organization would have their own escalation
policies and procedures in their organizational process assets.

**Details for Each Option:**

AError! Not a valid embedded object.Requirements management
Incorrect. Requirements management refers to the process by which project and product

---

requirements are analyzed, documented, and managed.
BError! Not a valid embedded object.Enterprise environmental factors
Incorrect. Enterprise environmental factors are conditions, not under the immediate
control of the team, which influence the project. This question is asking about an escalation
procedure which is typically part of the organizational process assets that can be updated
throughout the project lifecycle, i.e., an action that is under the control of the project team
making this an incorrect choice.
CError! Not a valid embedded object.Change management
Incorrect. Change management refers to the change control system for a project and does
not address escalation procedures.
DError! Not a valid embedded object.Organizational process assets
Correct. Organizational process assets include procedures, policies, and plans that are
specific to the performing organization. An internal escalation procedure is an example of
an organizational process asset.
