PMP Exam 4
Filtered Mode: Displaying 200 questions
Question 193 of 200
Question ID: 610089
After a change request to expand the scope of the project has been submitted to the change
control board (CCB), the project manager is reassigned to another project. The CCB approves
the change and communicates the status of the change request to the newly hired project
manager.
What should the new project manager do first?
AError! Not a valid embedded object.Direct the project team to implement the change
BError! Not a valid embedded object.Wait for further changes and implement them all together
CError! Not a valid embedded object.Consult the change management plan
DError! Not a valid embedded object.Update the lessons learned register
Question answered incorrectly

**Hint:**

What governs the way changes are managed?
Correct Answer: C

**Explanation:**

All proposed changes to a project must be handled according to the organization's change control
process via a change request. In this scenario, a change request to expand the scope of the project
was submitted to the change control board for review and analysis of its impact on the project.
Once approved, the status of the change request is updated in the change log. The next logical
step would be implementing the change. However, the scenario describes a new project manager
who is likely not familiar with the change control processes defined for this particular project.
One should look for the answer choice that best addresses the question asked under the
circumstances provided in the scenario. If consulting the change management plan was not
among the answer choices, then directing the project team to implement the change would have
been the best answer. However, since each organization and each project within the organization
may have its own change control process (which is specified in the change management plan),

---

consulting this plan should be the first thing the newly assigned project manager should do. For
example, the change management plan may require the project manager to inform particular
stakeholders about the approved change so that they may take actions assigned to them as part of
the procedure prior to the implementation of the change. Therefore, in this case, consulting the
change management plan is the best answer among the choices given in the situation described
by the scenario.

**Details for Each Option:**

AError! Not a valid embedded object.Direct the project team to implement the change
Incorrect. Eventually, the approved change should be implemented. However, among the
choices provided, directing the project team to implement the change is not the first thing
for the project manager to do. There is another answer choice that more accurately
addresses the question asked.
BError! Not a valid embedded object.Wait for further changes and implement them all
together
Incorrect. When a change request is approved, project resources are allocated to support
the implementation of the change. Waiting for further changes (that may or may not be
requested) would be wasting the allocated resources that otherwise could have been used
for other project activities or re-allocated to other projects.
CError! Not a valid embedded object.Consult the change management plan
Correct. Typically, once the change is approved, it should be implemented. However, each
organization and each project within the organization has an established procedure to
manage changes as outlined in the change management plan. Therefore, of the choices
offered, consulting the change management plan is what the project manager should do
first.
DError! Not a valid embedded object.Update the lessons learned register
Incorrect. The lessons learned register is a project document used to record knowledge
gained during a project so that it can be used in the current project and entered into the
lessons learned repository to be used on future projects. While updating the lessons learned
register is an ongoing activity that should be carried out continuously throughout the
project life cycle, there is nothing in the question to suggest that any specific lessons have
been learned from the situation described in the scenario.

**Reference:**

- **A Guide to the Project Management Body of Knowledge, (PMBOK® Guide) – Sixth Edition,**

---

Project Management Institute Inc., 2017, Page(s) 115-116

PMP Exam Simulator
PMP Exam 4
Filtered Mode: Displaying 200 questions
Question 194 of 200
Question ID: 612477
- **A project manager and team are creating the work breakdown structure (WBS) for a project. The**
project charter indicates that the project will take approximately seven years to complete. Since
some of the deliverables will not be produced until far into the future, the project team has
determined that further decomposition is not possible at this point for many of the
subcomponents.
How should the project team resolve this situation?
AError! Not a valid embedded object.Seek the advice of someone that has worked on similar projects in
the past
BError! Not a valid embedded object.Perform a product analysis to decompose the work packages into
activities
CError! Not a valid embedded object.Divide and then subdivide the project scope and project
deliverables into smaller, more manageable parts
DError! Not a valid embedded object.Employ rolling wave planning as a way to move forward with
project planning
Question answered incorrectly

**Hint:**

What technique can be used to plan near-term work in detail, while the work in the future is
planned at a higher level?
Correct Answer: D

**Explanation:**

Rolling wave planning is an iterative planning technique in which the work to be accomplished
in the near term is planned in detail, while the work in the future is planned at a higher level.

---

Rolling wave planning is a form of progressive elaboration applicable to work packages,
planning packages, and release planning when using an agile or waterfall approach. Work can
exist at various levels of detail depending on where it is in the project life cycle. During early
strategic planning when information is less defined, work packages may be decomposed to the
known level of detail. As more is known about the upcoming events in the near term, work
packages can be decomposed into activities. Of the available choices, rolling wave planning is
the best technique to use to address the issue raised by the question.

**Details for Each Option:**

AError! Not a valid embedded object.Seek the advice of someone that has worked on similar
projects in the past
Incorrect. This answer choice represents a form of expert judgment. Expertise should be
considered from individuals or groups with knowledge of or experience with similar
projects. However, the question states that further decomposition is not possible at this
point in the project, therefore, it is unlikely that expert judgment will overcome the problem
described by the question.
BError! Not a valid embedded object.Perform a product analysis to decompose the work
packages into activities
Incorrect. Product analysis is a technique that can be used to define products and services.
Product analysis is not a technique that is used in the creation of the work breakdown
structure (WBS) and, therefore, would not permit further decomposition.
CError! Not a valid embedded object.Divide and then subdivide the project scope and project
deliverables into smaller, more manageable parts
Incorrect. This answer choice represents the definition of decomposition. The question
states that further decomposition is not possible at this point in the project. Therefore,
decomposition cannot be used to break down the WBS further.
DError! Not a valid embedded object.Employ rolling wave planning as a way to move
forward with project planning
Correct. Decomposition may not be possible for a deliverable or subcomponent that will be
accomplished far into the future. The project management team usually waits until the
deliverable or subcomponent is agreed on, so the details of the work breakdown structure
(WBS) can be developed. This technique is sometimes referred to as rolling wave planning.

**Reference:**

- **A Guide to the Project Management Body of Knowledge, (PMBOK® Guide) – Sixth Edition,**

---

Project Management Institute Inc., 2017, Page(s) 185, 160
Live FeedbackTM Back to Results

PMP Exam 4

Question 195 of 200
Question ID: 610013
The sponsor asks the project manager for the project's resource breakdown structure (RBS) so
that she can present it to senior management during an upcoming meeting. All the subsidiary
management plans are complete, but the RBS is not yet developed.
Which process must be completed in order to produce the RBS for the sponsor?
AError! Not a valid embedded object.Plan Resource Management
BError! Not a valid embedded object.Estimate Activity Resources
CError! Not a valid embedded object.Develop Project Management Plan
DError! Not a valid embedded object.Acquire Resources
Question answered incorrectly

**Hint:**

In what process do you determine the personnel and equipment required to create the
deliverables?
Correct Answer: B

**Explanation:**

Estimate Activity Resources is a process of estimating team resources and the type and quantities
of materials, equipment, and supplies necessary to perform project work. The resource
breakdown structure (RBS) is one of the outputs of this process. The RBS is a hierarchical
representation of resources by category and type. One of the approaches to answering questions
on the PMP exam is elimination. The incorrect answer choices can be eliminated for the reasons
provided in their respective explanations. Of the choices provided, only Estimate Activity
Resources is the process that should be completed in order to produce the RBS for the sponsor,
thus making Estimate Activity Resources the best answer to the question asked.
Note, RBS is mainly referred to as a risk breakdown structure. However, in its Glossary, the

---

PMBOK® Guide mentions RBS as also a resource breakdown structure.

**Details for Each Option:**

AError! Not a valid embedded object.Plan Resource Management
Incorrect. The Plan Resource Management process is the first step of the Project Resource
Management Knowledge Area. The Plan Resource Management process produces the
resource management plan, which is a subsidiary plan of the project management plan.
This answer is incorrect because the scenario states all subsidiary plans have already been
completed.
BError! Not a valid embedded object.Estimate Activity Resources
Correct. The Estimate Activity Resources process estimates the team and physical
resources needed to carry out the project work. The RBS is an output of this process. The
RBS categorizes resources and is used for planning, managing and controlling project
work.
CError! Not a valid embedded object.Develop Project Management Plan
Incorrect. The Develop Project Management Plan process defines how the project is
executed, monitored and controlled, and closed. The resulting output is comprised of
several components, including the subsidiary resource management plan, which has
already been completed, making this choice an incorrect answer.
DError! Not a valid embedded object.Acquire Resources
Incorrect. The Acquire Resources process is part of the Executing Process Group, which
follows the creation of the RBS. In other words, since this process begins after the RBS is
created, this answer choice can be eliminated.

**Reference:**

- **A Guide to the Project Management Body of Knowledge, (PMBOK® Guide) – Sixth Edition,**
Project Management Institute Inc., 2017, Page(s) 320, 326

PMP Exam Simulator

Filtered Mode: Displaying 200 questions
Question 196 of 200
Question ID: 612545
- **A project manager sends an email to the product developers notifying them of a critical defect**
found by the customer and asking them to report back to her so that she could update the
sponsor. The next day, the project manager is bombarded by the developers stopping by her
office to defend their efforts and point the blame elsewhere.
What could the project manager have done differently to obtain a more positive response from
the developers?
AError! Not a valid embedded object.Used push communication method
BError! Not a valid embedded object.Chosen different communication media
CError! Not a valid embedded object.Used pull communication method
DError! Not a valid embedded object.Asked the developers to update the sponsor directly
Question answered incorrectly

**Hint:**

Effective communications management includes decisions on how to choose the best method to
meet specific project needs regarding communication.
Correct Answer: B

**Explanation:**

Some resources say as much as 90% of a project manager's time is spent on communication.
Effective communication builds a bridge to diverse stakeholders and team members and
develops the relationships necessary for successful project outcomes. The matching of media to
messages is an important aspect of effective communication and effective management. For
example, deciding when it is better to communicate in writing versus orally, or deciding when to
prepare an informal memo versus drafting a formal report is an important aspect of managing

---

communications on projects. According to the scenario, the developers did not respond well to
the email regarding the defect. By communicating the information verbally, for example setting
up a meeting, video call, or conference call, the project manager could have incorporated
opportunities for interaction and obtained a more positive response from the developers.

**Details for Each Option:**

AError! Not a valid embedded object.Used push communication method
Incorrect. Push communication is distributed directly to specific recipients who need to
receive the information but does not ensure the communication actually reached or was
understood by the recipient. Examples of push communication include email, letters,
memos, and faxes. In the scenario, the project manager sent the information about the
defect by email, which is an example of push communications. According to the scenario
described, this type of communication did not work well, making push communication an
incorrect answer.
BError! Not a valid embedded object.Chosen different communication media
Correct. The matching of media to messages is an important aspect of effective
communication and effective management. For example, deciding when it is better to
communicate in writing versus orally, or deciding when to prepare an informal memo
versus drafting a formal report. The developers' response to the email suggests that the
project manager might have been better off sharing the information verbally allowing for
more interaction between her and the developers.
CError! Not a valid embedded object.Used pull communication method
Incorrect. Pull communication requires the recipients to access the content at their
discretion. Examples of pull communication are web portals, intranet sites, and knowledge
repositories. The information the project manager sent by email was time sensitive and
required action. It is unclear if using pull communication would have resulted in a more
positive response from the developers.
DError! Not a valid embedded object.Asked the developers to update the sponsor directly
Incorrect. This action is likely to have the same effect as the one described in the scenario,
if not worse. It is the project manager's responsibility to communicate with the team and
update the stakeholders, including the sponsor, accordingly.

**Reference:**

- **A Guide to the Project Management Body of Knowledge, (PMBOK® Guide) – Sixth Edition,**
Project Management Institute Inc., 2017, Page(s) 381, 61; see

---

also https://www.pmi.org/learning/library/communication-key-life-cycle-media-5340

PMP Exam Simulator
PMP Exam 4
Filtered Mode: Displaying 200 questions
Question 197 of 200
Question ID: 612369
While reviewing the issue log of the project you are leading, you suspect there is a pattern of
errors and defects. You and your project team want to determine the causes and frequency of
these errors and defects in the system. In particular, you are interested in identifying and ranking
the vital few sources that are responsible for causing the majority of the problems.
Which of the following tools will help you the most?
AError! Not a valid embedded object.Run chart
BError! Not a valid embedded object.Scatter diagram
CError! Not a valid embedded object.Pareto chart
DError! Not a valid embedded object.Fishbone diagram
Question answered incorrectly

**Hint:**

The results are typically plotted on a vertical bar chart, a histogram.
Correct Answer: C

**Explanation:**

You want to group the error and defects captured in the issue log into categories. These
categories would represent the source of the issues. Of the choices provided, the Pareto chart is
the only answer choice that allows for the ranking of grouped data points (in this case the error
and defects) represented by categories. A Pareto chart is a special form of a vertical bar chart, or
a histogram, where each bar represents a source of a problem. The height of the bar reflects the
relative frequency of the corresponding source. A histogram, such as the Pareto chart, is an
example of the data representation tools and techniques that can be used during the Control
Quality process described in the scenario. Hence, of the available choices, the Pareto chart is the

---

best tool to use to identify and rank the vital few sources that are responsible for causing the
majority of the problems and is, therefore, the best answer to the question asked.
While the topic of this question is only briefly discussed in the PMBOK® Guide, the Project
Management Professional (PMP)® Examination Content Outline, June 2015, covers knowledge
and skills with which PMP aspirants are expected to be familiar. Various quality control tools
and techniques are among these topics.

**Details for Each Option:**

AError! Not a valid embedded object.Run chart
Incorrect. A run chart is a line graph with data points plotted over time used to identify
trends or patterns. A run chart does not categorize data but rather charts up and/or down
fluctuations in the data.
BError! Not a valid embedded object.Scatter diagram
Incorrect. A scatter diagram is a graph that shows the relationship between two variables
in order to determine if a correlation exists. A scatter diagram does not categorize or rank
data.
CError! Not a valid embedded object.Pareto chart
Correct. A Pareto chart is a special form of a histogram or vertical bar chart used to
identify the most common sources that are responsible for causing the majority of the
problems.
DError! Not a valid embedded object.Fishbone diagram
Incorrect. A fishbone diagram, also known as a cause-and-effect diagram, breaks down the
causes of the problem statement identified into discrete branches, helping to identify the
main or root cause of the problem. A fishbone diagram is a visualization tool and does not
rank data.

**Reference:**

- **A Guide to the Project Management Body of Knowledge, (PMBOK® Guide) – Sixth Edition,**
Project Management Institute Inc., 2017, Page(s) 304; see also
https://www.pmi.org/learning/library/leveraging-six-sigma-benefits-realization-6726
Live FeedbackTM Back to Results

Question 198 of 200
Question ID: 612216
- **A project manager is leading a product development project within a centralized organizational**
structure. One of the project team members has left the organization and needs to be replaced if
the project goals are to be met. The project manager has identified an employee within the
organization that has the necessary skill set to fill the vacancy.
What should the project manager do first?
AError! Not a valid embedded object.Submit a change request to update the schedule baseline
BError! Not a valid embedded object.Negotiate with the employee's functional manager
CError! Not a valid embedded object.Discuss the staffing situation with the project sponsor
DError! Not a valid embedded object.Reassign the identified employee to the project team
Question answered incorrectly

**Hint:**

- **A centralized organization is also known as a functional organization structure.**
Correct Answer: B

**Explanation:**

The question indicates that the project exists within a centralized (also called functional)
organizational structure. Within a centralized organization, the project manager has little or no
direct control over resources. If the project manager needs to acquire an employee from within
the company, the project manager will need to negotiate the reassignment of the employee to the
project. Therefore, of the available choices, the project manager should first negotiate with the
employee's functional manager to release the employee to work on the project.

**Details for Each Option:**


---

AError! Not a valid embedded object.Submit a change request to update the schedule baseline
Incorrect. Before such a step, the project manager should make every reasonable effort to
keep to the schedule baseline (e.g. acquire new team member, compress schedule, use
overtime options, fill the gap with existing team members).
BError! Not a valid embedded object.Negotiate with the employee's functional manager
Correct. Within a centralized organization, the functional manager has control over
resources. If the project manager needs to acquire an employee from within the company,
the project manager needs to negotiate with the functional manager.
CError! Not a valid embedded object.Discuss the staffing situation with the project sponsor
Incorrect. Before escalating this issue with the project sponsor, the project manager should
first attempt to acquire the identified employee from the functional manager.
DError! Not a valid embedded object.Reassign the identified employee to the project team
Incorrect. Within the centralized type of organizational structure, the project manager has
little or no control over project resources. Therefore, the project manager will not have the
authority to reassign the identified employee.

**Reference:**

- **A Guide to the Project Management Body of Knowledge, (PMBOK® Guide) – Sixth Edition,**
Project Management Institute Inc., 2017, Page(s) 47

PMP Exam 4

Question 199 of 200
Question ID: 612612
You are halfway through a project, which has experienced several setbacks due to unanticipated
problems. Based on recent feedback, you are concerned that critical support for the project
among key stakeholders is eroding. You want to bring the stakeholders together for a meeting to
address any concerns and rebuild support for the project.
Which of the following meetings would be the most beneficial for the key stakeholders to
attend?
AError! Not a valid embedded object.Customer wrap-up meeting
BError! Not a valid embedded object.Change control meeting
CError! Not a valid embedded object.Celebration meeting
DError! Not a valid embedded object.Iteration retrospective
Question answered incorrectly

**Hint:**

The ability of stakeholders to influence the project is typically highest during the initiating stage
and gets lower as the project progresses.
Correct Answer: D

**Explanation:**

The question suggests that the Manage Stakeholder Engagement process is underway. Various
meetings can be beneficial in this process including the iteration retrospective. An iteration
retrospective is a specialized type of meeting used on projects with an agile framework and is
conducted at the end of each iteration. The purpose of a retrospective is to cover project progress
thus far and determine what worked well, what did not work well, and how project performance
can be improved going forward. Inviting the key stakeholders to the iteration retrospective will
allow the project team to address any concerns the stakeholders may have and develop a plan to
ensure the problems encountered do not recur. This approach should be beneficial in reassuring
the stakeholders that positive action is being taken to bring the project back into alignment with

---

project goals. Additionally, the iteration retrospective is held throughout project execution at the
end of each iteration. The ability of stakeholders to influence the project is typically highest
during the initiating stage and gets lower as the project progresses. The incorrect answer choices
represent meetings that are held at the end of the project and/or are not relevant to the Manage
Stakeholder Engagement Process.
Note, even though in "pure" agile environment, the iteration retrospective meetings are typically
held by and for the team members with an agile leader (such as a scrum master or an agile
coach), other project stakeholders can be invited as necessary. Therefore, while not ideal, of the
available choices, the iteration retrospective would be the most beneficial for key stakeholders to
attend as it pertains to the Manage Stakeholder Engagement process.

**Details for Each Option:**

AError! Not a valid embedded object.Customer wrap-up meeting
Incorrect. The customer wrap-up meeting occurs at the end of the project. The level of
influence of project stakeholders is the lowest at the end of the project. With the project
halfway complete and project support in jeopardy, it would be best to take more immediate
action and not wait until the end of the project. While the customer wrap-up meeting may
be required for certain stakeholders, it is not the most beneficial meeting from the
standpoint of managing stakeholder engagement.
BError! Not a valid embedded object.Change control meeting
Incorrect. Change control meetings are held with a change control board (CCB) that is
responsible for meeting and reviewing the change requests and approving, rejecting, or
deferring change requests. It is not known from the description provided by the question if
a CCB has been authorized by the project management plan. Even if the project utilizes a
CCB, the focus of the meeting is to review and dispose change requests, which is unlikely to
have the desired effect on stakeholder engagement.
CError! Not a valid embedded object.Celebration meeting
Incorrect. A celebration meeting usually occurs at the end of a project to reward the
project team and celebrate the success of the project. The celebration meeting may also
include key stakeholders. However, at the conclusion of a project is when stakeholders
have the least influence on the outcome of the project, making the celebration meeting of
lesser importance for managing stakeholder engagement compared with meetings
conducted earlier in the project. Additionally, the scenario describes a project that has
been experiencing issues. It is not clear yet if there will be anything to celebrate.
DError! Not a valid embedded object.Iteration retrospective

---

Correct. An iteration retrospective is a specialized type of meeting used on projects with an
agile framework conducted at the end of each iteration. The purpose of an iteration
retrospective is to cover project progress thus far and determine what has gone well, what
has not gone well, and how project performance can be improved going forward. Inviting
the key stakeholders to the iteration retrospective will allow the project team to address
any concerns the stakeholders may have and develop a plan to ensure the problems
encountered do not recur.

**Reference:**

- **A Guide to the Project Management Body of Knowledge, (PMBOK® Guide) – Sixth Edition,**
Project Management Institute Inc., 2017, Page(s) 528
Live FeedbackTM Back to Results

Filtered Mode: Displaying 200 questions
Question 200 of 200
Question ID: 612595
- **A software developer on an agile project team has discovered that adding a second computer**
monitor has increased productivity by reducing the time spent opening and closing screens. The
company has extra monitors in storage, so cost is not an issue. As an agile coach, you want this
practice to be adopted by the rest of the team members.
What is your best course of action?
AError! Not a valid embedded object.Discuss the best practice with the project team during the project
retrospective
BError! Not a valid embedded object.Have the project team member share the best practice during the
upcoming iteration retrospective
CError! Not a valid embedded object.Request the PMO to establish a new corporate policy that all
developers should use two monitors
DError! Not a valid embedded object.Pull the extra monitors out of storage and assign one additional
monitor to each developer

---

Question answered incorrectly

**Hint:**

Project team members should feel empowered to share and adopt best practices.
Correct Answer: B

**Explanation:**

- **A common problem with establishing continuous improvement during project execution is that**
lessons learned can become an afterthought as the project team focuses on the work of producing
the project's deliverables. Best practices and knowledge gained may be recorded in the lessons
learned register but that information is of no value if it is not shared with the project team to
improve the performance of the project. When an agile approach is used, the Control Schedule
process implied by the question is concerned with conducting retrospectives. An iteration
retrospective is a scheduled review in which best practices can be shared to improve the
performance of future iterations. Having the team member that discovered the best practice share
her experience with the project team will bring credibility as she is already having success with
improved productivity. Therefore, of the available choices, having the project team member
share the best practice during the upcoming iteration retrospective is the best answer to the
question asked.

**Details for Each Option:**

AError! Not a valid embedded object.Discuss the best practice with the project team during
the project retrospective
Incorrect. A project retrospective is held at the end of a project to discuss knowledge
gained during the project that might be beneficial for future projects. However, this action
will not improve the performance of the current project.
BError! Not a valid embedded object.Have the project team member share the best practice
during the upcoming iteration retrospective
Correct. An iteration retrospective is a scheduled review in which best practices can be
shared to improve the performance of future iterations.
CError! Not a valid embedded object.Request the PMO to establish a new corporate policy
that all developers should use two monitors
Incorrect. While the project team member that discovered the best practice may find two
monitors beneficial, this might not be the case for all team members. Additionally, this
action may not be beneficial for all software development projects and may create
resentment among other teams within the organization who are being forced to conform to

---

someone else's work process.
DError! Not a valid embedded object.Pull the extra monitors out of storage and assign one
additional monitor to each developer
Incorrect. You, as a leader (either an agile coach or project manager), should make the
extra monitors available for the team. However, just assigning an additional monitor does
not mean that the team members will understand the benefits. This action also does not
empower the team members to determine how they can be the most productive.

**Reference:**

- **A Guide to the Project Management Body of Knowledge, (PMBOK® Guide) – Sixth Edition,**
Project Management Institute Inc., 2017, Page(s) 224, 230
